New 5e world setting
A New World of Adventure Awaits

 

 

The Adventurer’s Guide to Aevoria

Contents

 

 

Welcome to Aevoria

How to Use This Book

This guide is designed to help you navigate the world of Aevoria and the Northwatch Wardens campaign. Whether you’re a new player picking up your first character sheet or a veteran adventurer, this section will show you how to make the most of these materials.

For Players

Your First Session

If you’re new to the campaign, start here:

  1. Read the Charter — The Northwatch Wardens operate by a code. Familiarize yourself with Chapter 4: The Northwatch Wardens to understand what it means to be a Warden.

  2. Learn About Northreach — Your adventures begin in the cold frontier. Chapter 3: Northreach: Your Starting Point gives you everything you need to know.

  3. Choose or Create a Character — You can use one of the pre-made characters available from your DM, or create your own using standard D&D 5e rules.

  4. Arrive at the Waystone Inn — Your adventure begins at the guild headquarters, where contracts are posted and Wardens gather.

First-Time Players

Don’t worry about reading everything before your first session. The most important thing is to understand your character and the guild’s basic code. Your DM will introduce the world as you explore it.

Between Sessions

Keep your adventure alive between game nights:

  • Update Your Journal — The Northreach Journal (see Appendix) is designed as a player-facing reference. Use it to track names, locations, and discoveries.

  • Review Your Contracts — Each adventure is structured as a contract. Re-read the mission briefing and think about your approach.

  • Explore the Lore — Chapter 5: The Wider World of Aevoria contains setting information about regions beyond Northreach. Your character might have come from one of these places.

Understanding the Structure

What’s in This Book

This guide is organized into several major sections:

1. Welcome to Aevoria

An overview of the world and its regions. This section sets the stage and provides context for where Northreach fits in the larger world.

2. Character Creation

Guidelines for creating your character, including regional origins, languages, and cultural backgrounds.

3. Northreach: Your Starting Point

Everything you need to know about the frontier region where your adventures take place:

  • Setting overview and key locations
  • Local cultures and communities
  • Important NPCs and organizations

4. The Northwatch Wardens

The guild charter, code of conduct, and organizational structure. Read this to understand what it means to be a Warden.

5. The Wider World of Aevoria

Detailed descriptions of the ten major regions beyond Northreach. Your character might have ties to these places, or you may travel there in future adventures.

6. Gods and Religion

The divine pantheon and religious practices of Aevoria. Faith plays a meaningful role in this world.

7. Places of Legend

Legendary locations that feature in world history and lore.

8. Practical Information

Quick reference guide for travel, costs, goods, and services throughout Aevoria.

9. Appendix

Additional resources including the glossary, music recommendations, the extended journal, and reference materials.

HOW TO USE THIS BOOK

 

 

What You Need to Know

The Campaign Style

Northwatch Wardens is a modular, contract-based campaign:

  • Drop-In Friendly — Designed for 2-5 players with flexible attendance. You don’t need perfect attendance to participate.
  • Order Independent — Most adventures can be played in any order. Your DM will help determine what’s available.
  • Mystery-Driven — There’s a larger story unfolding, but each adventure stands on its own.
  • Consequence-Rich — Your choices matter. NPCs remember what you do, and settlements change based on your actions.

The frontier doesn’t announce itself with walls and banners—it reveals itself mile by mile. Wind combs through pine and scrub, the road narrows and widens like a breathing thing, and every settlement feels earned: a warm window in a wide, cold land.

Reading the Adventures

Each adventure follows a standard structure:

  • Contract Brief — The mission outline and what you know going in
  • Investigation — Gathering information and making choices
  • Encounters — Combat, social challenges, or exploration
  • Resolution — Multiple possible outcomes based on your decisions

There isn’t always a “right” answer. The frontier is complicated, and perfect solutions are rare.

Player Safety and Expectations

Content and Themes

This campaign explores:

  • Frontier Survival — Cold, isolation, and the challenges of remote living
  • Moral Ambiguity — Not all problems have clean solutions
  • Mystery — Strange events and ancient magic awakening
  • Community — The importance of people looking out for each other

The tone is generally serious but not grim. There’s room for levity and heroism, but the setting emphasizes realistic consequences.

Session Zero

Your DM should conduct a session zero to discuss boundaries, comfort levels, and any content players want to avoid. The campaign is flexible enough to accommodate different play styles and comfort zones.

Communication

Good communication makes for better games:

  • Talk to Your DM — If something isn’t working for you, speak up. The campaign is meant to be fun.
  • Work Together — The Wardens are a team. Look for ways to help each other succeed.
  • Embrace Failure — Not every plan works. Some of the best stories come from setbacks and complications.

HOW TO USE THIS BOOK

 

 

Making the Most of Your Adventure

Engage with the World

Northreach feels alive when you interact with it:

  • Talk to NPCs — Everyone has a story, even the bartender at the Shepherd’s Crook Inn.
  • Explore Side Paths — Not everything is on the contract. Sometimes the best discoveries happen when you follow your curiosity.
  • Ask Questions — Your DM has thought about this world. Ask about what you see, hear, and smell.

Build Your Story

Your character’s journey is unique:

  • Make Choices That Matter to You — Don’t just follow the “optimal” path. Make choices your character would make.
  • Form Connections — Develop relationships with NPCs and other player characters.
  • Leave Your Mark — The frontier remembers. Your actions shape the world.

When winter bites early, when rumors travel faster than wagons, and when something in the dark makes even seasoned hunters hesitate, people look for the ones who will show up anyway—boots muddy, lamp lit, and questions asked only after everyone is safe.

Keep Records

Small details become important later:

  • Names Matter — Write down NPC names. The blacksmith you helped in session one might remember you in session five.
  • Track Locations — Note places you’ve been and what happened there.
  • Record Discoveries — Clues about the larger mystery are scattered throughout the adventures. Keep notes.

Additional Resources

Music and Atmosphere

The Songs of the Northreach (see Appendix) provides curated playlists to set the mood for different situations. Consider listening during sessions or while preparing your character.

Character Creation Guidelines

When creating a character for this campaign:

  • Low Magic Setting — Magic exists but isn’t common in daily life. Spellcasters are notable.
  • Frontier Background — Consider why your character came to the frontier or joined the Wardens.
  • Practical Skills — Survival, investigation, and social skills are often as useful as combat prowess.
  • Moral Flexibility — Perfect heroes rarely last long in the grey areas of frontier justice.
Recommended Starting Level

Most adventures are designed for characters starting at level 1-2. Your DM will specify the appropriate level for your group.

Where to Find Things

In This Guide:

  • Character Creation → Chapter 2
  • Northreach Information → Chapter 3
  • Guild Charter → Chapter 4
  • World Regions → Chapter 5
  • Gods and Faith → Chapter 6
  • Quick Reference → Chapter 8
  • Glossary → Chapter 9

From Your DM:

  • Adventures and contracts
  • NPC details and secrets
  • Pre-made characters (if desired)
  • Additional world lore and campaign-specific information

The frontier is vast. The mysteries are deep. The adventure awaits. – Welcome to the Northwatch Wardens.

Final Thoughts

This book is a tool, not a textbook. You don’t need to memorize everything or read it cover to cover. Use it as a reference when you need to understand something about the world, refresh your memory about a location, or deepen your character’s connection to the setting.

The best adventures come from curiosity, courage, and characters who care about the world around them. The Northwatch Wardens need people who will show up when it matters, make hard choices when necessary, and stand by their commitments even when it’s difficult.

HOW TO USE THIS BOOK

 

 

Character Creation

Creating Your Character

A guide for creating characters in the Northwatch Wardens campaign

Welcome to the frontier. You’ve come to Northreach for your own reasons—seeking opportunity, fleeing trouble, or answering a call to adventure. The Northwatch Wardens accept capable individuals regardless of their past. What matters is what you can do now, and whether you’re willing to stand with others when the cold winds blow.

What Makes This Campaign Different

The Guild Structure

You’re not just adventurers who met in a tavern—you’re members of the Northwatch Wardens, a frontier guild dedicated to protecting Northreach settlements. Your character has made a conscious choice to join this organization and uphold its code.

Contract-Based Adventures

The Wardens operate on a contract system. Jobs appear on the Waystone Board, and you choose which missions to accept. This structure supports:

  • Flexible attendance — Real life happens; the guild accommodates it
  • Character goals — Pick contracts that align with your motivations
  • Team variety — Different contracts bring different Wardens together

Frontier Setting

Northreach is a low-magic, high-stakes environment:

  • Most folk live practical lives; magic is rare and respected
  • The wilderness is dangerous, and communities depend on each other
  • Your reputation matters—people remember what you do
  • Winter is lethal: it doesn’t discriminate

Campaign Themes

  • Investigation and exploration over constant combat
  • Moral complexity — not every problem has a clear solution
  • Community impact — your choices affect settlements and people
  • Survival and resourcefulness — the frontier is unforgiving

Campaign Rules

Starting Specifications

Core Rules

Starting Level: 3rd level
Ability Scores: Standard Array (15, 14, 13, 12, 10, 8) or Point Buy
Starting Equipment: Class default + Warden’s Kit (see below)
Alignment: Any, but must be compatible with the Guild Code
Source Books: Player’s Handbook + Xanathar’s + Tasha’s (others with DM approval)
Hit Points: Maximum at 1st level, roll or take average thereafter

Ability Score Methods

Choose one of the following:

Standard Array (Recommended)

  • Use these six scores: 15, 14, 13, 12, 10, 8
  • Assign them to your abilities in any order
  • Apply your species modifiers
  • Simple and balanced for all characters

Point Buy

  • Start with all abilities at 8
  • Spend 27 points to increase them (max 15 before racial bonuses)
  • See Player’s Handbook page 13 for costs
  • Allows precise customization

CREATING YOUR CHARACTER

 

 

Warden’s Kit

All Wardens receive this basic frontier equipment in addition to class starting gear:

  • Warm winter clothing (cold weather outfit)
  • Bedroll and wool blanket
  • Waterskin and mess kit
  • Tinderbox and 10 torches
  • 50 feet of hempen rope
  • Set of common clothes
  • Belt pouch

Guild Resources

Once accepted as a Warden, you have access to:

  • Waystone Inn lodging — Bed, meals, and basic medical care
  • Guild quartermaster — Steward Mara Fenwick provides standard supplies
  • Contract stipends — Some missions provide specialized equipment
  • Guild library — Lorewarden Elric maintains records and references

Your Character Concept

Start with who your character is, not just what they can do mechanically.

The Three Essential Questions

Answer these to ground your character in Northreach:

1. Why did you come to the frontier?

  • Escaping something (debt, scandal, war, betrayal, family)
  • Seeking fortune in a land of opportunity
  • Following someone (friend, mentor, loved one, rumor)
  • Driven by curiosity about the region’s mysteries
  • Answering a call for help from the Wardens
  • Nowhere else to go

2. What skills did you bring?

  • Combat training (guard, soldier, mercenary, pit fighter)
  • Wilderness expertise (hunter, trapper, guide, ranger)
  • Scholarly knowledge (researcher, mage, healer, sage)
  • Social finesse (diplomat, merchant, performer, spy)
  • Practical trades (smith, carpenter, herbalist, cook)

3. What keeps you with the Wardens?

  • The pay and regular work
  • Protecting vulnerable communities
  • Investigating the strange phenomena
  • Brotherhood/sisterhood with other Wardens
  • Redemption for past mistakes
  • Nowhere better to go
  • Personal quest (finding someone, uncovering truth)
Keep It Simple

You don’t need a twenty-page backstory. One page is plenty. Focus on:

  • Your character’s personality and values
  • Their reason for being here now
  • What they hope to achieve
  • What they fear or avoid

The best characters reveal themselves through play, not exposition.

Classes in Northreach

All Player’s Handbook classes work in this campaign, but some fit the frontier theme more naturally. Choose what excites you—competence matters more than optimization.

Highly Recommended for the Frontier

Barbarian — The wild lands call to you. Primal fury and survival skills are invaluable in Northreach. Recommended Paths: Totem Warrior, Ancestral Guardian

Cleric — Healers and divine champions are desperately needed. The frontier tests faith but also needs it. Recommended Domains: Life, Light, Tempest

Druid — Those who understand nature’s balance are respected, if sometimes feared. The wild places hold secrets. Recommended Circles: Land (Forest/Coast), Moon

Fighter — Every frontier needs capable warriors. Versatile and reliable in any situation. Recommended Archetypes: Battle Master, Champion

Ranger — Scouts, trackers, and wilderness guides are the Wardens’ backbone. You know the land and its dangers. Recommended Archetypes: Hunter, Gloom Stalker

Rogue — Sneaking, scouting, and solving problems with cunning are as important as brute force. Recommended Archetypes: Scout, Inquisitive

CREATING YOUR CHARACTER

 

 

Well-Suited

Bard — Diplomats, chroniclers, and support specialists. Social skills solve many frontier problems. Recommended Colleges: Lore, Valor

Paladin — Oathbound warriors bringing justice to lawless lands. Your convictions will be tested. Recommended Oaths: Devotion, Ancients, Redemption

Warlock — Pact magic for power or knowledge. Your patron’s interest in Northreach should be explained. Recommended Patrons: Archfey, Celestial

Wizard — Rare but valued. Arcane scholars investigating awakening magic find mysteries here. Recommended Schools: Divination, Abjuration, War Magic

Less Common (But Viable)

Artificer — Researching Aeorian ruins or developing frontier survival tools. Requires Tasha’s Cauldron

Monk — Unusual in Northreach. Perhaps you’re from a distant monastery or seeking enlightenment. Consider training origin

Sorcerer — Wild magic and awakening power fit campaign themes. Your innate magic may connect to local phenomena. Recommended Origins: Wild Magic, Draconic

Ancestries in Northreach

All standard D&D species exist in Aevoria. Here’s what you’ll find in Northreach and how they’re perceived:

Common

Humans — Most numerous; adaptable settlers from across Aevoria. They fill every role in frontier society.

Dwarves — Skilled in stonecraft and metallurgy. Some came north as prospectors or engineers seeking fortune. Typical Classes: Fighter, Cleric, Artificer

Half-Elves — Often serve as mediators between human and elven communities. Common and well-integrated. Typical Classes: Bard, Ranger, Rogue

Halflings — Practical and community-minded. Welton’s shepherd culture is predominantly halfling. Typical Classes: Rogue, Bard, Cleric

Uncommon

Elves — Most stay in the Nullwood Expanse. Those in Northreach are usually scouts, exiles, or scholars. Wood elves more common than high elves. Typical Classes: Ranger, Wizard, Druid

Half-Orcs — Accepted based on actions, not heritage. Many find the frontier’s meritocracy welcoming. Typical Classes: Barbarian, Fighter, Ranger

Tieflings — Rare and sometimes viewed with suspicion, but respected once they prove themselves. Typical Classes: Warlock, Sorcerer, Rogue

Rare

Dragonborn — Extremely rare. Usually travelers or exiles from distant lands. Their presence draws attention.

Gnomes — A handful of tinkerers and scholars pursue arcane research or mechanical projects. Typical Classes: Wizard, Artificer, Bard

Other Ancestries — Tabaxi, Genasi, Aarakocra, etc. are exceptionally rare. Discuss with your DM and have a compelling reason for being on the frontier.

Frontier Practicality

In Northreach, your competence matters more than your ancestry. Prove you can handle the work, keep your word, and contribute to the community, and you’ll be respected regardless of heritage.

Backgrounds and Previous Life

Your background represents your life before joining the Northwatch Wardens.

Frontier-Appropriate Backgrounds

Folk Hero — You protected your community and gained a reputation. Now you seek to do more.

Outlander — You’ve spent your life in the wilderness. The frontier is home.

Soldier — Former military from southern kingdoms. You came north for a fresh start.

Criminal — Everyone deserves a second chance. Northreach doesn’t judge your past if you contribute now.

Sage — You’re researching strange phenomena in Northreach. The Aeorian ruins call to you.

Guild Artisan — Skilled craftspeople are always needed: smiths, carpenters, tanners, brewers.

Hermit — You sought isolation in the north. Now circumstances draw you back to civilization.

Other Backgrounds

Acolyte, Charlatan, Entertainer, Noble, Sailor, Urchin — All work with appropriate backstory. A noble might be a disgraced heir seeking redemption; a sailor could be a shipwreck survivor; an urchin grew up in a settlement.

CREATING YOUR CHARACTER

 

 

Custom Backgrounds

Work with your DM to create custom backgrounds following the standard structure:

  • 2 skill proficiencies
  • 2 tool proficiencies or languages
  • Equipment package
  • Feature
Northreach Connection

Whatever your background, consider how you ended up here. The frontier attracts the desperate, the ambitious, the curious, and the damned. Which are you?

Skills and Capabilities

Recommended Proficiencies

Given this campaign’s investigative nature, these skills prove particularly valuable:

High Priority:

  • Investigation — Analyzing clues, searching scenes, making deductions
  • Insight — Reading people, detecting lies, understanding motivations
  • Perception — Noticing details, spotting danger, finding hidden things
  • Survival — Tracking, wilderness navigation, reading natural signs

Very Valuable:

  • Persuasion — Negotiating with NPCs, swaying councils, recruiting allies
  • Nature — Understanding beasts, plants, terrain, environmental magic
  • Arcana — Recognizing magical phenomena (increasingly important)
  • Medicine — Treating injuries and diseases in the field

Situationally Useful:

  • Athletics/Acrobatics — Physical challenges and combat maneuvers
  • Stealth — Reconnaissance and avoiding unnecessary fights
  • Intimidation — Sometimes threats work better than diplomacy
  • Deception — Not encouraged by the Code, but sometimes necessary

Tool Proficiencies

Practical tools prove their worth on the frontier:

  • Herbalism Kit — Crafting healing supplies
  • Thieves’ Tools — Lock-picking and trap-handling
  • Navigator’s Tools — Wilderness navigation
  • Cartographer’s Tools — Mapping unknown territories
  • Mason’s Tools — Assessing structures and ruins
  • Smith’s Tools — Equipment repair

Languages

Common is universal, but additional languages provide advantages:

  • Dwarvish — Ancient stonework inscriptions
  • Elvish — Old magic and Nullwood refugees
  • Giant — Communicating with larger threats
  • Draconic — Ancient texts and dragons
  • Goblin/Orc — Frequent frontier threats
  • Primordial — Understanding elemental phenomena

Joining the Northwatch Wardens

Your character needs a reason to join or be interested in the guild. Consider these hooks:

Motivations for Joining

Idealists — You believe in protecting the vulnerable and making the frontier safer. The work matters more than recognition.

Pragmatists — Steady employment, fair pay, mutual support. It’s good work with decent people.

Seekers — Something strange is happening in Northreach. The Wardens investigate rather than ignore it.

Survivors — You need somewhere to belong. The guild accepts those who prove themselves, regardless of past.

Exiles — You can’t return home. Northreach is far enough from wherever you’re running.

Redemption — You’re trying to make up for past mistakes by helping others.

Justice — Someone or something wronged you or someone you care about. The Wardens give you the means to act.

CREATING YOUR CHARACTER

 

 

Your Current Status

New Recruit — You just arrived at Waystone Inn and are taking your first contracts.

Returning Warden — You’ve been gone for a while but are coming back to active duty.

Vouched For — Someone in the Wardens recommended you for membership.

On Trial — You’re on a probationary contract to demonstrate your worthiness.

The Guild Code

All Wardens must uphold the Code:

  1. Protect the innocent — Prioritize civilian safety
  2. Honor your contracts — Complete jobs you accept
  3. Share vital information — Keep fellow Wardens informed
  4. Respect the frontier — Its people, land, and traditions
  5. Stand against corruption — Mortal or magical
  6. Never abandon a companion — Unless retreat is the only survival path

This Code provides in-character justification for party cohesion and moral boundaries.

Personality and Character

Frontier Traits

The frontier shapes people in specific ways. Consider these common traits:

Practical — You focus on what works, not what’s ideal.

Direct — Polite but straightforward. No time for excessive flattery.

Resilient — You don’t give up easily. Survival requires persistence.

Self-Reliant — You handle your own problems when possible.

Community-Minded — Despite self-reliance, survival depends on cooperation.

Adaptable — Plans change. Weather, wildlife, and magic don’t care about your schedule.

Frontier Values

Understanding these helps you navigate Northreach society:

Competence — Can you do what you claim? Actions matter more than words.

Keeping Your Word — Contracts are sacred. Oath-breakers are marked as untrustworthy.

Mutual Aid — Help your neighbors during emergencies.

Respect for the Land — The wilderness is dangerous and should be treated as such.

These don’t have to define your character, but they define how Northreach operates.

Personality Elements

Use your background’s personality traits, ideals, bonds, and flaws as a starting point, but make them personal:

Traits — 2-3 defining characteristics. Are you optimistic or grimly realistic? Direct or diplomatic?

Ideals — What principle guides you? Justice, freedom, knowledge, power, community?

Bonds — What connects you to the world? A person, place, ideal, or organization?

Flaws — Everyone has weaknesses. A fear, vice, prejudice, secret, or personality trait that creates problems?

Remember: Your character doesn’t need to be perfect. Flaws create interesting stories. A paladin who struggles with mercy, a rogue who’s too trusting, a wizard who fears their own power—these tensions make for compelling play.

Starting Equipment

Equipment Package (Recommended)

Take your class’s starting equipment package from the Player’s Handbook plus the Warden’s Kit (see page 2). This is simple and ensures you have everything needed.

Alternative: Starting Gold

If you prefer to customize, roll for starting gold and purchase equipment:

Class Starting Gold
Monk 5d4 gp
Barbarian, Druid 2d4 × 10 gp
Sorcerer 3d4 × 10 gp
Rogue, Warlock, Wizard 4d4 × 10 gp
Bard, Cleric, Fighter, Paladin, Ranger, Artificer 5d4 × 10 gp

Essential Frontier Gear

If building from gold, prioritize:

  • Weapon(s) — Your primary combat tools
  • Armor — Best you can afford and wear
  • Backpack — To carry everything
  • Bedroll — Wilderness sleeping
  • Rations (5+ days) — Food is life
  • Waterskin — Hydration
  • Rope (50 ft) — Endless uses
  • Tinderbox — Fire in the cold
  • Torches or lantern — Light source
  • Cold weather outfit — Winter gear (5 gp)
  • Healer’s Kit — Basic medical supplies

CREATING YOUR CHARACTER

 

 

Spellcasting Components

Arcane Focus or Component Pouch — Required for most spellcasters. Don’t forget this!

Holy Symbol — Clerics and paladins need this for spells.

Don’t Overthink It

You’ll acquire more equipment through play. Start with essentials and build from there.

Character Advancement

After Character Creation

Once your character sheet is complete:

Share with Your DM — Let them review and provide feedback. They may have suggestions or plot hooks based on your backstory.

Coordinate with Your Party — Ensure you have balanced group composition. You don’t need every role, but extreme overlap can be limiting.

Read Campaign Materials — Familiarize yourself with:

  • Chapter 3: Northreach: Your Starting Point
  • Chapter 4: The Northwatch Wardens (guild charter and operations)
  • Chapter 8: Practical Information (quick reference for costs and travel)

Session Zero Checklist

Before play begins, discuss with your group:

Character Basics

  • Name, ancestry, class, background
  • Ability scores and core stats
  • Skills and proficiencies
  • Key personality traits
  • Character concept and motivation

Campaign Integration

  • Why are you in Northreach?
  • Why join the Wardens?
  • What are you hoping to accomplish?
  • What are you afraid of or avoiding?

Group Dynamics

  • How do you know the other PCs (if at all)?
  • What role do you fill in the party?
  • Are there character conflicts or tensions?
  • How does your character handle disagreements?

Player Expectations

  • Preferred play style (combat, roleplay, exploration)?
  • Any topics or themes to avoid?
  • Comfort with consequences (injury, death, moral dilemmas)?
  • Decision-making preference (in-character vs. meta-discussion)?

Example Character Concepts

Need inspiration? Here are concepts that fit the campaign:

The Frontier Medic — Life Cleric who came north to provide healing where desperately needed.

The Exiled Soldier — Fighter or Paladin dishonored in former service, seeking redemption.

The Beast Whisperer — Ranger or Druid who understands the wild better than civilization.

The Arcane Scholar — Wizard or Sorcerer drawn to Northreach’s awakening magic.

The Reformed Scoundrel — Rogue trying to do right by communities they once wronged.

The Wilderness Guide — Ranger or Barbarian born in Northreach, determined to keep people safe.

The Oath-Keeper — Paladin or Cleric whose convictions brought them to where need is greatest.

The Desperate Seeker — Any class looking for someone or something in Northreach.

The Curious Tinkerer — Artificer investigating Aeorian ruins and ancient technology.

The Haunted Veteran — Fighter or Ranger who came north to escape war’s aftermath.

The Folk Hero — Any class who earned reputation protecting their home, now expanding their reach.

The Traveling Sage — Wizard or Bard chronicling frontier life and magical phenomena.

These are starting points, not rigid templates. Mix, modify, and make them your own. The best character is one that excites you to play and contributes to the group’s story.

CREATING YOUR CHARACTER

 

 

Quick Reference: Character Creation Steps

Follow these steps to create your Northwatch Warden:

1. Concept (10 minutes)

  • Answer the three questions (page 3)
  • Decide on character personality and motivation
  • Consider how they fit the frontier and Wardens

2. Mechanical Choices (20 minutes)

  • Choose class (consult PHB)
  • Choose ancestry/species (consult PHB)
  • Choose background (consult PHB)
  • Distribute ability scores (Standard Array or Point Buy)

3. Skills and Features (15 minutes)

  • Assign skill proficiencies from class and background
  • Choose tool proficiencies and languages
  • Select starting equipment (package or gold)
  • Note class features and abilities

4. Campaign Integration (10 minutes)

  • Define relationship to the Wardens
  • Establish ties (or lack thereof) to Northreach
  • Consider secrets or personal goals
  • Write brief (one paragraph) character summary

5. Details and Polish (10 minutes)

  • Name your character
  • Determine appearance
  • Set personality traits, ideals, bonds, flaws
  • Calculate final stats (AC, HP, initiative, saves, attack bonuses)

6. Review and Confirm (Variable)

  • Share with DM for approval and feedback
  • Coordinate with party for group balance
  • Finalize any DM-specific adjustments
  • Prepare for Session Zero
Total Time: ~60-75 minutes

Experienced D&D players can complete this faster. New players should take their time and ask questions. Your DM is there to help!

Final Thoughts

What You Don’t Need

  • A twenty-page backstory (one page is plenty)
  • Perfect mechanical optimization
  • A tragic past to justify adventuring
  • Connections to world-shaking events
  • Complex multi-class builds (unless that’s your thing)

What You Do Need

  • A reason to accept dangerous contracts
  • Skills that contribute to party success
  • Personality traits that create interesting interactions
  • Willingness to engage with moral complexity
  • Openness to consequences and character growth

Remember the Frontier

The Northwatch Wardens accept you for what you can do now, not who you were. The frontier doesn’t care about your bloodline, homeland, or past failures.

It asks only one question:

When the wolves howl and the cold winds blow, will you stand with your fellow Wardens?

Welcome to Northreach. There’s work to be done.

CREATING YOUR CHARACTER

 

 

Regional Origins Guide

Where You Come From Shapes Who You Are

The Ten Regions of Aevoria

From the frozen wastes of the Far North to the sun-drenched plazas of Solaris, Aevoria spans a vast and diverse world. Each region shapes its people in distinctive ways—through climate, culture, history, and the values passed down through generations.

Your character’s origin isn’t just flavor text. It’s the foundation of who they are, how they see the world, and why they’ve traveled to the frontier. Whether you’re a Solarian bard seeking truth beyond the factions, a Stonebound geomancer studying frontier anomalies, or a Northreach native fighting for your home, your regional origin provides rich roleplay opportunities and meaningful connections to the wider world.

How to Use This Guide

This guide provides:

  • Cultural context for each of Aevoria’s ten regions
  • Background adaptations showing how standard D&D backgrounds manifest in different regions
  • Character concepts to inspire your creation process
  • Roleplay hooks connecting your origin to the campaign
  • Mechanical guidance for regional customization

Why Origins Matter

Your regional origin affects:

Perspective: What you consider normal, dangerous, or valuable
Connections: Who you might know and what organizations matter to you
Motivations: Why you traveled to Northreach and joined the Wardens
Roleplay: How you speak, act, and approach problems
Story hooks: What rumors, threats, or opportunities interest you

Using Regional Origins

  1. Choose your region based on the character concept that excites you
  2. Select or adapt a background that fits both your region and your story
  3. Review the cultural traits to understand regional perspectives
  4. Answer the character questions to develop your backstory
  5. Discuss with your DM how your origin connects to the campaign
Starting in Northreach

All player characters begin in Northreach, either as locals or newcomers. If you’re from another region, you need a reason for traveling to the frontier and joining the Northwatch Wardens. Each regional section includes common motivations for making this journey.

REGIONAL ORIGINS GUIDE

 

 

The Ten Regions

1. Northreach — The Frozen Frontier

Where winter bites and wolves prowl, where communities cling to survival through mutual aid and grim determination. This is the frontier—hard, honest, and unforgiving.

Overview

Northreach is a cold, sparsely settled frontier region where survival depends on self-reliance, practical competence, and community cooperation. Most inhabitants know only local concerns—wolves, bandits, missing hunters, and the ever-present threat of winter. This is the starting region for the campaign and home to the Northwatch Wardens.

  • Climate: Cold temperate to subarctic
  • Population: Scattered villages, isolated farmsteads
  • Government: Local councils, guild influence
  • Economy: Subsistence farming, trapping, logging

Common Backgrounds

  • Folk Hero
    You defended your village from wolves, bandits, or worse. The frontier breeds heroes out of necessity—those who stand when others can’t.

  • Outlander
    The most natural choice for Northreach natives. You know the woods, the weather, and the dangers. You were born to this life.

  • Soldier
    Perhaps you served with a militia defending villages, or you’re a veteran who sought peace on the frontier (and found new conflicts instead).

  • Hermit
    The frontier has plenty of isolated places for those seeking solitude. But even hermits eventually need to return to civilization—or defend it.

Cultural Traits

  • Practical over proper: If it works, it’s good enough. Results matter more than tradition
  • Earned respect: Your reputation is built by actions, not words or lineage
  • Mutual aid: Communities survive by helping each other; selfishness is remembered
  • Wary of strangers: Trust must be earned, but once given, it’s genuine
  • Direct communication: Frontier folk say what they mean; flowery speech is seen as suspicious
  • Respect for winter: The cold is honest—it’ll kill rich and poor alike
If You’re From Northreach…

You Know:

  • How to read weather, tracks, and animal behavior
  • Which villages are reliable and which have problems
  • That the wilderness is dangerous and should be respected
  • The names of local threats (bandits, predators, haunted places)
  • How to preserve food, maintain gear, and survive winters

Others See You As:

  • Practical and straightforward
  • Tough and self-reliant
  • Perhaps unsophisticated or rough around the edges
  • Trustworthy if you prove yourself
  • Someone who understands frontier life

Why Join the Wardens:

  • This is your home and you’ll defend it
  • The guild provides steady work and purpose
  • You want to protect communities like yours
  • You’ve lost someone to frontier dangers
  • You believe in what the Wardens stand for

Sample Character Concepts

  • Mira Blackwood, Human Ranger (Hunter)
    Lost her parents to wolves as a child; raised by village hunters. Joined the Wardens to ensure no other child faces the same fate. Specializes in tracking predators and protecting settlements.

  • Thoren Ironfoot, Dwarf Fighter (Battle Master)
    Former soldier from the Stonebound Depths who settled in Northreach seeking peace. Found the frontier needed defenders as much as anywhere else. Brings tactical experience to contract operations.

  • Ash, Half-Elf Druid (Circle of the Land - Arctic)
    Born during a blizzard in a frontier cabin. Speaks little but understands the land deeply. Joined the Wardens because civilization and wilderness must coexist for either to survive.

Character Tie-In Questions

Answer 2-3 of these to develop your backstory:

  1. Which village or settlement do you consider home? (Welton, Palebank, Pinebrook, or another)
  2. What frontier danger have you faced that shaped you? (Wolves, bandits, starvation, isolation)
  3. Who taught you to survive in Northreach? (Parent, mentor, harsh experience)
  4. What do you miss most about the “civilized” south? (Or do you prefer the frontier?)
  5. Have you ever been lost in the wilderness? What happened?

THE TEN REGIONS

 

 

2. Solaris Dominion — The Cultural Capital

Where songs echo through sunlit plazas and every tale has three versions. Solaris thrives on creativity, politics, and performance—a city that feels alive with drama at every corner.

Overview

Solaris is a vibrant metropolis known as the beating heart of music, storytelling, and bardic tradition. The city thrives on creativity, performance, and mythmaking—its plazas echo with tales and its streets feel like they’re always mid-song. Three political factions compete to define the city’s soul, making Solaris equal parts cultural paradise and political powder keg.

  • Climate: Temperate Mediterranean; mild and pleasant
  • Population: ~50,000 (diverse, cosmopolitan)
  • Government: Factional (Harmonists, Veilbound, Chorus)
  • Economy: Arts, culture, trade, scholarship

Common Backgrounds

  • Entertainer
    The natural choice for Solarians. You’re a performer, storyteller, musician, or actor trained in a city that invented half the songs sung in taverns across Aevoria.

  • Noble
    Solaris’ elite families wield cultural rather than military power. You understand politics, patronage, and the performance of status.

  • Sage
    Solaris hosts libraries, colleges, and scholarly institutions where knowledge is currency and information flows like wine.

  • Charlatan
    In a city built on performance, the line between artist and con artist is paper-thin. You learned to read crowds, tell people what they want to hear, and disappear before questions get uncomfortable.

Character Tie-In Questions

  1. Which faction do you lean toward—or do you reject them all?
  2. What performance, scandal, or event made you memorable in Solaris?
  3. Why did you leave the cultural capital for the frozen frontier?
  4. Who in Solaris would want to hear from you—or want you to stay silent?
  5. What story are you trying to tell about your time in Northreach?

Cultural Traits

  • Performance is life: Everything is a story worth telling; appearances matter
  • Faction loyalty: Most Solarians lean toward Harmonist, Veilbound, or Chorus ideals
  • Verbal flourish: Eloquence is valued; plain speech is considered dull
  • Information currency: News, rumors, and secrets have tangible value
  • Artistic pride: Solaris created bardic tradition; others merely imitate
  • Political awareness: Everyone has opinions on the factions and Eclipse Day
If You’re From Solaris…

You Know:

  • Current songs, popular plays, and trending stories
  • The three factions and their philosophical differences
  • How to read a crowd and gauge their mood
  • That reputation and perception often matter more than truth
  • Eclipse Day changed everything—but no one agrees how

Others See You As:

  • Eloquent, dramatic, or overly theatrical
  • Politically aware or factionally biased
  • Sophisticated but possibly untrustworthy
  • Someone who talks too much
  • Educated and culturally refined

Why Travel to Northreach:

  • Escaping factional politics or consequences
  • Seeking “authentic” stories beyond the city
  • Investigating rumors of strange events
  • Following a patron’s commission
  • Proving yourself beyond the safety of civilization
  • Documenting frontier life for Solarian audiences

Sample Character Concepts

Lyra Brightsong, Half-Elf Bard (College of Lore)
Rising star at the Tail Spinner’s Cord who grew disillusioned with factional manipulation of truth. Came to Northreach seeking real stories, not manufactured narratives. Documents everything.

Marcus Vael, Human Wizard (Divination)
Scholar from a Veilbound family researching magical anomalies. Eclipse Day pointed him toward Northreach. His family expects regular reports—and results.

Senna Darkwater, Tiefling Rogue (Inquisitive)
Former spy for the Chorus who saw too much and fled north. Excellent at gathering information and reading people. Never quite stops looking over her shoulder.

THE TEN REGIONS

 

 

3. Nullwood Expanse — The Silent Kingdom

Where magic whispers rather than roars, where pale trees sway without wind, and where elves tend memories like gardens. The Nullwood is beautiful, serene, and subtly unsettling.

Overview

The Nullwood Expanse is an ancient elven kingdom hidden within a vast forest where magic feels strangely muted and sound seems softened. The Nullwood Elves are a people shaped by caution, memory, and an old fear they no longer fully understand. Their magic is subtle and disciplined, their architecture grown rather than built, and their society structured around emotional balance and preservation of harmony.

  • Climate: Mild temperate; cool summers, misty winters
  • Population: ~12,000 (overwhelmingly elven)
  • Government: Memory Courts (elven councils)
  • Economy: Self-sufficient; limited external trade

Common Backgrounds

  • Sage
    The Nullwood values memory preservation and historical study. You’re trained in recording, cataloging, and maintaining clarity of past events.

  • Hermit
    The quiet forests suit those seeking introspection. Many Nullwood elves spend years in isolated contemplation, emerging with deep insights.

  • Outlander
    Scouts and rangers patrol the borders, monitoring threats and watching for magical disturbances from the wider world.

  • Acolyte
    Nullwood spirituality centers on memory rituals and emotional balance rather than traditional gods. You’re trained in these practices.

Character Tie-In Questions

  1. What memory do you hold most clearly—and why?
  2. Why did you leave the Nullwood’s peaceful silence?
  3. Do you perform memory rituals privately, or have you abandoned them?
  4. What about Nullwood culture do you miss—or reject?
  5. Have you seen anything in Northreach that the Memory Courts should know?

Cultural Traits

  • Emotional discipline: Feelings are acknowledged but carefully managed
  • Memory reverence: History is sacred; forgetting is feared
  • Subtle magic: Flashy spells are seen as crude; refinement is prized
  • Cautious engagement: The outside world is watched but rarely joined
  • Architectural harmony: Living with nature rather than conquering it
  • Unspoken wariness: An old fear they don’t discuss with outsiders
If You’re From the Nullwood…

You Know:

  • How to perform memory rituals and emotional centering practices
  • That some history is curated—edited for harmony
  • The Stillgrove dampens magic for reasons unexplained
  • Ancient ruins should be avoided, not explored
  • Patience and precision matter more than speed

Others See You As:

  • Serene but emotionally distant
  • Wise but overly cautious
  • Graceful and refined
  • Mysterious or withholding
  • Uncomfortable with chaos or noise

Why Travel to Northreach:

  • Scouting reports of magical anomalies
  • Seeking experiences beyond curated silence
  • Running from the weight of memory
  • Following visions or portents
  • Testing yourself in a world that isn’t controlled
  • Documenting threats to report to the Memory Courts

Sample Character Concepts

  • Elara Stillwater, Wood Elf Druid (Circle of the Moon)
    Veilwatch scout who witnessed strange stirrings in the Verdant Marches. Sent north to investigate whether similar patterns emerge in Northreach. Uncomfortable in settlements but adapting.

  • Thaelan Silverleaf, High Elf Wizard (Abjuration)
    Memory Court scholar researching why magic behaves strangely in certain regions. Northreach’s frontier anomalies match historical patterns he’s trying to understand. Takes meticulous notes.

  • Whisper, Wood Elf Ranger (Gloom Stalker)
    Refused the memory rituals and emotional curation. Left the Nullwood seeking “real” experiences—raw, unfiltered, and honest. Found exactly that in Northreach.

THE TEN REGIONS

 

 

4. Stonebound Depths — The Deep Kingdom

Where stone sings and metal hums, where dwarves carve cities from living rock and listen to the earth’s deep voice. The Stonebound Depths are ancient, monumental, and resonant with power.

Overview

Deep beneath the mountains lies the dwarven kingdom known as the Stonebound Depths—a vast subterranean realm built around massive crystalline formations and metallic structures the dwarves call “Deep Roots.” The Stonebound Dwarves believe these are natural geological features, not understanding their true Aeorian origin. Their culture revolves around geomancy, resonance magic, and the deep patience of stone.

  • Climate: Stable subterranean (cool, dry)
  • Population: ~40,000 (majority dwarven)
  • Government: The Resonant Council (master crafters)
  • Economy: Mining, metalwork, geomancy, runecraft

Common Backgrounds

  • Guild Artisan
    The natural choice for Stonebound dwarves. You’re trained in smithing, stonework, gemcutting, or other crafts the Depths perfected.

  • Soldier
    The Depths maintain organized defense forces protecting the entrances and patrolling the deep tunnels where things stir in the dark.

  • Acolyte
    Rune-singers and deep-readers serve as spiritual leaders, interpreting the “song of stone” and maintaining harmonic rituals.

  • Sage
    Scholars study geological patterns, resonance theory, and the properties of the Deep Roots. You understand what the earth “says.”

Character Tie-In Questions

  1. What was your greatest craft—or greatest failure—before leaving?
  2. How do you feel about the sky and open spaces?
  3. Do you still perform resonance rituals, or have you adapted?
  4. What debt, oath, or obligation drove you to the surface?
  5. Have you found anything in Northreach that resonates with the Depths?

Cultural Traits

  • Patience of stone: Rushing is foolish; quality takes time
  • Resonant magic: Power flows through vibration and harmony
  • Craft pride: Work speaks louder than words; reputation is built by what you create
  • Geological faith: The earth has a voice; listening is wisdom
  • Practical honor: Oaths are binding; debts are remembered
  • Suspicious of surface: The world above changes too quickly
If You’re From the Stonebound Depths…

You Know:

  • How to identify metals and minerals by sight, sound, and feel
  • Resonance techniques for shaping stone and metal
  • That the Deep Roots are sacred and ancient
  • The importance of proper tool maintenance
  • How to navigate underground without getting lost

Others See You As:

  • Stubborn and slow to decide
  • Incredibly skilled at crafts
  • Blunt and direct in speech
  • Uncomfortable above ground
  • Trustworthy once your word is given

Why Travel to Northreach:

  • Eclipse Day’s tremors need investigation
  • Rare minerals reported in northern mountains
  • Testing surface weapons and armor in field conditions
  • Family honor demands proving yourself
  • Exile or voluntary departure to see the sky
  • Studying geological patterns connected to the Depths

Sample Character Concepts

  • Borin Deepstrider, Mountain Dwarf Cleric (Forge Domain)
    Rune-singer studying surface forges and their inferior resonance. Came to Northreach because “if you can make a blade sing in winter wind, you’ve mastered the craft.”

  • Kara Stoneheart, Shield Dwarf Fighter (Eldritch Knight)
    Former Depths guard who wanted to see the sun. Found surface life chaotic but exhilarating. Applies underground tactical thinking to surface combat.

  • Rurik Ironvein, Dwarf Wizard (War Magic)
    Deep-reader who sensed disturbances in the earth pointing north. Sent to investigate whether surface anomalies connect to changes in the Depths. Doesn’t like being cold.

THE TEN REGIONS

 

 

5. Vharoxis — The City of Masks

Where smugglers trade in broad daylight, where masks hide more than faces, and where chaos is currency. Vharoxis is opportunity and danger in equal measure.

Overview

Vharoxis is the infamous outlaw city where laws are suggestions, factions shift weekly, and everyone wears at least one mask. Built on a jagged peninsula surrounded by treacherous reefs, the city thrives on smuggling, espionage, black-market trade, and controlled chaos. There’s no king, no council—only the syndicates that rule the districts and the understanding that business continues regardless.

  • Climate: Coastal Mediterranean; foggy and temperate
  • Population: ~15,000 (diverse, transient)
  • Government: Syndicate rule (shifting)
  • Economy: Smuggling, contraband, assassination, information

Common Backgrounds

  • Criminal
    The obvious choice. You’re a thief, smuggler, fence, or con artist trained in a city where crime is the only real industry.

  • Charlatan
    Masks aren’t just fashion—they’re business tools. You’ve learned to be whoever you need to be.

  • Spy
    Vharoxis hosts more spies per capita than any city in Aevoria. You gathered secrets for someone—or sold them to the highest bidder.

  • Urchin
    You grew up in the Ember Warrens or other slums, surviving through cunning, speed, and knowing which alleys lead where.

Character Tie-In Questions

  1. Which syndicate did you work for—or betray?
  2. What’s the worst deal you ever made, and what were the consequences?
  3. Do you still wear masks, or have you left that behind?
  4. Who in Vharoxis wants you dead, captured, or returned?
  5. What’s the one job you refused to take—and why?

Cultural Traits

  • Anonymity is safety: Don’t give real names; masks are expected
  • Profit over principle: Everything has a price; morality is expensive
  • Reputation matters: Not your real identity—your professional reputation
  • Faction fluidity: Alliances change; loyalty is situational
  • Surface civility: Violence is bad for business; professionals handle disputes quietly
  • Opportunity mindset: Chaos creates chances; adaptation is survival
If You’re From Vharoxis…

You Know:

  • How to navigate black markets and read syndicate politics
  • At least three escape routes from any room
  • That trust is transactional and temporary
  • Which questions get you killed
  • How to spot undercover agents and informants

Others See You As:

  • Untrustworthy by default
  • Skilled but morally flexible
  • Street-smart and resourceful
  • Paranoid (perhaps justifiably)
  • Someone with dangerous connections

Why Travel to Northreach:

  • Fleeing a deal gone wrong or syndicate politics
  • Following a contract or target
  • Smuggling routes through the frontier
  • Information gathering for a patron
  • Fresh start under a new identity
  • Avoiding heat until things cool down

Sample Character Concepts

  • Raven (not her real name), Human Rogue (Assassin)
    Former Ember Veil operative who completed one job too many. Disappeared to Northreach where no one knows her face. Wears different personas like clothing.

  • Dante Blackwater, Tiefling Warlock (Hexblade)
    Masked Market dealer in magical contraband who crossed the wrong people. His pact weapon and frontier expertise make him valuable to the Wardens—and dangerous.

  • Silva Thorngage, Half-Elf Ranger (Monster Slayer)
    Grew up in Vharoxis slums hunting rats and worse. Came north because frontier monsters are more honest than city predators. Direct in a way that unsettles people expecting masks.

THE TEN REGIONS

 

 

6. The Shattered Coast — Maritime Frontier

Where ships meet their doom on razor reefs, where salvagers grow rich on wrecks, and where the sea whispers secrets to those brave—or foolish—enough to listen.

Overview

The Shattered Coast is a treacherous stretch of shoreline along Aevoria’s western edge where jagged reefs and unpredictable tides have created a graveyard of ships—and opportunities for those willing to risk the waters. Despite the danger, the coast is a vital trade route and hub for maritime commerce, smuggling, and salvage operations. Strange things wash ashore here, and stranger things lurk beneath the waves.

  • Climate: Stormy coastal; unpredictable weather
  • Population: ~8,000 (spread across settlements)
  • Government: Harbor councils, loose alliances
  • Economy: Trade, smuggling, salvage, fishing

Common Backgrounds

  • Sailor
    You know ships, tides, navigation, and the hundred ways the sea can kill you. Coastal life is in your blood.

  • Pirate (Sailor variant)
    The Shattered Coast hosts more pirates than any region outside Vharoxis. Some call it freedom; others call it theft with extra steps.

  • Fisher (Folk Hero variant)
    You’ve spent your life pulling food from the sea while avoiding the things that pull back.

  • Smuggler (Criminal variant)
    The coast’s maze of reefs and coves makes it perfect for moving contraband. You know the safe channels—and you’re not sharing.

Cultural Traits

  • Respect the sea: The water demands caution; arrogance drowns
  • Salvage rights: What the sea claims, salvagers can take—if they dare
  • Superstition: Sailors have rituals, omens, and taboos for good reason
  • Storm-reading: Weather prediction is survival; watch the sky constantly
  • Coastal solidarity: Different crews compete, but everyone helps during disasters
  • Secret-keeping: Some wrecks are cursed; some catches shouldn’t be examined
If You’re From the Shattered Coast…

You Know:

  • How to read tides, clouds, and reef patterns
  • That some shipwrecks are cursed or haunted
  • Smuggling routes and safe harbors
  • The sea takes more than it gives
  • Strange things wash ashore—especially lately

Others See You As:

  • Weather-worn and practical
  • Superstitious or spiritual
  • Good in a crisis
  • Possibly involved in smuggling
  • Someone with sea stories worth hearing

Why Travel to Northreach:

  • Following trade routes inland
  • Fleeing coastal dangers
  • Investigating strange salvage or phenomena
  • Crew disbanded after disaster
  • Seeking steady work away from storms
  • Following rumors of Aeorian artifacts inland

Sample Character Concepts

  • Captain Mira Stormcrow, Human Fighter (Battle Master)
    Former merchant captain whose ship met the reefs. Crew scattered, but she survived with her tactical mind intact. Leads Warden teams like a ship’s crew.

  • Finn Tidecaller, Water Genasi Druid (Circle of the Land - Coast)
    Tide-priest from a fishing village who sensed wrongness in the waters. Came north following patterns in the storms, seeking their source.

  • “Lucky” Jack Kelver, Halfling Rogue (Swashbuckler)
    Salvage diver who pulled up one relic too many from the Gravewater Trench. Got out before whatever was awakening down there fully noticed him. Mostly.

Character Tie-In Questions

  1. What ship did you serve on, and what happened to it?
  2. What’s the strangest thing you’ve pulled from the sea?
  3. Do you miss the water, or are you glad to be inland?
  4. What superstition or ritual do you still observe?
  5. Who or what are you running from on the coast?

THE TEN REGIONS

 

 

7. The Emberlands — The Volcanic South

Where fire carves the landscape and ash paints the sky, where the earth itself breathes heat and fury. The Emberlands forge hard people in hotter fires.

Overview

The Emberlands are a harsh volcanic region in southern Aevoria where rivers of magma flow, ash storms sweep across blackened plains, and the land seems to breathe with primal power. Despite the danger, the region hosts resilient communities, valuable mineral deposits, and ancient traditions tied to fire, transformation, and the raw strength of the earth. Those who survive here are forged by adversity into something stronger.

  • Climate: Hot, dry, volcanic; ash storms frequent
  • Population: ~10,000 (scattered settlements)
  • Government: Fire Councils (forge-master oligarchies)
  • Economy: Mining, metalwork, obsidian craft, fire-gems

Common Backgrounds

  • Guild Artisan (Fire-Forge)
    You’re trained in the legendary fire-forges of Cindermarch, where volcanic heat creates unmatched metalwork.

  • Outlander
    Nomadic tribes follow the rhythms of the volcanic land, moving with the flows and storms. You know how to survive in impossible conditions.

  • Hermit
    The Emberlands attract those seeking isolation, transformation, or penance. Fire has a way of burning away everything but truth.

  • Soldier
    You served in the defense forces protecting mining operations, settlements, or caravans from fire-touched creatures and rival clans.

Cultural Traits

  • Endurance pride: Surviving here proves your worth; weakness is culled by the land
  • Fire reverence: Destruction and creation are one; fire transforms
  • Practical toughness: Complaints won’t save you; action will
  • Resource scarcity: Water is precious; waste is unforgivable
  • Crafting excellence: If you make something, make it to last
  • Rebirth belief: What burns away reveals truth beneath
If You’re From the Emberlands…

You Know:

  • How to recognize toxic gases, unstable ground, and coming eruptions
  • That fire isn’t evil—it’s honest and impartial
  • The value of water and the cost of waste
  • How to work metal, glass, or stone shaped by heat
  • That soft people don’t last in hard places

Others See You As:

  • Tough, perhaps to the point of harshness
  • Uncomfortable in cold or wet environments
  • Skilled at working with fire and forges
  • Scarred (physically or emotionally)
  • Someone who’s survived worse than this

Why Travel to Northreach:

  • Escaping volcanic disaster or clan conflict
  • Seeking rare minerals reported in northern mountains
  • Testing fire-forged equipment in extreme cold
  • Proving yourself in different hardships
  • Following geomantic patterns or resonance
  • Fresh start after losing everything to the fire

Sample Character Concepts

  • Kael Ashwalker, Human Monk (Way of the Four Elements)
    Raised in a fire-cult that worships transformation through heat. Came north to test whether fire-discipline works in ice. Finding interesting parallels.

  • Magna Emberforge, Fire Genasi Artificer (Artillerist)
    Master fire-forge artisan studying how extreme cold affects her designs. Brought her portable forge to Northreach. Constantly complains about the temperature.

  • Scar, Half-Orc Barbarian (Path of the Ancestral Guardian)
    Sole survivor of a tribe consumed by volcanic eruption. Came north carrying their ashes and memories. Rage burns as hot as the homeland she lost.

Character Tie-In Questions

  1. What did the fire take from you—and what did it give?
  2. How do you cope with the cold after a lifetime of heat?
  3. What did you forge, create, or craft in the Emberlands?
  4. Why did you leave a land that shaped you so completely?
  5. Do you believe the land is “reawakening,” as some claim?

THE TEN REGIONS

 

 

8. The Verdant Marches — The Green Stirring

Where ancient forests breathe and the land speaks in whispers, where life grows with almost aggressive vitality. The Marches are awakening to something new and strange.

Overview

The Verdant Marches are a vast stretch of untamed wilderness where ancient forests, rolling meadows, and tangled swamps blend into a living tapestry. In recent years, the land has begun to change—animals show unusual intelligence, plants react to emotion, and druids speak of whispers from the earth. Locals call it the “Green Stirring,” and no one fully understands what it means.

  • Climate: Lush temperate; humid and vibrant
  • Population: ~6,000 (nomadic and village-based)
  • Government: Druidic circles, clan elders
  • Economy: Hunting, gathering, herbal trade, beast-taming

Common Backgrounds

  • Outlander
    You’re from one of the nomadic clans or isolated villages living in harmony with the ever-changing wilderness.

  • Hermit
    The Marches offer profound isolation for those seeking communion with nature. You lived among the whispers long before others noticed them.

  • Folk Hero
    You defended your community from awakened predators, guided lost travelers through shifting forests, or discovered the truth about the Green Stirring.

  • Acolyte
    Druidic circles serve as spiritual leaders. You’re trained in reading the land, performing rituals, and interpreting what the wilderness is trying to say.

Cultural Traits

  • Land-listening: The wilderness communicates; wise people listen
  • Adaptive living: The forest changes; you change with it
  • Beast kinship: Animals are neighbors, not resources
  • Circle authority: Druids interpret the land’s will
  • Minimal footprint: Take only what you need; leave no lasting scars
  • Stirring awareness: Something is waking, and everyone feels it
If You’re From the Verdant Marches…

You Know:

  • How to read plant growth, animal behavior, and seasonal patterns
  • That the land is more aware than it used to be
  • Which plants heal, harm, or alter consciousness
  • How to move through wilderness without leaving trace
  • That civilization and nature must balance

Others See You As:

  • Mysterious and spiritual
  • Uncomfortable in cities or stone buildings
  • Connected to animals in unsettling ways
  • Prophetic or strange
  • Someone who understands the wild

Why Travel to Northreach:

  • Investigating whether the Stirring extends north
  • Fleeing changes in the Marches that frightened you
  • Following druidic visions or mandates
  • Seeking communities where wilderness and civilization meet
  • Testing whether you can live among “stone people”
  • Warning others about what’s awakening

Sample Character Concepts

  • Rowan Greencloak, Human Ranger (Beast Master)
    Clan hunter whose animal companion began speaking in dreams. Came north following patterns the wilderness showed him through his wolf’s eyes.

  • Thistledown, Firbolg Druid (Circle of Dreams)
    Wandering druid who experienced visions during the Green Stirring. Sent north by her circle to observe how the awakening manifests in different environments.

  • Moss, Half-Elf Rogue (Scout)
    Grew up in a Marches village before the Stirring. Left because the forest she knew became something she didn’t recognize. Homesick for a place that no longer exists.

Character Tie-In Questions

  1. What did the land tell you before you left?
  2. How do you feel about cities, walls, and “tamed” nature?
  3. Has an animal ever spoken to you—and what did it say?
  4. Do you see the Stirring as dangerous, wonderful, or both?
  5. What druidic circle or clan do you still answer to?

THE TEN REGIONS

 

 

9. The Sunken Dominion — Drowned Mysteries

Where crystalline towers rise from the seabed, where currents glow with ancient light, and where divers return changed—if they return at all. The depths hold secrets older than memory.

Overview

Far beneath the waves lies the Sunken Dominion, a drowned civilization whose ruins stretch across the ocean floor. Strange relics wash ashore, glowing currents appear without warning, and sea creatures behave unnaturally. Most believe it was a coastal empire swallowed by cataclysm; others claim it was always a realm of the deep. Either way, the Dominion is awakening—and not everyone who studies it remains unchanged.

  • Climate: Coastal and maritime
  • Population: Coastal settlements ~3,000
  • Government: Loose harbor councils, diving guilds
  • Economy: Salvage, deep-diving, relic trade, fishing

Common Backgrounds

  • Sailor (Deep Diver variant)
    You’re trained in the dangerous art of deep-water salvage, recovering relics from the drowned ruins below.

  • Sage (Marine Scholar)
    You study the Dominion’s artifacts, architecture, and anomalies, trying to understand what it was and why it calls.

  • Hermit
    You lived in isolation near the water, drawn to the whispers from below. Some say you spent too long listening.

  • Haunted One (CoS variant)
    You dove too deep, saw too much, or brought back something that won’t let you go. The Dominion marked you.

Cultural Traits

  • Ocean reverence: The sea gives and takes; respect both
  • Relic caution: Dominion artifacts are valuable and dangerous
  • Diving superstition: Rituals protect divers; ignoring them invites disaster
  • Changed acceptance: The deep changes people; it’s expected
  • Secret burden: Some discoveries shouldn’t be shared
  • Depth fear: Even experienced divers know there are limits
If You’re From the Sunken Dominion…

You Know:

  • How to hold your breath longer than should be possible
  • That some ruins call to you in dreams
  • The signs of someone touched by the deep
  • Which artifacts are safe and which aren’t
  • That water remembers things land forgets

Others See You As:

  • Strange or distant
  • Obsessed with the ocean
  • Uncomfortable on dry land
  • Possibly touched by something unnatural
  • Someone with haunted eyes

Why Travel to Northreach:

  • Fleeing what you found in the depths
  • Following patterns that point inland and north
  • Seeking distance from the calling
  • Investigating whether Dominion ruins extend underground
  • Proving you can leave the water behind
  • Running from what the tide brought in

Sample Character Concepts

  • Marina Deepcaller, Water Genasi Warlock (Fathomless)
    Deep diver who formed a pact with something in the Luminous Trenches. It taught her power in exchange for service she’s still fulfilling. Came north because “it” wanted her to.

  • Coral (birth name forgotten), Triton Paladin (Oath of Redemption)
    Former salvager who recovered a relic that showed her terrible visions. Swore an oath to prevent others from waking what sleeps below. Hunts Dominion artifacts.

  • Jonas Tiderunner, Human Wizard (School of Illusion)
    Marine scholar who studied Glassspire geometry until it started appearing in his waking vision. Fled north to study “safer” magic. The patterns followed him.

Character Tie-In Questions

  1. What did you find in the depths—and did you bring it back?
  2. Do you still hear the ocean calling, even this far inland?
  3. What changed in you after diving too deep?
  4. Who did you lose to the Dominion’s ruins?
  5. Do the glowing currents appear in your dreams?

THE TEN REGIONS

 

 

10. The Far North — Where the World Ends

Where blizzards rage without end, where ice stretches to the horizon, and where ruins emerge from eternal frost. The Far North is where civilization stops and something older begins.

Overview

The Far North is a frozen wasteland beyond Palebank Village, one of the most inhospitable regions in the known world. It’s a place where survival is measured in hours without proper preparation, where nomadic groups eke out existence on the edges, and where ancient ruins emerge from the ice during brief thaws. Few travel there by choice. Fewer return unchanged.

  • Climate: Subarctic to arctic; perpetual winter
  • Population: ~800 (nomadic and isolated)
  • Government: Clan elders, survival hierarchy
  • Economy: Hunting, ice fishing, limited scavenging

Common Backgrounds

  • Outlander
    You’re from one of the nomadic reindeer-herding or ice-fisher clans that follow the herds and seasons across the frozen waste.

  • Hermit
    You sought ultimate isolation in the world’s harshest environment. Perhaps you found enlightenment—or just frostbite and madness.

  • Folk Hero
    You saved your clan from a blizzard, discovered a safe route, or defended against ice-touched predators. Your people remember.

  • Soldier (Survivor variant)
    You served in a failed expedition, refugee group, or research mission. You survived when others didn’t.

Cultural Traits

  • Survival pragmatism: If it doesn’t help you live, it doesn’t matter
  • Resource sharing: Hoarding food in winter is murder
  • Respect for cold: The ice is honest—it’ll kill without malice
  • Oral tradition: Stories are survival guides passed through generations
  • Minimal possessions: Own only what you can carry when moving
  • Silent endurance: Complaints waste breath and energy
If You’re From the Far North…

You Know:

  • How to predict deadly storms hours in advance
  • That warmth is life; never waste fuel
  • The ruins in the ice are dangerous for reasons beyond cold
  • How to survive on minimal food and water
  • That some sounds in the wind aren’t wind

Others See You As:

  • Taciturn and grim
  • Incredibly tough
  • Uncomfortable in “warm” weather (above freezing)
  • Wasteful-averse to an extreme degree
  • Someone who’s seen things they won’t discuss

Why Travel to Northreach:

  • Your clan was lost to the ice
  • Following game herds south
  • Fleeing something emerging from the ruins
  • Seeking “warmth” (even Northreach seems tropical)
  • Guiding an expedition that never returned
  • Warning of what’s waking in the frozen north

Sample Character Concepts

  • Eira Frostborn, Human Barbarian (Path of the Totem Warrior - Bear)
    Last survivor of a clan lost to an unexpected deep freeze. Came south with their story and determination to ensure others remember. Rage is grief given voice.

  • Njal Icecaller, Goliath Ranger (Monster Slayer)
    Former expedition guide who encountered something in the Far North ruins that shouldn’t exist. Hunts creatures touched by ancient cold. Doesn’t talk about what he saw.

  • Frost, Kalashtar Monk (Way of the Long Death)
    Hermit who meditated in ice caves until something spoke back. Emerged with uncanny cold resistance and fragments of memory that aren’t his own. Seeking answers.

Character Tie-In Questions

  1. What did the ice take from you?
  2. How do you cope with the relative “heat” of Northreach?
  3. What’s the closest you came to dying in the Far North?
  4. What did you see in the ruins that made you leave?
  5. Do you ever want to return—or would death be preferable?

THE TEN REGIONS

 

 

Cross-Regional Tensions

Understanding how different regions view each other enriches roleplay and creates natural character conflicts—not hostile, but the friction of different worldviews meeting.

Regional Relationship Matrix

Nullwood Too cautious; won’t take necessary risks
Stonebound Reliable but stubborn; “my way or the long way”
Vharoxis Untrustworthy; probably criminals

Emberlands Tough but harsh; need to learn flexibility

Stonebound Master crafters; lack artistic vision
