LANGUAGES OF AEVORIA

 

 

Cultural Practices

Greetings and Social Etiquette

How you greet someone—and how they greet you—sets the tone for every interaction. Different regions have different expectations.

Formal Greetings

Northreach:

  • Firm handshake (hand-to-wrist for equals, hand-to-shoulder for respect)
  • Eye contact expected
  • Simple: “Well met” or stating your name directly
  • Offering shelter: “Safe hearth and warm walls”

Solaris Dominion:

  • Elaborate bows or hand-over-heart gestures
  • Flowery language expected in formal contexts
  • “May your song never fade” (standard greeting)
  • Introduction includes titles and achievements

Nullwood Expanse:

  • Soft touch to forehead or chest (asking permission first)
  • Quiet, respectful tone
  • “Peace in memory” (common greeting)
  • Silence is not awkward—it’s courteous

Stonebound Depths:

  • Firm handshake (strong grip shows strength, not aggression)
  • “Stone endures” or “May the earth hold you firm”
  • Formal contexts: state your craft or clan
  • Offering hospitality: “My hearth is yours”

Vharoxis:

  • No handshakes (vulnerability)
  • Nod or slight bow from safe distance
  • Names are optional; aliases expected
  • “Fortune favors” (neutral greeting)

Emberlands:

  • Fist-to-chest salute
  • Direct eye contact (looking away suggests weakness)
  • “Fire tempers” (greeting between equals)
  • Physical strength displays are common

Verdant Marches:

  • Touching foreheads (close friends/family)
  • Hand over heart (respectful greeting)
  • “The land provides” (common saying)
  • Offering food as greeting gesture

Informal Greetings

Among Friends:

  • Northreach: “You’re still kicking” or “Survived another day”
  • Solaris: “Well met, friend!” with exaggerated gestures
  • Nullwood: Quiet acknowledgment, gentle smiles
  • Stonebound: “How’s your forge?” (metaphorical—means “how are you”)
  • Vharoxis: Coded phrases and hand signals
  • Emberlands: Shoulder bumps, casual fist-salutes
  • Verdant Marches: Warm hugs, casual physical contact

Terms of Address

Showing Respect:

  • Northreach: Use first names; “Master” or “Mistress” for skilled craftspeople
  • Solaris: Titles matter (Maestro, Virtuoso, Luminary, etc.)
  • Nullwood: “Elder” for aged elves; “Keeper” for Memory Keepers
  • Stonebound: Clan name + craft (e.g., “Ironforge the Smith”)
  • Vharoxis: Avoid names; use “friend,” “associate,” or titles of rank
  • Emberlands: Earned names (often related to deeds)
  • Verdant Marches: “Wanderer,” “Brother/Sister,” or nature-titles

Important NPCs:

  • Guild leaders: “Steward,” “Marshal,” “Guildmaster”
  • Religious figures: “Father/Mother,” “Priest/Priestess,” “Reverend”
  • Nobility: “Lord/Lady,” “Your Grace,” “Your Excellency”
  • Scholars: “Master,” “Professor,” “Lorewarden”
Social Fumbles

Using the wrong greeting or title can impose disadvantage on Charisma checks. Your DM might rule that:

  • Being too formal in Northreach makes you seem pretentious
  • Being too casual in Solaris seems disrespectful
  • Breaking the silence in Nullwood is jarring
  • Using real names in Vharoxis marks you as an outsider

CULTURAL PRACTICES

 

 

Dining Customs

Breaking bread—or refusing it—carries deep cultural meaning.

Meal Structure

Northreach:

  • Two main meals: morning (hearty) and evening (communal)
  • Midday snacks (portable food for workers)
  • Nothing is wasted; clean your plate or save leftovers
  • Meals are practical fuel, not performances

Solaris:

  • Three elaborate meals: breakfast (light), lunch (social), dinner (grand)
  • Multiple courses expected in formal settings
  • Presentation matters as much as taste
  • Dining is performance and social maneuvering

Nullwood:

  • Quiet, contemplative eating
  • Food blessed before consumption
  • Minimal meat (vegetarian-leaning)
  • Meals are meditative, not rushed

Stonebound:

  • Two heavy meals: mid-morning and evening
  • Food served in courses, each announced
  • Ale or mead accompanies every meal
  • Eating is communal bonding

Emberlands:

  • Whenever food is available (irregular)
  • Communal cooking over open fires
  • Spicy, heavily seasoned food
  • Sharing food is sacred

Verdant Marches:

  • Grazing culture (many small meals)
  • Fresh food preferred (little preservation)
  • Meals outdoors when possible
  • Food blessed with druidic prayers

Food Taboos

Breaking food taboos can cause genuine offense:

  • Nullwood: Refusing blessed food insults the preparer
  • Stonebound: Wasting food is deeply disrespectful
  • Emberlands: Eating alone when others are hungry is shameful
  • Verdant Marches: Killing animals needlessly or wasting meat
  • Northreach: Complaining about food insults survival efforts

Table Manners

Universal:

  • Wait for host to begin eating
  • Don’t reach across others
  • Offer dishes to neighbors before serving yourself
  • Thank the cook/host

Regional Differences:

  • Northreach: Elbows on table acceptable; talking with mouth full tolerated
  • Solaris: Perfect posture; small bites; constant conversation
  • Nullwood: Silence preferred; chewing quietly essential
  • Stonebound: Loud eating acceptable; compliment the cook enthusiastically
  • Vharoxis: Masks removed or lifted; eat quickly and stay alert
  • Emberlands: Eating with hands common; licking fingers acceptable
  • Verdant Marches: Relaxed; bare feet common; casual atmosphere

Drinking Customs

Toasts:

  • Northreach: “To those who aren’t here” (remembering the dead/absent)
  • Solaris: Elaborate poetic toasts; first toast to host
  • Stonebound: “Stone and steel!” or “To the mountain!”
  • Emberlands: “May the fire within never die!”
  • Verdant Marches: “To the land and its bounty”

Alcohol:

  • Refusing the first drink can be insulting
  • After the first, you can decline without offense
  • Dwarves will challenge drinking capacity (friendly competition)
  • Getting drunk in Nullwood is deeply inappropriate
  • Solaris: Wine preferred; know your varieties
  • Northreach: Ale and spirits; practical drinks

CULTURAL PRACTICES

 

 

Gift-Giving Traditions

Gifts carry meaning beyond their material value.

When Gifts Are Appropriate

Common Occasions:

  • First meeting with important NPCs
  • Accepting hospitality
  • Formal diplomatic exchanges
  • Successful business deals
  • Celebrations and festivals
  • Apologies and reconciliation

Timing Matters:

  • Northreach: Gifts after services rendered, not before (seems like bribery)
  • Solaris: Elaborate gift presentation during formal events
  • Stonebound: Gifts when accepting hospitality
  • Vharoxis: “Gifts” are transactions; nothing is free
  • Emberlands: Spontaneous gifts show strong bonds

Regional Gift Preferences

Region Appreciated Gifts Insulting Gifts
Northreach Practical tools, preserved food, quality materials Frivolous luxuries, “city” fashions
Solaris Art, books, wine, musical instruments Crude tools, cheap items
Nullwood Seeds, rare plants, memories (stories), silence-stones Loud items, wasteful luxuries
Stonebound Quality metals, tools, stonework, ale Poorly made items, flimsy construction
Vharoxis Information, leverage, useful contacts “Honest” gifts (always suspect ulterior motive)
Emberlands Fire-touched items, weapons, survival gear Fragile decorations, impractical items
Verdant Marches Seeds, natural items, carved wood Manufactured goods, metal weapons

Gift-Giving Protocol

Presentation:

  • Northreach: Simple, direct, no ceremony
  • Solaris: Elaborate presentation, public acknowledgment
  • Nullwood: Private, quiet, no expectation of immediate reciprocation
  • Stonebound: Present with both hands, explain significance
  • Vharoxis: Discrete exchange, no public display
  • Emberlands: Dramatic presentation, physical strength sometimes involved

Receiving Gifts:

  • Always accept first offer (refusing is insulting)
  • Express gratitude appropriate to culture
  • Reciprocity expected but timeline varies
  • Dwarves: Acknowledge with “The mountain remembers”
  • Elves: “My memory honors this”
  • Northreach: “Appreciated” or “Won’t forget it”
Some cultures view gifts as creating obligations:
  • Stonebound: Every gift must eventually be repaid (stone remembers debts)
  • Vharoxis: Gifts always have strings attached; accepting means owing
  • Nullwood: Gifts are freely given; expecting return is rude
  • Solaris: Public gifts require public reciprocation

CULTURAL PRACTICES

 

 

Hospitality Expectations

The customs of host and guest govern much of frontier life.

Guest Rights

Universal Principles:

  • Guests are under host’s protection
  • Violence against guests is grave offense
  • Guests must not harm host or property
  • Both parties bound by honor

Duration:

  • Northreach: “Three days and three nights” (traditional)
  • Solaris: Until host offers departure gifts
  • Stonebound: “Stone holds” (essentially permanent until guest leaves)
  • Nullwood: As long as guest respects silence and customs
  • Emberlands: Until next dawn (nomadic culture)

Host Duties

Minimum Expected:

  • Shelter from elements
  • Food and drink
  • Safe place to sleep
  • Information about local dangers

Regional Variations:

  • Northreach: Practical accommodations; you might share quarters
  • Solaris: Guest quarters prepared; entertainment provided
  • Stonebound: Best accommodations offered; ale flows freely
  • Nullwood: Quiet space; needs met without asking
  • Vharoxis: “Hospitality” is business transaction
  • Emberlands: Share what they have (may be little)
  • Verdant Marches: Communal sleeping; abundant food

Guest Duties

Minimum Expected:

  • Respect host’s property and customs
  • Contribute to household (offer labor or payment)
  • Defend household if attacked
  • Leave no worse than you found it

Contributions:

  • Northreach: Chop wood, repair items, share news
  • Solaris: Entertain, share stories, bring prestige
  • Stonebound: Craft work, manual labor, songs/stories
  • Verdant Marches: Help with harvest, tend animals
Breaking Hospitality

Violating guest-host customs is one of the most serious social offenses:

Attacking your host: Marks you as oath-breaker permanently Stealing from host: Reputation destroyed in all honest communities Betraying host’s trust: Word spreads; doors close everywhere Host attacking guest: Loss of honor; may face exile or worse

These violations follow you. In Northreach, a broken hearth-oath is remembered for generations.

Payment vs. Free Lodging

When to Pay:

  • Inns and taverns (always)
  • Professional lodging houses
  • Cities and large towns
  • When explicitly asked

When Payment Is Insult:

  • Invited into someone’s home
  • Offered shelter during emergency
  • Among friends and allies
  • After establishing guest-right

Appropriate Reciprocation:

  • Services (repair, guard duty, storytelling)
  • Gifts (see gift-giving section)
  • Future hospitality (return the favor)
  • Public praise (especially in Solaris)

CULTURAL PRACTICES

 

 

Business and Trade Practices

Commerce follows different rules in different places.

Negotiation Styles

Northreach:

  • Direct, honest, practical
  • Haggling is moderate (not aggressive)
  • Price reflects fair value plus reasonable profit
  • Handshake seals deals
  • Breaking contracts destroys reputation

Solaris:

  • Theatrical, relationship-based
  • Extensive haggling expected (part of the performance)
  • Initial prices inflated 30-50%
  • Written contracts for anything significant
  • Witnesses for important deals

Stonebound:

  • Straightforward, formal
  • Quality and craftsmanship emphasized
  • Less haggling (dwarves know their value)
  • Written contracts in runes
  • Contracts are sacred; breaking one is unthinkable

Vharoxis:

  • Everything is negotiable
  • Never accept first offer
  • Hidden costs assumed
  • Written contracts have loopholes
  • Trust no one; verify everything

Verdant Marches:

  • Barter preferred over coin
  • Emphasis on fair exchange
  • Community benefit considered
  • Oral agreements honored
  • Druidic elders mediate disputes

Haggling vs. Fixed Prices

Region Haggling? Expected Range Notes
Northreach Moderate 5-15% off asking Don’t insult with lowball offers
Solaris Expected 30-50% off initial Part of social dance
Stonebound Minimal 0-10% off Quality justifies price
Vharoxis Aggressive 20-60% off Everything negotiable
Verdant Marches Rare Barter-based Fair exchange preferred

Contract and Oath Customs

Binding Force:

Oaths and contracts carry different weight:

  • Northreach: Spoken oaths are binding; breaking them destroys reputation. Written contracts for significant transactions.

  • Solaris: Everything in writing, multiple copies, witnesses. Oral agreements are “preliminary discussions.”

  • Stonebound: Oaths sworn on stone or steel are absolutely binding. Breaking such an oath is cultural anathema.

  • Nullwood: Oaths sworn before Memory Keepers are magically and culturally binding. Memory itself holds you accountable.

  • Vharoxis: Written contracts only; spoken promises mean nothing. Even written contracts have exploitable loopholes.

  • Emberlands: Fire oaths (sworn while touching flame) are unbreakable. Lesser oaths are flexible.

  • Verdant Marches: Oaths sworn before druids or nature spirits are binding. The land itself witnesses.

Merchant Guilds

Guild Membership:

  • Guarantees standards and quality
  • Provides connections and protection
  • Sets prices and trading terms
  • Mediates disputes

Notable Guilds:

  • Waystone Merchants’ Alliance (Northreach): Fair trade, reliable goods
  • Solaris Artisan Consortium: Luxury goods, artistic items
  • Deepforge Crafters (Stonebound): Metalwork, stonework, quality tools
  • Verdant Trade Circle: Natural goods, fair exchange emphasis

CULTURAL PRACTICES

 

 

Regional Customs and Taboos

Northreach — The Frozen Frontier

Northreach values practical competence, keeping your word, mutual aid, and self-reliance. Frontier life is hard; people who make it harder through incompetence or dishonesty are remembered unfavorably.

Things Considered Polite

  • Offering help during emergencies: Community survival depends on mutual aid
  • Maintaining your tools and property: Shows competence and respect for resources
  • Sharing warnings about dangers: Wolves, bandits, bad weather—warn your neighbors
  • Keeping your promises: Your word is your reputation
  • Being direct and honest: Flowery speech is suspicious; say what you mean
  • Respecting the winter: Take cold seriously; prepare properly

Things Considered Rude

  • Idle bragging without skills to back it up: Actions matter, not words
  • Refusing to help during genuine emergencies: Marks you as selfish
  • Wasting resources (especially food or fuel): Disrespectful to everyone’s survival
  • Being a constant burden: Ask for help when needed, but don’t make it a habit
  • Excessive formality or pretension: “City manners” seem fake and suspicious
  • Breaking promises or contracts: Destroys your reputation permanently

Serious Offenses in Northreach

Breaking Hearth-Oath:

Violating guest-host customs or sworn promises. Marks you as oath-breaker; reputation destroyed across the frontier.

Deliberately Endangering the Community:

Through incompetence, sabotage, or selfishness. May result in exile or worse.

Abandoning Others in Danger:

Especially during winter or wilderness emergencies. Considered cowardice and betrayal.

Desecrating the Dead:

The frontier kills enough people; disrespecting the dead is unforgivable.

Religious Observances

  • No dominant religion: Pragmatic frontier spirituality
  • Respect the wild: Nature is dangerous and should be respected
  • Remember the dead: Toast absent friends; maintain graves
  • Seasonal festivals: Harvest celebrations, midwinter feasts (practical community bonding)

Reputation Matters

Northreach society tracks reputation carefully:

Good Reputation:

  • Trusted with responsibilities
  • Offered opportunities and partnerships
  • Given benefit of doubt
  • Welcomed into communities

Bad Reputation:

  • Doors close
  • Prices increase
  • Information withheld
  • May be refused service or shelter

Recovery:

Possible through consistent actions over time, but takes years. “Fool me once, and I’ll remember. Fool me twice, and everyone will.”

REGIONAL CUSTOMS AND TABOOS

 

 

Solaris Dominion — The Cultural Capital

Solaris values artistic expression, social performance, political awareness, and cultural sophistication. Everything is a story; how you present yourself matters as much as what you accomplish.

Things Considered Polite

  • Elaborate greetings and farewells: Social grace expected
  • Appreciating art, music, and performance: Shows cultural sophistication
  • Using proper titles and forms of address: Respect for social hierarchy
  • Telling engaging stories: Solaris runs on narrative
  • Supporting local artists and performers: Cultural patronage is valued
  • Participating in public discourse: Engagement shows citizenship

Things Considered Rude

  • Being too direct or blunt: Lacks social grace
  • Ignoring artistic performances: Insults the artist and culture
  • Using crude language in formal settings: Shows lack of refinement
  • Dismissing faction politics: Seems naive or deliberately obtuse
  • Wearing obviously practical/unfashionable clothing: Social statement matters
  • Refusing to engage with stories and culture: Why are you in Solaris?
Serious Offenses in Solaris
Plagiarizing Art or Songs:

Stealing credit for creative work. Career-ending scandal; may face legal action.

Breaking Performance Etiquette:

Interrupting performances, heckling artists. Shows profound disrespect; audiences will turn against you.

Publicly Insulting the Arts:

Declaring art “useless” or dismissing cultural traditions. Marks you as barbarian.

Factional Violence in Cultural Spaces:

The Tail Spinner’s Cord and similar venues are neutral ground. Violence there is unforgivable.

Religious Observances

Multi-factional:

  • Luminary Concord: Divine law, order, traditional faith
  • Veilbound Assembly: Tolerance, balance, measured acceptance
  • Eclipse Chorus: Change, transformation, new possibilities

Daily Impact:

  • Temples are gathering spaces
  • Religious debates are entertainment
  • Eclipse Day is commemorated monthly
  • Faith is performative and public

Social Navigation

Key Skills:

  • Know which faction you’re perceived as supporting
  • Attend performances and cultural events
  • Maintain social connections
  • Tell good stories
  • Dress appropriately for context

Social Fumbles:

  • Getting faction allegiances wrong
  • Being unable to discuss current songs/stories
  • Wearing wrong clothes to wrong events
  • Boring people with lack of narrative flair

REGIONAL CUSTOMS AND TABOOS

 

 

The Nullwood Expanse — The Elven Kingdom

The Nullwood values silence, memory, emotional balance, and caution. Life is long; rushing is foolish. Everything should be considered, preserved, and approached with care.

Things Considered Polite

  • Speaking softly and moving gracefully: Respect for the quiet
  • Emotional restraint and balance: Outbursts are uncomfortable
  • Patience and deliberation: Don’t rush decisions
  • Respecting memory rituals: Central to culture
  • Asking permission before entering spaces: Privacy and boundaries matter
  • Appreciating subtlety and nuance: Direct approach lacks sophistication

Things Considered Rude

  • Being loud or boisterous: Disturbs the peace
  • Emotional outbursts (anger, excessive joy): Shows lack of control
  • Rushing or demanding quick answers: Disrespects deliberation
  • Dismissing memory customs as “dwelling on the past”: Insults core values
  • Flashy or destructive magic: Shows dangerous lack of restraint
  • Questioning the silence-wards: Core cultural practice

Serious Offenses in Nullwood

Approaching Ancient Ruins Without Permission:

Elves have cultural aversion to old sites for reasons they don’t fully articulate. Ignoring this is deeply unsettling.

Disrupting Memory Rituals:

Sacred ceremonies at the Stillwater Mirror and Memory Courts. Interruption is profound violation.

Uncontrolled Magic:

Using loud, flashy, or destructive magic without need. Shows dangerous lack of discipline.

Disturbing the Stillwater Mirror:

The lake at Vaeltharyn’s heart. Causing ripples deliberately is grave offense.

Religious Observances

  • Memory-focused spirituality: Not quite religion, not quite philosophy
  • Regular memory ceremonies: Communal processing and “pruning”
  • Silent contemplation: Daily practice
  • Respect for ancient fears: Cultural taboos about ruins treated seriously

Interaction Tips

Do:

  • Speak quietly
  • Take your time
  • Show emotional restraint
  • Ask about memory customs (they’ll explain)
  • Appreciate silence (it’s not awkward)

Don’t:

  • Rush conversations
  • Demand immediate answers
  • Show excessive emotion
  • Question why they avoid ruins
  • Cast flashy spells unnecessarily

REGIONAL CUSTOMS AND TABOOS

 

 

The Stonebound Depths — The Dwarven Kingdom

The Stonebound value craftsmanship, resonance, patience, strength, and keeping your word. Stone endures; so must we. Quality work, given time, speaks for itself.

Things Considered Polite

  • Admiring quality craftsmanship: Shows understanding and respect
  • Strong, firm handshakes: Confidence and strength
  • Keeping oaths and contracts: Absolutely essential
  • Taking time to do things right: “Done well” beats “done fast”
  • Offering and accepting hospitality: “My hearth is yours”
  • Singing, storytelling, and loud celebration: Dwarven joy is boisterous

Things Considered Rude

  • Praising shoddy workmanship: Shows ignorance
  • Rushing or cutting corners: Disrespects the craft
  • Refusing hospitality without good reason: Insults host
  • Weak or limp handshakes: Suggests untrustworthiness
  • Breaking promises or contracts: Unforgivable
  • Wasting food, drink, or materials: Disrespectful

Serious Offenses in Stonebound Culture

Breaking an Oath Sworn on Stone:

Absolutely unforgivable. Marks you as oath-breaker permanently. May face exile or blood price.

Destroying Quality Craftsmanship:

Vandalism of good work is deeply offensive. Shows disrespect for effort, skill, and time invested.

Insulting a Dwarf’s Craft:

Calling quality work “adequate” or “good enough” is serious insult. Questioning someone’s craftsmanship attacks their honor.

Disrespecting the Heartstone:

The sacred crystal formation at Khardûn-Tharum’s heart. Treating it as “just rock” is culturally offensive.

The Emberlands — Volcanic South

The Emberlands value strength, endurance, adaptability, communal bonds, and respect for fire’s power. Fire tempers; those who survive are stronger. Weakness kills; strength is honored.

Things Considered Polite

  • Demonstrating strength (physical or mental): Respect earned through prowess
  • Sharing resources in hardship: Community survival matters
  • Direct, honest communication: No time for games
  • Accepting challenges: Shows confidence
  • Respecting fire rituals: Central to culture
  • Rebuilding after destruction: Shows resilience

Things Considered Rude

  • Showing weakness unnecessarily: Invite exploitation
  • Hoarding resources during crisis: Shameful selfishness
  • Backing down from challenges without reason: Cowardice
  • Complaining about heat or hardship: Everyone suffers; deal with it
  • Refusing fire-blessed food: Insults ritual
  • Excessive caution or fear: Life is dangerous; accept it

Serious Offenses in Emberlands

Breaking Fire Oaths:

Oaths sworn while touching flame are absolutely binding. Breaking them invites volcanic wrath (they believe).

Eating Alone When Others Starve:

Selfish hoarding during hardship. May result in exile or worse.

Refusing to Rebuild:

After destruction, everyone helps rebuild. Refusing marks you as useless to community.

Extinguishing Sacred Flames:

Fire-shrines and ceremonial flames must never be intentionally put out. Grave spiritual offense.

Religious Observances

  • Fire-reverence: Fire as purifier and teacher
  • Rebirth philosophy: Destruction enables renewal
  • Strength rituals: Proving yourself through trials
  • Volcanic festivals: Celebrating eruptions as renewal
  • Fire dances: Spiritual and social practice

REGIONAL CUSTOMS AND TABOOS

 

 

The Verdant Marches — Beast-Haunted Wilds

The Marches value harmony with nature, community cooperation, druidic wisdom, and respect for the Green Stirring. The land provides—if you respect it. The land takes—if you don’t.

Things Considered Polite

  • Respecting nature and wildlife: Central philosophy
  • Sharing food and resources: Community focus
  • Consulting druids about land use: Their guidance matters
  • Minimal environmental impact: Leave no trace
  • Participating in communal efforts: Everyone contributes
  • Listening to the land: Observing natural signs

Things Considered Rude

  • Unnecessary killing of animals: Hunt for need, not sport
  • Wasting natural resources: Disrespectful
  • Ignoring druidic warnings: Dangerous and foolish
  • Damaging plants without reason: The land notices
  • Excessive greed or hoarding: Community comes first
  • Dismissing the Green Stirring: Willful ignorance

Serious Offenses in the Marches

Defiling Sacred Groves:

Ancient forests and stone circles are holy ground. Desecration invites druidic retribution—and the land’s wrath.

Poisoning Water or Land:

Deliberate environmental destruction. Exiled from all communities; druids will hunt you.

Breaking Oaths Sworn Before Druids:

The land witnesses; the land remembers. Breaking such oaths causes tangible consequences.

Killing Awakened Creatures:

Animals touched by the Green Stirring are sacred. Killing them is murder, not hunting.

Religious Observances

  • Druidic spirituality: Nature as divine
  • Seasonal festivals: Equinoxes and solstices
  • Stone circle ceremonies: Ancient sacred sites
  • Animal communion: Speaking with beasts
  • Green Stirring reverence: Awakening seen as blessing

The Sunken Dominion — Drowned Civilization

The Dominion has no living culture—but approaching its ruins carries expectations of caution, respect for the deep, and awareness that some things are best left buried.

Coastal Community Customs

  • Reporting strange findings from the deep: Safety measure
  • Respecting diving claims: Salvage rights matter
  • Quarantining potentially dangerous artifacts: Precaution
  • Supporting divers’ families: Dangerous work
  • Heeding lighthouse warnings: Lives depend on it

Serious Offenses on the Coast

  • Whistling on Ships: Summons storms (superstition, but taken deadly seriously). Crew may throw you overboard.
  • Stealing Salvage: What you pull from the deep is yours by right. Theft of salvage may result in death.
  • Abandoning Crew: Leaving shipmates in danger. You’ll never crew again; reputation destroyed.
  • Disrespecting the Drowned: The sea takes many. Speaking ill of the lost invites their return.
  • Diving Without Reporting: Settlements require divers to log their dives. Going down alone means no rescue if things go wrong.
  • Bringing Up Glowing Artifacts Unexamined: Strange relics can be dangerous. Lighthouse of Memory checks all finds.
  • Disturbing Certain Ruins: Some places are clearly marked as forbidden. Ignoring warnings invites disaster.
  • Obsession with the Deep: Divers who become obsessed with the ruins are watched carefully. Many never return—or return changed.

Sea Superstitions

  • Never whistle on ships
  • Black cats are good luck
  • Red sky at night, sailor’s delight; red sky at morning, sailors take warning
  • No women on ships (old superstition, mostly ignored now)
  • Don’t rename ships (offends previous identity)
  • Pour one out for the drowned (first drink goes to sea)

REGIONAL CUSTOMS AND TABOOS

 

 

The Far North — Frozen Wasteland

The Far North has minimal living culture—nomadic groups value survival, practical knowledge, and not asking too many questions about what lives in the ice.

Nomad Customs

  • Sharing warmth and food: Survival necessity
  • Respecting ice-fisher knowledge: They know safe routes
  • Trading fairly: Resources are scarce
  • Warning of dangers: Ice, storms, things in the ruins
  • Not questioning what people fled from: Everyone has reasons
Far North Dangers
  • Approaching Salsvault Unprepared: The ancient ruin is deadly. Going without preparation is suicide.
  • Ignoring Weather Signs: The North kills the careless. Dismissing warnings is fatal.
  • Disturbing the Ice: Some things are frozen for good reason. Don’t dig too deep.

Superstitions and Common Beliefs

Omens and Portents

Good Luck Signs

Universal:

  • Rainbows after storms
  • Finding rare flowers
  • Animals approaching peacefully
  • Successful first catches/harvests

Regional:

  • Northreach: Three crows flying together; clear skies after red dawn
  • Solaris: Seeing shooting stars during performances; finding forgotten coins
  • Nullwood: Perfect silence; finding unblemished white stones
  • Stonebound: Discovering new mineral veins; resonance harmonics
  • Vharoxis: Black cats; perfectly executed deals
  • Emberlands: Volcanic eruptions (rebirth); fire that burns blue
  • Verdant Marches: Animals leading you to water; flowering out of season

Bad Luck Signs

Universal:

  • Blood moons
  • Animals fleeing en masse
  • Sudden temperature drops
  • Unusual silence

Regional:

  • Northreach: Wolves howling at noon; snow in summer
  • Solaris: Broken instruments; songs that won’t end
  • Nullwood: Ripples on the Stillwater Mirror; uncontrolled memories surfacing
  • Stonebound: Stone cracking without cause; resonance going silent
  • Vharoxis: Masks breaking; real names spoken in Market
  • Shattered Coast: Whistling on ships; seeing ghost ships
  • Emberlands: Fire refusing to catch; cold ash where flame should be
  • Verdant Marches: Plants dying overnight; animals acting wrong

SUPERSTITIONS AND COMMON BELIEFS

 

 

Weather Superstitions

Northreach:

  • “Red sky at morning, winter’s warning”
  • “When wolves are silent, the storm is violent”
  • “Ice that sings will break in spring”

Shattered Coast:

  • “Red sky at night, sailor’s delight”
  • “Seabirds flying inland, storm’s at hand”
  • “When the fog speaks, death seeks”

Emberlands:

  • “Ash falls soft, fire comes swift”
  • “When the mountain rumbles, the wise man humbles”
  • “Cold wind from the peak means the volcano’s not asleep”

Verdant Marches:

  • “When trees bow low, the storm will blow”
  • “Animals hiding, storm’s residing”
  • “Green lightning strikes, nature fights”







Grieving Expectations

How Long:

  • Northreach: 3 days formal, then back to work
  • Solaris: 1 month public mourning
  • Nullwood: Lifelong quiet remembrance
  • Stonebound: 40 days formal, then memories in stone
  • Emberlands: 1 week, then celebration of life
  • Verdant Marches: Until the body is reclaimed by nature

Public vs. Private:

  • Solaris: Public displays expected
  • Nullwood: Private grief preferred
  • Others: Moderate public acknowledgment

Death and Mourning Customs

Funeral Practices

Northreach:

  • Body burned (practical in frozen ground)
  • Ashes scattered in meaningful place
  • Wake with stories and drinking
  • “To those who aren’t here” (toast)
  • Three days of mourning

Solaris:

  • Elaborate funeral ceremonies
  • Songs composed for the deceased
  • Public mourning displays
  • Artists commissioned to capture memory
  • Month-long memorial period

Nullwood:

  • Body returned to forest (natural burial)
  • Memory ceremony to preserve important moments
  • Quiet mourning (loud grief inappropriate)
  • Memory-stones carved
  • Centuries-long remembrance

Stonebound:

  • Entombed in stone
  • Name and craft carved in runes
  • Clan ceremonies lasting weeks
  • Tools buried with the dead
  • “Stone holds them now”

Emberlands:

  • Funeral pyre (fire returns all)
  • Possessions burned with body
  • Dancing and celebration (life honored)
  • Ashes mixed with volcanic soil
  • Rebirth philosophy

Verdant Marches:

  • Sky burial (nature reclaims)
  • Druidic ceremonies
  • Body left in sacred groves
  • Seeds planted in their honor
  • Life continues in new forms

SUPERSTITIONS AND COMMON BELIEFS

 

 

Birth and Naming Traditions

Childbirth Customs

Universal:

  • Midwives or healers attend
  • Celebrations after successful birth
  • Community support for new parents
  • Protection rituals (vary by region)

Regional Specifics:

  • Northreach: Practical support (meals, childcare help)
  • Solaris: Elaborate naming ceremonies, public announcements
  • Nullwood: Quiet welcome, memory ceremony to record first moments
  • Stonebound: Child’s name carved in stone, clan ceremonies
  • Emberlands: Fire-blessing (passing child near flame)
  • Verdant Marches: Druidic blessing, planting tree

Naming Practices

Northreach:

  • Simple, practical names
  • Family names matter (reputation)
  • Nicknames earned through deeds

Solaris:

  • Multiple names (given, family, earned titles)
  • Names chosen for sound and meaning
  • Stage names for performers

Nullwood:

  • Names given in infancy, confirmed at maturity
  • Names reflect qualities or hopes
  • Secret “true names” known only to close family

Stonebound:

  • Personal name + clan name
  • Craft name earned through mastery
  • Formal name carved in stone

Emberlands:

  • Birth names often changed
  • Earned names reflect deeds
  • Fire-names (given during trials)

Verdant Marches:

  • Nature-inspired names
  • Names can change with seasons or life stages
  • Some have multiple names for different contexts

Marriage and Bonding Customs

Engagement Practices

Northreach:

  • Simple proposal, often practical (“We work well together”)
  • Engagement period moderate (few months)
  • Public announcement at gathering
  • Shared projects (building, planning)

Solaris:

  • Elaborate courtship rituals
  • Public declarations and performances
  • Engagement can last years
  • Songs composed for beloveds

Nullwood:

  • Quiet, private proposals
  • Long contemplation period (decades acceptable)
  • Memory ceremonies to evaluate compatibility
  • Shared silence as courtship

Stonebound:

  • Formal proposal with crafted gift
  • Craft-exchange (each makes something for other)
  • Clan approval required
  • Stone-oath engagement

SUPERSTITIONS AND COMMON BELIEFS

 

 

Wedding Ceremonies

Northreach:

  • Community gathering
  • Practical vows (support, survive together)
  • Shared work after ceremony (building home)
  • Feast with toasts
  • Handfast tradition (binding hands with rope)

Solaris:

  • Theatrical public ceremonies
  • Multiple-day celebrations
  • Artistic performances
  • Elaborate vows (often poetic)
  • Public record keeping

Nullwood:

  • Private, intimate ceremonies
  • Memory-bond ritual (sharing important memories)
  • Before the Stillwater Mirror
  • No loud celebrations
  • Eternal commitment (elves live centuries)

Stonebound:

  • Forge ceremony (bonds sealed before flame)
  • Exchanging crafted rings or items
  • Clan witnesses required
  • Stone-carved names joined
  • Weeklong celebration

Emberlands:

  • Fire ceremony (couple walks through flame)
  • Community witnesses
  • Shared feast
  • Physical trials (proving strength together)
  • Dancing until dawn

Verdant Marches:

  • Outdoor ceremonies in sacred groves
  • Druidic blessings
  • Handfasting with living vines
  • Planting trees together
  • Seasonal timing (spring preferred)

Divorce/Separation

Allowed?

  • Northreach: Yes, but uncommon (reputation impact)
  • Solaris: Yes, often dramatic and public
  • Nullwood: Rare (centuries together, careful choices)
  • Stonebound: Possible but shameful (broken oath)
  • Emberlands: Yes, through ritual release
  • Verdant Marches: Yes, druids mediate

Coming-of-Age Rituals

Age of Maturity

  • Humans: 16-18 years
  • Elves: 100 years (physically mature at 20, socially at 100)
  • Dwarves: 50 years
  • Halflings: 20 years
  • Others: Varies by race

Rites of Passage

Northreach:

  • First successful solo hunt
  • Surviving winter alone
  • Completing major project
  • Community recognition feast

Solaris:

  • First public performance
  • Presenting masterwork to community
  • Faction affiliation declaration
  • Elaborate coming-of-age celebrations

Nullwood:

  • Memory ceremony (choosing which memories to keep)
  • Confirmation of adult name
  • Private ritual before elders
  • Decades-long process

Stonebound:

  • Creating journeyman-piece
  • Clan trial (specific to clan)
  • Carving adult name in stone
  • Forge ceremony

Emberlands:

  • Trial by fire (literal or metaphorical)
  • Solo survival test
  • Earning warrior-name
  • Community feast and dancing

Verdant Marches:

  • Vision quest in wilderness
  • Druidic evaluation
  • Receiving adult responsibilities
  • Naming ceremony

SUPERSTITIONS AND COMMON BELIEFS

 

 

Conflict Resolution Customs

Formal Dueling Practices

Northreach Duels

When Used: Personal honor disputes, serious accusations

Process:

  1. Challenge issued publicly
  2. Witnesses appointed
  3. Terms negotiated (first blood, yield, or death)
  4. Combat conducted fairly

Rules:

  • No magic beyond personal abilities
  • Equal weapons (usually)
  • Seconds stand by to intervene
  • Community enforces outcome
Cultural Note:

Duels are rare but respected. Refusing valid challenge damages reputation.

Solaris Duels

When Used: Artistic disputes, honor challenges, political positioning

Process:

  1. Dramatic public challenge
  2. Choice of duel type (combat, artistic, debate)
  3. Elaborate preparation
  4. Public spectacle

Types:

  • Blade duels: First blood usually
  • Bardic duels: Performance competition
  • Wit duels: Verbal sparring with judges
Cultural Note:

More theater than combat. Style matters as much as outcome.

Stonebound Duels

When Used: Craft disputes, serious honor violations

Process:

  1. Challenge before clan
  2. Terms carved in stone
  3. Chosen representatives (if needed)
  4. Combat with traditional weapons

Rules:

  • Ancient laws govern
  • Death is rare (first yield acceptable)
  • Clan enforces outcome
  • Result carved in stone permanently
Cultural Note:

Extremely serious. Stone remembers.

Emberlands Duels

When Used: Common for most disputes

Process:

  1. Challenge issued (often immediate)
  2. Brief terms stated
  3. Combat begins quickly
  4. Community watches

Rules:

  • Few restrictions
  • Until yield or unconsciousness
  • Death is risk but not goal
  • Winner’s position vindicated

Cultural Note: Frequent. Strength proves rightness.

CONFLICT RESOLUTION CUSTOMS

 

 

Mediation and Arbitration

When Mediation Is Preferred

Instead of Violence:

  • Trade disputes
  • Property boundaries
  • Contract disagreements
  • Community tensions

Who Mediates:

  • Northreach: Respected elders, guild officials
  • Solaris: Appointed arbitrators, faction representatives
  • Nullwood: Memory Keepers, Silent Regents
  • Stonebound: Clan elders, master craftspeople
  • Vharoxis: Syndicate representatives (for members)
  • Verdant Marches: Druids, circle elders

Mediation Process

Common Elements:

  1. Both parties agree to mediate
  2. Neutral third party selected
  3. Each side presents case
  4. Mediator proposes solution
  5. Parties accept or escalate

Binding Force:

  • Reputation pressure (most places)
  • Legal enforcement (cities)
  • Cultural obligation (Stonebound, Nullwood)
  • Practical necessity (Northreach)

Honor Satisfaction

What Satisfies Honor

Northreach:

  • Public apology
  • Making restitution
  • Performing service
  • Accepting punishment
  • (Rarely) Duel

Solaris:

  • Public performance of apology
  • Artistic tribute
  • Public recognition of wrong
  • Elaborate compensation
  • (Sometimes) Duel

Nullwood:

  • Private acknowledgment
  • Memory ceremony (acknowledging fault)
  • Restoration of balance
  • Time and demonstrated change
  • (Rarely) Exile

Stonebound:

  • Formal apology before clan
  • Craft-work restitution
  • Stone-carved acknowledgment
  • Blood price (serious offenses)
  • (Sometimes) Duel

Vharoxis:

  • Payment or service
  • Favor owed
  • Information traded
  • (Often) Nothing—revenge instead
  • Business solutions

Emberlands:

  • Trial by combat
  • Shared ordeal (proving strength together)
  • Fire ceremony
  • (Usually) Duel

CONFLICT RESOLUTION CUSTOMS

 

 

Blood Price and Compensation

When Blood Price Applies

Serious Crimes:

  • Murder
  • Severe injury
  • Breaking sacred oaths
  • Destroying livelihoods

How It Works

Northreach:

  • Victim’s family sets reasonable price
  • Community validates fairness
  • Exile if unpaid
  • Payment expected within year

Stonebound:

  • Clan council determines price
  • Often requires both coin and service
  • Price carved in stone
  • Unpaid debt follows generations

Emberlands:

  • Combat or compensation
  • Trial determines appropriate response
  • Honor satisfied through strength or payment

Verdant Marches:

  • Druids mediate
  • Restoration required
  • Service to community
  • Natural restitution preferred

Modern Complications

In cities with formal legal systems, blood price conflicts with state law. Traditional communities still honor it; cosmopolitan areas consider it barbaric.

CONFLICT RESOLUTION CUSTOMS

 

 

Practical Gameplay Impact

When Language Barriers Matter

Common Scenarios

Overhearing Conversations

  • Scenario: Nullwood scouts are discussing something in Elvish. Do you understand?
  • Speak Elvish: You understand; gain information advantage
  • Don’t Speak Elvish: DM gives you basic tone/emotion, but not content
  • Possible Solution: Comprehend Languages spell, another PC translates, context clues

Reading Ancient Inscriptions

  • Scenario: You find runes carved into stone in the Stonebound Depths.
  • Read Dwarvish: Instant understanding; possible advantage on related checks
  • Don’t Read Dwarvish: Must find translator or use magic
  • Partial Solution: History check might give general context; other PCs might help

Negotiating with Non-Common Speakers

  • Scenario: You meet a giant who only speaks Giant.
  • Speak Giant: Normal social interaction; Charisma checks as usual
  • Don’t Speak Giant: Communication via gestures; disadvantage on Charisma checks, or impossible without magic
  • Solutions: Tongues spell, translator NPC, creative pantomime

DM Guidance for Language Barriers

Make It Meaningful:

  • Don’t use language barriers to frustrate; use them to create opportunities
  • Reward players who chose useful languages
  • Provide workarounds (NPCs who translate, magic items, spells)

Balance:

  • Language barriers shouldn’t block critical plot progress
  • They should create interesting challenges and choices
  • Social encounters can become skill challenges or puzzles

Cultural Knowledge Affects Checks

Advantage from Respect

Examples:

Negotiating with Dwarf Merchant
  • Action: You compliment the craftsmanship of their wares (specific details) and speak a few words of Dwarvish
  • DM Ruling: Advantage on Persuasion check
  • Reason: You’ve shown respect for their culture and craft
Seeking Help in Nullwood
  • Action: You speak quietly, show patience, and don’t rush the conversation
  • DM Ruling: Lower DC for social checks or advantage
  • Reason: You’ve demonstrated understanding of their values
Asking Favors in Northreach
  • Action: You offer to help with chores first, demonstrating practical competence
  • DM Ruling: Advantage on Persuasion, or NPC simply agrees
  • Reason: You’ve proven you’re not just a “taker”

Disadvantage from Mistakes

Examples:

Insulting Stonebound Craft
  • Action: “This sword is good enough, I guess”
  • DM Ruling: Disadvantage on all Charisma checks with this dwarf
  • Reason: Grave insult to their craftsmanship
Being Loud in Nullwood
  • Action: Shouting, laughing loudly, making unnecessary noise
  • DM Ruling: Disadvantage on social interactions; NPCs may refuse to engage
  • Reason: Cultural violation of core value
Refusing Hospitality
  • Action: Declining offered food/shelter without good reason
  • DM Ruling: Disadvantage on Persuasion; NPC becomes suspicious
  • Reason: Insult to host; suggests distrust

PRACTICAL GAMEPLAY IMPACT

 

 

DM Tools for Cultural Checks

Intelligence (History):

  • Recall cultural customs: DC 10-15
  • Remember specific taboos: DC 15-20
  • Understand obscure traditions: DC 20+

Wisdom (Insight):

  • Read social cues: DC 12-18
  • Detect cultural mistake: DC 15
  • Understand unspoken rules: DC 18+

Charisma (Performance):

  • Adapt to cultural expectations: DC 13-18
  • Convincingly follow unfamiliar customs: DC 15-20

Regional Reputation and Prejudices

Stereotypes (Often Wrong)

How Northreachers Are Seen:

  • Solaris: Uncultured barbarians, practical but boring
  • Nullwood: Too loud, too impulsive, interesting but exhausting
  • Stonebound: Capable but unrefined
  • Vharoxis: Easy marks, too trusting

How Solarians Are Seen:

  • Northreach: Pretentious, useless in crisis, “all talk”
  • Nullwood: Too loud, too performative
  • Stonebound: Shallow, lacking substance
  • Vharoxis: Perfect targets (wealth + naivety)

How Nullwood Elves Are Seen:

  • Northreach: Mysterious, helpful but strange
  • Solaris: Exotic, fascinating, sources of ancient knowledge
  • Stonebound: Too quiet, too slow to decide
  • Vharoxis: Rich with secrets (valuable targets)

How Stonebound Dwarves Are Seen:

  • Northreach: Skilled, reliable, respected
  • Solaris: Stubborn, inflexible, but masterful
  • Nullwood: Too loud, but patient in their way
  • Vharoxis: Wealthy, bound by honor (exploitable)

How Vharoxans Are Seen:

  • Everyone: Untrustworthy, dangerous, criminals
  • Reality: Varies wildly; not everyone there is evil

Overcoming Prejudice

Roleplay Opportunities:

  • Prove stereotypes wrong through actions
  • Use prejudice to your advantage (lower expectations)
  • Call out unfair assumptions
  • Find allies who see past origin

Mechanical Impact:

  • Initial Charisma checks might have higher DC
  • Proving yourself grants reputation bonuses
  • Some NPCs refuse service based on origin
  • Others offer special opportunities

Using Culture for Roleplay Advantages

Playing to Cultural Strengths

The Solaris Bard

  • Situation: Gathering information in a tavern
  • Cultural Advantage: Solarians are expected to tell stories and perform
  • Action: Offer to perform in exchange for information
  • Result: Natural fit; NPCs open up, DM rewards creativity

The Stonebound Cleric

  • Situation: Need to convince merchant to extend credit
  • Cultural Advantage: Dwarven oaths are taken seriously
  • Action: Swear formal stone-oath to repay
  • Result: Merchant trusts oath; DM might not require Persuasion check

The Northreach Ranger

  • Situation: Frontier village facing wolf attacks
  • Cultural Advantage: Northreach natives understand wolves
  • Action: Share practical knowledge, offer to track
  • Result: Village trusts your expertise; immediate acceptance

PRACTICAL GAMEPLAY IMPACT

 

 

Creating Cultural Hooks

Backstory Integration:

  • Your Solaris bard is seeking rumors of Eclipse Day
  • Your dwarf is tracking stolen clan heirloom
  • Your elf is studying memory-magic anomalies
  • Your Northreach native is defending home

Cultural Motivations:

  • Solaris: Seeking truth/stories, advancing faction goals
  • Nullwood: Investigating ancient sites (cautiously), preserving memory
  • Stonebound: Pursuing quality craft, honoring clan
  • Northreach: Protecting community, surviving together
  • Emberlands: Proving strength, embracing challenges
  • Verdant Marches: Preserving nature, investigating Green Stirring

Common Social Skill Challenges

Persuasion Examples

  • DC 10 (Easy): Convince Northreach villager to share local rumors (you’re polite and respectful)
  • DC 15 (Moderate): Persuade Solaris merchant to lower prices (requires cultural knowledge or good argument)
  • DC 20 (Hard): Convince Stonebound clan to break tradition (nearly impossible without compelling reason)
  • DC 25 (Very Hard): Persuade Vharoxan syndicate to trust you (requires leverage, information, or reputation)

Deception Examples

  • DC 12 (Easy): Lie about minor details in Vharoxis (everyone lies there)

  • DC 15 (Moderate): Conceal your true purpose in Northreach (they’re wary but not paranoid)

  • DC 20 (Hard): Deceive Nullwood Memory Keeper (they sense emotional truth)

  • DC 25 (Very Hard): Trick Stonebound dwarf into breaking oath (honor runs deep)

Intimidation Examples

  • DC 12 (Easy): Intimidate Vharoxis street thug (shows of force work)
  • DC 15 (Moderate): Intimidate Emberlands warrior (they respect strength but aren’t easily cowed)
  • DC 20 (Hard): Intimidate Northreach veteran (frontier folk are tough)
  • DC 25 (Very Hard): Intimidate Stonebound clan elder (stone doesn’t fear)

Cultural Do’s and Don’ts by Region

Region DO DON’T
Northreach Be practical, keep promises, help in emergencies Waste resources, break oaths, be pretentious
Solaris Appreciate art, use titles, tell stories Be crude, ignore performances, dismiss culture
Nullwood Speak quietly, be patient, respect memory Be loud, rush, show excessive emotion
Stonebound Admire craft, keep oaths, offer hospitality Insult quality, break promises, waste
Vharoxis Use aliases, verify everything, respect power Use real names, trust freely, break Market rules
Shattered Coast Respect sea, help sailors, mind business Whistle on ships, steal salvage, abandon crew
Emberlands Show strength, share resources, be direct Show weakness, hoard, refuse challenges
Verdant Marches Respect nature, share food, consult druids Waste meat, damage land, ignore warnings

PRACTICAL GAMEPLAY IMPACT

 

 

Formal Greetings in Different Languages

Common Phrases to Know

Common (Universal):

  • Greeting: “Well met” / “Good day”
  • Farewell: “Safe travels” / “Fare you well”
  • Thanks: “I’m grateful” / “Much obliged”

Dwarvish (Stonebound):

  • Greeting: “Tharum-kal” (Stone endures)
  • Farewell: “Dûm-marak” (May the mountain hold you)
  • Thanks: “Khaz-dun” (Honored)

Elvish (Nullwood):

  • Greeting: “Sîla en ómënte” (Peace in memory)
  • Farewell: “Alae en tempte” (Until the silence calls again)
  • Thanks: “Hantalë” (With gratitude)

Giant (Far North):

  • Greeting: “Hraak!” (Stand strong!)
  • Farewell: “Grum-skal” (Ice holds)
  • Thanks: “Drak” (Respect)

Draconic (Vharoxis/Academic):

  • Greeting: “Thrae-vor” (I acknowledge your power)
  • Farewell: “Vur-shakal” (Until the flames meet again)
  • Thanks: “Vor-darastrix” (Honor to the mighty)

Orc (Emberlands/Tribal):

  • Greeting: “Ghar-uk!” (Blood and honor!)
  • Farewell: “Krag-morok” (Fight well)
  • Thanks: “Thraka” (Strength recognized)

Sylvan (Verdant Marches):

  • Greeting: “Lathil en’tempre” (Leaf and branch)
  • Farewell: “Aman en’sulta” (Walk with the green)
  • Thanks: “Sulta’mae” (The land remembers)

Final Thoughts

Culture and language are tools for immersion and storytelling. They shouldn’t be obstacles that prevent fun—they should be opportunities that create depth. Use this guide to enhance your character’s personality, navigate social situations, and engage with the rich diversity of Aevoria.

Remember: Your character’s background shapes how they see the world, but it doesn’t limit who they can become. A Northreach frontier scout can learn Solaris’ artistic traditions. A Solaris bard can earn respect in the Emberlands through strength. Cultural origin is where you start, not where you must end.

Welcome to Aevoria. May your words be well-chosen and your customs respected.

Using This Guide at the Table

For Players

During Character Creation:

  1. Choose languages that fit your backstory
  2. Consider campaign setting (Northreach frontier)
  3. Coordinate with party (cover multiple languages)
  4. Think about what your choices say about your character

During Play:

  1. Note when NPCs speak other languages
  2. Use cultural knowledge for roleplay advantages
  3. Respect cultural customs in-character
  4. Ask DM about cultural context when uncertain

Cultural Roleplay:

  1. Incorporate region-appropriate greetings
  2. React to customs appropriately
  3. Show respect (or deliberate disrespect) for traditions
  4. Use culture to define your character’s worldview

For DMs

Rewarding Language Choices:

  • Give meaningful opportunities to use each language
  • Provide clues in multiple languages (choice matters)
  • NPCs appreciate being addressed in native tongues
  • Language skill can replace or augment social checks

Using Culture in Play:

  • Describe regional customs as part of setting
  • Let cultural knowledge provide mechanical benefits
  • Make cultural fumbles have consequences (not fatal, but awkward)
  • Use stereotypes as starting points, not absolute truths

When to Hand-Wave:

  • Don’t let language barriers halt story progression
  • Provide NPC translators when needed
  • Assume Common is understood in most settlements
  • Focus on cultural interesting-ness, not frustration

FINAL THOUGHTS

 

 

Northreach: Your Starting Point

Northreach: Your Frontier Home

NORTHREACH: YOUR FRONTIER HOME

 

 

Northreach in One Paragraph

Northreach is a cold, sparsely settled frontier where survival depends on community, preparation, and the protection provided by organizations like the Northwatch Wardens. Waystone Inn sits at the practical center of travel and trade—a safe hearth between small settlements, logging roads, and old ruins. Most people here concern themselves with local problems: wolves, bandits, missing hunters, and weather. But recently, strange reports have been filtering in from across the region, making even seasoned frontiersmen uneasy.

Common Knowledge

Everyone in Northreach knows these facts. Your character would be familiar with all of this information.

Geography and Settlement

The Hub-and-Spokes: Northreach is organized around Waystone Inn, with small settlements scattered like spokes on a wheel:

  • Waystone Inn (center) — Northwatch Warden headquarters; neutral ground; safest place between settlements
  • Welton (southwest) — Farming village of ~200 people; governed by elected council
  • Pinebrook (southeast) — Trading post and lumber camp; smaller than Welton
  • Palebank Village (northeast coast) — Fishing settlement; gateway to the Far North
  • Noke’s Tower (west of Waystone) — Wizard’s tower; local eccentric
  • Temple of the Dragonknights (northwest mountains) — Monastery; keeps to itself

Travel Times from Waystone Inn:

  • Welton: 1–2 days on foot
  • Pinebrook: 2–3 days on foot
  • Noke’s Tower: Half-day to 1 day (easy trek)
  • Palebank Village: 3–5 days (weather dependent)
  • Temple of the Dragonknights: 4–6 days (mountain roads)

Climate and Seasons

Winter Dominates: Northreach has three seasons:

  • Long Winter (8 months): Snow, ice, temperatures well below freezing. Travel is dangerous without preparation.
  • Mud Season (2 months): Spring thaw turns roads to muck. Almost worse than winter for travel.
  • Short Summer (2 months): Brief warm period. Everyone rushes to complete outdoor work before winter returns.

Survival Basics:

  • Always carry cold-weather gear outside settlements
  • Never travel alone in winter
  • Stock supplies before winter; resupply may be impossible for months
  • Learn to read weather signs or hire someone who can

NORTHREACH: YOUR FRONTIER HOME

 

 

The Northwatch Wardens

The Wardens are Northreach’s frontier protection guild, operating from Waystone Inn. When communities face threats beyond their capability—awakened wolves, bandits, strange magical events—they post contracts for the Wardens to handle.

Leadership: Marshal Brenna Thorne (field operations), Steward Mara Fenwick (logistics and supplies), Lorewarden Elric Vael (research and arcane threats).

→ For the complete charter, guild code, roster, and membership details, see Chapter 4: The Northwatch Wardens.

Money and Trade

Currency:

  • Coins are accepted but relatively rare on the frontier
  • Most transactions involve barter: labor, goods, future favors
  • A day’s skilled work = 2 gp equivalent in value
  • A day’s heavy labor = 5 sp equivalent in value

What’s Available:

  • Basic supplies (food, rope, common tools): readily available
  • Quality weapons and armor: rare; usually imported or custom-made
  • Spell components: very limited selection; exotic components require trips to cities
  • Healing potions and magic items: extremely rare; often family heirlooms

Where to Shop:

  • Waystone Inn: basic adventuring supplies, some weapons/armor
  • Welton: food, farming tools, basic goods
  • Pinebrook: lumber, trapping supplies, furs
  • Palebank: fishing gear, cold-weather equipment, seal-oil lamps

NORTHREACH: YOUR FRONTIER HOME

 

 

Magic and the Strange

Low-Magic Society:

Most people in Northreach go their entire lives without seeing magic. When it does appear, reactions vary:

  • Clerics and paladins — Generally trusted; divine magic is seen as gods’ will
  • Wizards and sorcerers — Viewed with caution; arcane magic is powerful but unpredictable
  • Warlocks — Distrusted; pact magic implies dangerous bargains
  • Druids and rangers — Respected; nature magic is understood as part of the land
  • Bards — Welcome; entertainment is rare and valued

Rules of Frontier Magic:

  1. Don’t cast flashy spells in settlements without warning people first
  2. Don’t use magic to cheat, steal, or intimidate
  3. If your magic hurts someone or breaks something, you pay restitution
  4. If locals ask you not to cast magic in their home/shop, respect it

Recent Strangeness:

Over the past few months, people across Northreach have reported unusual events:

  • Animals behaving with uncanny awareness or coordination
  • Objects moving on their own or responding to emotions
  • Dreams shared among entire villages
  • Colors, sounds, or sensations that “shouldn’t exist”
  • Plants growing in impossible patterns or seasons

No one knows what’s causing it. The Northwatch Wardens are investigating.

What You’ve Heard

Rumors, gossip, and stories circulating around Northreach. Your character might have heard some or all of these. They may or may not be true.

About Settlements

Welton:

  • “The village council is arguing again about whether to hire more guards or trust the Wardens.”
  • “Westly the shepherd lost half his flock to wolves last month. He swears the wolves opened the gate themselves.”
  • “Someone—or something—has been leaving strange symbols carved into trees around Westly’s Farm.”
  • “The Shepherd’s Crook Inn serves the best mutton stew in Northreach. Arrive early or it sells out.”

Pinebrook:

  • “Lumber crews are refusing to work certain sections of forest. They say the trees whisper to each other.”
  • “The trading post had a break-in, but nothing was stolen. Just… rearranged. Like someone was searching for something specific.”
  • “There’s good money in logging, but the work destroys your back and the pay barely covers winter supplies.”

Palebank:

  • “Fishermen pulled up something from the deep last week. Metal, covered in ice, with strange markings. They threw it back.”
  • “People are going missing in the far north. Search parties find tracks that just… end. No struggle, no body, nothing.”
  • “The village elder has been acting strange since the summer—staring north for hours, muttering about ‘something waking up.’”

NORTHREACH: YOUR FRONTIER HOME

 

 

About Notable Figures

Marshal Brenna Thorne (Northwatch Wardens):

  • “She’s former military—maybe imperial, maybe something else. She doesn’t talk about it.”
  • “Fair but tough. She’ll give you a chance, but only one. Screw up and you’re out.”
  • “I heard she turned down a command position in Solaris to stay on the frontier. Wonder why?”

Steward Mara Fenwick (Northwatch Wardens):

  • “She knows the value of everything within a copper piece. Can’t cheat her.”
  • “Surprisingly good fighter for a quartermaster. Don’t let the ledgers fool you.”
  • “She’s been at Waystone longer than anyone. If you want to know frontier history, ask Mara.”

Lorewarden Elric Vael (Northwatch Wardens):

  • “He spends more time in his library than with people. Bit odd, but brilliant.”
  • “I heard he used to teach at a magical college down south before coming here. No one knows why he left.”
  • “If it’s weird, magical, or ancient, Elric probably has a book about it. Or he’ll write one.”

Noke the Finicky (Wizard, Noke’s Tower):

  • “Eccentric doesn’t begin to describe him. Last month he tried to polymorph himself into a sheep to ‘understand their perspective.’ It went badly.”
  • “Don’t accept random magical items from him. Half of them are cursed or backfire spectacularly.”
  • “Despite everything, he’s actually quite skilled. Just… unpredictable.”

About Dangers

Wolves:

  • “They’re not acting like normal wolves. Too smart. Too organized.”
  • “Some say a sorcerer is controlling them. Others claim they’re awakening on their own.”
  • “Whatever the cause, they’re more dangerous than usual. Don’t travel alone.”

Bandits:

  • “There’s a group operating out of Croaker Cave, north of Palebank. They hit supply wagons.”
  • “Most bandits are just desperate people trying to survive. Some are worse.”

The Wild Places:

  • “The old ruins scattered across Northreach? They’re waking up. Lights in windows that haven’t had glass in centuries.”
  • “Rangers say the forests feel… aware. Like they’re being watched by something old and patient.”
  • “There are caves in the northern mountains that no one explores twice. The first group comes back shaken. The second doesn’t come back at all.”

NORTHREACH: YOUR FRONTIER HOME

 

 

Practical Information for Adventurers

Where to Find Work

Waystone Inn (Northwatch Wardens):

  • Primary job board for adventuring work
  • Contracts range from escort duty to monster hunting to investigation
  • Payment negotiated per contract
  • Guild takes 10% to maintain headquarters and supplies

Local Communities:

  • Direct hire: Villages sometimes hire adventurers directly for specific tasks
  • Trade: Work for supplies, lodging, or crafted goods instead of coin
  • Favors: Building reputation may be more valuable than immediate payment

Ongoing Opportunities:

  • Escort duty: Caravans and travelers need protection between settlements
  • Scouting: Settlements pay for information about nearby threats
  • Resource gathering: Rare herbs, monster parts, or salvage from ruins
  • Construction/labor: Off-season work when contracts are scarce

Supplies and Services

Waystone Inn:

  • Basic weapons and armor: shortswords, spears, leather armor, shields
  • Adventuring gear: rope, torches, rations, basic tools
  • Healing supplies: bandages, healer’s kits (no potions)
  • Lodging: 5 sp/night (includes meals)
  • Stabling: 5 cp/night per mount

Welton (Shepherd’s Crook Inn):

  • Food supplies: jerky, cheese, bread, ale
  • Farming tools and supplies
  • Warm clothing (wool, fur-lined cloaks)
  • Lodging: 2 sp/night (meals extra)

Palebank Village:

  • Cold-weather gear: fur coats, seal-skin boots, oil lamps
  • Fishing supplies and preserved fish
  • Limited basic goods (expensive due to isolation)
  • Lodging: 3 sp/night (limited availability)

Pinebrook:

  • Lumber and woodworking
  • Trapping and hunting supplies
  • Furs and hides
  • Lodging: Very limited (most workers camp)

NORTHREACH: YOUR FRONTIER HOME

 

 

Local Customs and Etiquette

Frontier Hospitality:

  • Offering food and shelter to travelers is expected
  • Refusing hospitality without good reason is an insult
  • Guests are expected to contribute (chores, stories, information, small payment)
  • Overstaying your welcome: 2-3 nights is standard; longer requires explicit invitation

Survival Culture:

  • Wasting resources (food, firewood, supplies) is considered shameful
  • Hoarding during hard times while others starve is remembered forever
  • “Winter debt”: owing someone aid you can’t repay until spring is acceptable; refusing to help because they can’t pay immediately is not

Social Hierarchy:

  • Frontier culture is relatively egalitarian
  • Respect is earned through competence and reliability, not birth or title
  • Elders and those with specialized knowledge (healers, trackers, etc.) are valued
  • Empty boasts or exaggerated credentials are quickly exposed and mocked

Magic:

  • In settlements, ask before casting
  • Demonstrating useful magic (light, mending, etc.) builds goodwill
  • Using magic to intimidate or show off creates distrust
  • If your magic causes problems, you fix it—no excuses

The Wardens:

  • “Guild business is guild business”—don’t ask Wardens to discuss active contracts
  • Wardens are expected to be neutral in local disputes unless hired
  • Offering to buy a Warden a drink is standard friendliness
  • Trying to bribe a Warden on contract is a good way to make enemies

Seasonal Considerations

Winter (Most of the Year):

  • Plan for being snowed in; always have 2 weeks of supplies
  • Cold damage is a real threat—track exposure carefully
  • Travel may be impossible during storms (1d4 days)
  • Some contracts can’t be completed until spring—communicate honestly with clients

Mud Season:

  • Roads become impassable bogs
  • Travel takes 50% longer
  • Wheel-based vehicles are useless; use sleds or pack animals
  • Disease spreads more easily—freshwater and hygiene are priorities

Summer:

  • Everyone works frantically to prepare for winter
  • Harvest-time work is plentiful but exhausting
  • Best time for long-distance travel or ruin exploration
  • Prices for preserved goods rise as winter approaches

NORTHREACH: YOUR FRONTIER HOME

 

 

Important NPCs and Their Public Roles

Waystone Inn Leadership

Marshal Brenna Thorne:

  • Role: Northwatch Wardens field commander
  • Public Persona: Professional, tough, fair
  • What She Does: Assigns contracts, coordinates Warden operations, makes tactical decisions
  • How to Impress Her: Competence, honesty, results

Steward Mara Fenwick:

  • Role: Quartermaster and logistics coordinator
  • Public Persona: Sharp, organized, no-nonsense
  • What She Does: Manages supplies, tracks finances, maintains equipment
  • How to Impress Her: Efficiency, keeping your word, returning equipment in good condition

Lorewarden Elric Vael:

  • Role: Scholar and arcane consultant
  • Public Persona: Bookish, curious, slightly awkward socially
  • What He Does: Researches threats, identifies magical items, maintains records
  • How to Impress Him: Bringing interesting information, asking intelligent questions, protecting books

Welton Notables

Westly:

  • Role: Shepherd and frequent Warden client
  • Public Persona: Hardworking, practical, concerned father
  • Current Situation: Lost livestock to wolves; believes something unnatural is happening

Tillus Merrion:

  • Role: Welton council member
  • Public Persona: Traditional, cautious, protective of village
  • Stance: Skeptical of outside help but will hire Wardens when necessary

Leanor Slatebeard:

  • Role: Tracker and occasional Warden contractor
  • Public Persona: Competent, quiet, observant
  • Value: Can guide expeditions or provide wilderness information

Palebank Notables

Pelc Throstmein:

  • Role: General store owner
  • Public Persona: Friendly merchant; gossip hub
  • Value: Source of information about village and northern activity

Tulgi Lutan:

  • Role: Village healer
  • Public Persona: Knowledgeable, practical, motherly
  • Value: Medical services and local lore

Urgon Wenth:

  • Role: Blacksmith
  • Public Persona: Gruff but skilled craftsman
  • Value: Weapon/armor repairs; limited custom work

Elro Aldataur:

  • Role: Retired scholar
  • Public Persona: Eccentric, obsessed with ancient history
  • Value: Knowledge about ruins and pre-Calamity civilizations

NORTHREACH: YOUR FRONTIER HOME

 

 

The Mysteries of Northreach

Your character might wonder about these things. Investigating them could lead to adventures.

The Recent Strangeness

Something is changing in Northreach. The signs are subtle but accumulating:

  • Wildlife Behavior: Animals coordinating in ways that seem impossible. Pack hunters developing strategies that shouldn’t occur naturally.
  • Ruins Activating: Ancient structures showing signs of life—lights, sounds, warmth—after centuries of dormancy.
  • Shared Experiences: Multiple people reporting identical dreams or sensations with no obvious connection.
  • Objects Awakening: Tools, weapons, or other items responding to emotions or intentions.

Questions No One Can Answer:

  • Is this happening elsewhere, or just in Northreach?
  • Is it connected to the ruins scattered across the region?
  • Why now, after so long?
  • Is it dangerous, or just strange?

The Northwatch Wardens are actively investigating, but they’re being careful not to cause panic. Most locals dismiss individual incidents as coincidence or exaggeration. Those who’ve seen multiple events know better.

The Far North

North of Palebank, the frozen wastes stretch toward the top of the world. Buried beneath the ice are ruins—towers of metal, chambers sealed for millennia, artifacts of a civilization lost to time.

Most people avoid the ruins. Those who explore them report:

  • Strange technology that doesn’t run on magic
  • Sealed vaults that resist all attempts to open them
  • A pervasive sense of unease, like being watched
  • Occasionally: treasures, knowledge, or items of power

Lately, the rumors have grown darker:

  • Ice melting around certain ruins, exposing entrances
  • Lights moving beneath frozen surfaces
  • People venturing north and not returning

The Question: Is the strangeness in Northreach somehow connected to whatever lies beneath the northern ice?

For Curious Minds

The world is larger and stranger than these few pages can capture. Northreach is your starting point, but it’s not your boundary. As you gain experience and reputation, contracts may take you far from the Waystone Inn—to southern cities, ancient forests, or deeper mysteries than you can currently imagine.

The frontier rewards the bold, the clever, and the prepared. But it punishes the reckless.

Stay sharp. Trust your companions. Question everything.

— Marshal Brenna Thorne, Northwatch Wardens

NORTHREACH: YOUR FRONTIER HOME

 

 

Places of Northreach

Overview

Northreach reveals itself mile by mile: wind-combed forests, narrow roads that widen and contract like breathing, and settlements that feel earned against the cold expanse. This is a region where distance matters, where the space between warm lights can swallow the unwary, and where every community represents a deliberate choice to endure.

The Waystone Inn (Central Northreach)

What It Is

The Waystone Inn serves as both a traveler’s rest and the headquarters of the Northwatch Wardens. Built around an ancient standing stone (the “waystone” that gives the place its name), the inn occupies a strategic crossroads where several major routes converge.

Geography

  • Location: Center of the region, roughly equidistant from Welton, Pinebrook, and Palebank
  • Terrain: Rolling hills with scattered pine forests
  • Roads: Three main roads converge here—west to Welton, southeast to Pinebrook, northeast to Palebank

The Building

The inn is a sprawling structure that’s grown organically over decades:

  • Main Hall: Two-story structure with a common room, kitchen, and guest quarters
  • Warden’s Wing: Added fifteen years ago, includes meeting rooms, armory, and private quarters
  • Stables: Large enough for two dozen horses and several wagons
  • The Waystone: A weathered standing stone in the courtyard, covered in ancient carvings nobody can fully read

Atmosphere

The inn maintains a careful balance:

  • Warm and welcoming to travelers seeking rest
  • Professionally neutral ground for those seeking help
  • Quietly watchful of those who bring trouble

Notable Features

  • The Contract Board: Posted contracts available for wardens to accept
  • The Common Room: Where news, rumors, and stories circulate
  • The Library: Small but growing collection of maps, reports, and historical documents
  • The Armory: Well-stocked with practical gear
  • The Waystone Itself: Some claim it hums during storms; others say it’s just wind

Services Available

  • Meals (hearty frontier cooking)
  • Lodging (clean beds, reasonable rates)
  • Stabling and wagon storage
  • Maps and route information
  • Contract postings
  • Equipment requisition (for wardens)
  • Message relay to other settlements

Local Knowledge

  • “The waystone was here before anyone. The inn grew up around it.”
  • “If you need help and can’t get it anywhere else, go to the Waystone.”
  • “Neutral ground—start trouble there, and you’ll answer to the Marshal.”
  • “They say the stone marks an old battleground, but who fought and why is long forgotten.”

Welton (Southwest)

What It Is

A farming and herding village built on good soil and stubborn determination. Welton supplies grain and livestock to other settlements and serves as a model of frontier community cooperation.

Geography

  • Location: Southwest of the Waystone Inn, about a day’s travel
  • Terrain: Fertile valley with gentle hills, bordered by forests to the north and west
  • Climate: Cold winters, short growing seasons, reliable rainfall

PLACES OF NORTHREACH

 

 

The Settlement

Welton is organized around its main square:

  • Village Square: Market area and community gathering space
  • Council Hall: Where village decisions are made
  • Shepherd’s Crook Inn: Social heart of the village
  • Farms: Spread in a rough circle around the village center
  • Grazing Lands: Communal pastures to the south

Economy

  • Grain farming (wheat, barley, oats)
  • Sheep and goat herding
  • Limited vegetable gardens (short season)
  • Wool production
  • Seasonal trading with other settlements

Population

About 120 permanent residents:

  • Primarily human farmers
  • Some dwarf stoneworkers
  • Handful of halfling traders
  • A few elf families (newer arrivals)

Governance

Village council of five elected members who rotate leadership:

  • Represent farming, herding, trade, crafts, and general community interests
  • Decisions made by consensus when possible
  • Serious disputes arbitrated by the full community

Notable Locations Within Welton

The Shepherd’s Crook Inn

  • Proprietor: Darvin Crook (human, third generation)
  • Atmosphere: Warm, loud, and welcoming
  • Specialty: Mutton stew and locally brewed ale
  • Function: Where everyone goes to hear news and gossip

Village Square

  • Market Days: Every ten days, weather permitting
  • Features: Community well, message board, stocks (rarely used)
  • Gatherings: Seasonal celebrations, town meetings, emergency assemblies

The Old Mill

  • Function: Grain processing for the community
  • Operator: Millwright Torrhen (dwarf, expert craftsman)
  • Note: The mill wheel can be heard throughout the village

Cultural Notes

  • Strong emphasis on communal work (barn-raisings, harvests, defense)
  • Superstitions about wolves (recent troubles have intensified this)
  • Seasonal festivals mark planting and harvest
  • Stories about “the old woods” passed down through generations

Current Situation

  • Recent wolf attacks have people on edge
  • Some livestock has been lost
  • Patrols have increased around outlying farms
  • Tensions between those who want to hunt the wolves and those who fear something worse

Local Knowledge

  • “Good bread, good people, but keep your animals penned.”
  • “Welton folks remember favors—and grudges.”
  • “Don’t mock their superstitions about the wolves. They’ve seen things.”
  • “The Shepherd’s Crook is where you hear the truth, if you buy enough rounds.”

Westly’s Farm (West of Welton)

What It Is

An outlying sheep farm that represents the isolated homesteads common on the frontier. Westly’s Farm sits at the edge of Welton’s protected area, closer to the wild forests than most residents prefer.

Geography

  • Location: About three miles west of Welton proper
  • Terrain: Rolling grassland transitioning to forest
  • Isolation: No other farms within an hour’s walk

The Farmstead

  • Main House: Single-story stone and timber construction
  • Sheep Pens: Sturdy wooden enclosures, recently reinforced
  • Barn: For hay storage and shelter during harsh weather
  • Well: Deep and reliable
  • Fields: Open grazing land bordered by forest

PLACES OF NORTHREACH

 

 

Daily Life

Westly manages the farm with occasional hired help during shearing season:

  • Tends a flock of about forty sheep
  • Raises a few goats
  • Maintains fences and buildings
  • Watches for predators

Why Farm Here?

  • Better grazing than closer to town
  • Privacy and independence
  • Good water source
  • Proximity to timber for repairs

The Risk

Outlying farms like Westly’s face constant challenges:

  • Predators (wolves, bears, occasional worse things)
  • Distance from help
  • Harsh weather with no nearby shelter
  • Isolation during emergencies

Recent Troubles

  • Multiple wolf attacks over recent weeks
  • Livestock losses
  • Strange behavior from the wolves (too organized, too persistent)
  • Growing fear that something is deliberately targeting the farm

Local Knowledge

  • “Westly’s a hard worker, but he farms hard land.”
  • “You couldn’t pay me enough to live that far from town.”
  • “Those wolves have been at his flock every few nights.”
  • “He’s too proud to ask for help, but he needs it.”

Pinebrook (Southeast)

What It Is

A trading village positioned at the intersection of several routes. Pinebrook serves as a commercial hub where goods from Northreach’s scattered communities are bought, sold, and redistributed.

Geography

  • Location: Southeast of the Waystone Inn, about a day and a half travel
  • Terrain: Forested region near a reliable river crossing
  • Trade Position: Routes from Waystone, Welton, Palebank, and southern settlements converge here

The Settlement

Pinebrook is built for commerce:

  • Market Square: Largest in the region, bustling with activity
  • Trading Post: Main commercial building with secure storage
  • The Pine Lodge: Inn catering to merchants and traders
  • Warehouses: Several secure buildings for stored goods
  • Workshops: Craftspeople who repair wagons and equipment

Economy

  • Trading hub for regional goods
  • Wagon repair and maintenance
  • Secure storage for traveling merchants
  • Money changing and basic banking services
  • Information brokerage (news and rumors)

Population

About 90 permanent residents, plus floating population of travelers:

  • Merchants and shopkeepers
  • Craftspeople (smiths, carpenters, leatherworkers)
  • Warehouse workers
  • Inn and tavern staff
  • A few retired traders

What Passes Through Pinebrook

  • Grain and wool from Welton
  • Fish and sealskins from Palebank
  • Timber from northern logging camps
  • Southern manufactured goods (tools, cloth, luxuries)
  • Artifacts and relics (quietly, through certain merchants)

Governance

  • Merchant’s Council of five trading families
  • Decisions prioritize commerce and safe passage
  • Disputes settled by arbitration (fees charged)
  • Maintains armed watch to protect trade goods

PLACES OF NORTHREACH

 

 

Notable Locations Within Pinebrook

The Pine Lodge

  • Proprietor: Merryn Pine (halfling, shrewd businesswoman)
  • Services: Lodging, meals, private meeting rooms
