ROSTER

 

 

The Triad: Guild Leadership

The Northwatch Wardens are overseen by three leaders, each responsible for a critical aspect of operations. Together, they form the Triad Council—requiring at least two signatures for major decisions, but empowered to act individually in emergencies.

Marshal Brenna Thorne

Role: Field Commander and Tactical Leader

Appearance: A weathered human woman in her early forties, with short-cropped dark hair streaked with gray. Her military bearing is unmistakable—she stands straight, moves with purpose, and her eyes constantly assess her surroundings. Scars mark her hands and forearms, evidence of years in combat. She typically wears practical leather armor reinforced with steel plates, and keeps her longsword within easy reach.

Personality: Fair but demanding. Marshal Thorne gives every Warden one chance to prove themselves—but only one. She values competence, honesty, and results above all else. Cross her once and you’re out; prove yourself and she’ll trust you with her life. She doesn’t waste words, but when she speaks, people listen.

Background: Former military from the south—possibly imperial forces, though she never discusses it. Fifteen years ago, she founded the Northwatch Wardens after turning down what was rumored to be a command position in Solaris. Whatever drove her to the frontier, she’s committed to staying.

What People Say:

  • “She’s seen things that haunt her. Makes her careful, sometimes too careful.”
  • “Fair but tough. She’ll give you a chance, but only one. Screw up and you’re out.”
  • “I heard she turned down a command position in Solaris to stay on the frontier. Wonder why?”

Working With Her: Marshal Thorne respects competence and honesty. If you take a contract, she expects you to complete it or die trying—and if you survive a failure, she expects an honest report of what went wrong. She doesn’t tolerate cowardice, but she understands tactical retreat. Show her you can handle yourself in a fight, think tactically, and put the mission above personal glory, and you’ll earn her respect.

Steward Mara Fenwick

Role: Quartermaster and Logistics Coordinator

Appearance: A sturdy dwarf woman in her sixties, with steel-gray hair worn in practical braids and keen eyes that miss nothing. Her hands are calloused from years of work, and she moves with the confident efficiency of someone who knows exactly where everything should be. She dresses practically—reinforced work clothes with multiple pockets and pouches, always carrying a ledger, measuring tools, and a well-maintained shortsword.

Personality: Sharp, organized, and no-nonsense. Mara knows the value of everything within a copper piece, and attempting to cheat her is a waste of time. She’s fair in her dealings but expects the same in return. Despite her focus on logistics, she’s a surprisingly capable fighter—quartermaster doesn’t mean defenseless.

Background: Mara has been at Waystone Inn longer than anyone else in the guild—she was running the inn’s stores before Marshal Thorne arrived. Her knowledge of frontier history, trade routes, and community relationships makes her invaluable. She joined the Wardens’ leadership when the guild was founded, providing the organizational backbone that keeps operations running smoothly.

What People Say:

  • “She knows the value of everything within a copper piece. Can’t cheat her.”
  • “Surprisingly good fighter for a quartermaster. Don’t let the ledgers fool you.”
  • “She’s been at Waystone longer than anyone. If you want to know frontier history, ask Mara.”

Working With Her: Mara appreciates efficiency, honesty, and respect for guild resources. Return equipment in good condition, keep accurate expense records, and don’t waste supplies. If you need something for a contract, make your case clearly and she’ll provision you fairly. Break or lose equipment without good reason, and expect to pay for replacement. Keep your word, and she’ll remember you as reliable—worth more than gold on the frontier.

Lorewarden Elric Vael

Role: Scholar and Arcane Consultant

Appearance: A half-elf man who appears to be in his forties (likely much older), with ash-blond hair tied back loosely and thoughtful gray eyes that often seem focused on something not quite present. He’s lean and slightly awkward in social situations, more comfortable with books than people. His robes are practical but well-maintained, marked with ink stains on the sleeves. He carries a weathered leather satchel filled with notebooks, reference materials, and writing supplies.

Personality: Bookish, curious, and genuinely passionate about understanding the world. Elric is more at home in his library than in conversation, but he’s eager to discuss topics that interest him—particularly anything weird, magical, or ancient. He’s patient with genuine questions but has little time for willful ignorance. Socially awkward but not unkind.

Background: Elric taught at a prestigious magical college in the south before coming to Northreach, though he never explains why he left. He joined the Wardens shortly after their founding, drawn by the opportunity to study frontier mysteries and ancient ruins. His expertise in arcane theory, ancient civilizations, and magical threats has proven invaluable to the guild’s investigations.

What People Say:

  • “He spends more time in his library than with people. Bit odd, but brilliant.”
  • “I heard he used to teach at a magical college down south before coming here. No one knows why he left.”
  • “If it’s weird, magical, or ancient, Elric probably has a book about it. Or he’ll write one.”

Working With Him: Elric appreciates curiosity, careful observation, and respect for knowledge. Bring him interesting information—particularly about magical phenomena, ancient ruins, or unusual creatures—and he’ll gladly share what he knows. Ask intelligent questions and he’ll teach willingly. Protect books and records, and he’ll consider you a kindred spirit. Most importantly: if you encounter something strange, document it carefully and report honestly. That information might save lives.

THE TRIAD: GUILD LEADERSHIP

 

 

Field Members

The Wardens maintain a roster of active field members, organized by specialization. Not all members are present at Waystone Inn at any given time—many are out on contracts, visiting family, or handling personal business. The following represents the core membership as of the current season.

Trailwardens (Scouts & Wilderness Specialists)

The Trailwardens handle wilderness scouting, tracking, and operations requiring deep knowledge of Northreach’s terrain. They’re the guild’s eyes in the wild.

Corel (halfling ranger)

  • Senior shepherd from Welton; expert tracker and wilderness guide
  • Knows every game trail and seasonal pattern in the region
  • Quiet and patient; preferred guide for long wilderness expeditions
  • Often contracts independently but maintains guild membership

Bordel Barleywind (human ranger)

  • Experienced tracker with specialized knowledge of predator behavior
  • Traumatized by a past encounter (doesn’t discuss details)
  • Reliable but cautious; sometimes too careful
  • Excellent at reading signs and predicting animal movement

Rowan Fairweather (half-elf druid)

  • Connected to natural cycles; senses disturbances in the land
  • Soft-spoken but confident in wilderness settings
  • Specializes in plant lore and natural healing
  • Often meditates alone; respects boundaries but friendly when approached

Mila Teno (elf ranger)

  • Young and enthusiastic; eager to prove herself
  • Skilled archer and competent tracker
  • Has an irrational fear of wolves after a childhood incident
  • Learning quickly but still building experience

Lantern Guard (Frontline Fighters)

The Lantern Guard forms the guild’s primary combat force, handling direct threats and providing security for dangerous contracts.

Takk (half-orc fighter)

  • Veteran warrior; straightforward and reliable
  • Specializes in defensive tactics and protecting others
  • Few words but absolute loyalty to companions
  • Preferred for contracts requiring a strong frontline presence

Galvena (human paladin)

  • Devoted to protecting the innocent; follows the Triad’s code
  • Inspires courage in others through word and deed
  • Can be rigid about principles but learns from experience
  • Healing abilities make her valuable for extended expeditions

Ariodh (elf fighter)

  • Graceful combatant with decades of battle experience
  • Tactical thinker; often coordinates group combat strategies
  • Patient teacher for less experienced members
  • Excellent at reading opponents and adjusting tactics

Guz (dwarf barbarian)

  • Raw power; devastating when unleashed
  • Surprisingly thoughtful outside combat
  • Values directness and honesty above all else
  • Best deployed against single powerful threats

Lorewatch (Knowledge Specialists)

The Lorewatch supports investigations requiring specialized knowledge, magical insight, or research capabilities.

Sera (human cleric)

  • Divine caster with focus on healing and protection
  • Serves Pelor; brings light to dark places (literally and metaphorically)
  • Compassionate but pragmatic about frontier realities
  • Often accompanies contracts involving disease or undead threats

Aurixean (dragonborn sorcerer)

  • Arcane specialist with dragon bloodline heritage
  • Proud but professional; values competence over flattery
  • Particularly effective against magical threats
  • Occasionally consults with Lorewarden Elric on arcane matters

Shinebright (gnome wizard)

  • Inventive problem-solver with broad magical knowledge
  • Enthusiastic about experimentation (sometimes too enthusiastic)
  • Creates custom solutions for unusual problems
  • Best suited for contracts requiring magical analysis or utility casting

Baleth (tiefling warlock)

  • Pact magic user; specific patron undisclosed
  • Professional and discreet about contract work
  • Specializes in information gathering and social manipulation
  • Some members distrust warlocks, but Baleth has proven reliable

Hearthwardens (Support & Community)

The Hearthwardens focus on community support, healing, diplomacy, and maintaining relationships with local settlements.

Father Merriksonn (human cleric)

  • Elderly cleric of Bahamut; spiritual advisor to many Wardens
  • Provides healing, counseling, and last rites
  • Gentle demeanor but unwavering principles
  • Rarely travels far from Waystone but his blessing is valued

Willen (halfling bard)

  • Storyteller and morale booster; keeps spirits high
  • Maintains relationships with settlements through performance
  • Excellent information gatherer through social connections
  • Often accompanies diplomatic or social contracts

Flynt (human artificer)

  • Equipment maintenance and magical item identification
  • Tinkers constantly; always improving guild gear
  • Practical inventor focusing on useful rather than flashy
  • Occasionally creates custom items for specific contracts

Joel (human ally)

  • Community liaison and local guide
  • Not a full Warden but trusted ally and friend to the guild
  • Provides information about local politics and settlement needs
  • Often helps negotiate contracts with outlying communities

Wild Allies

Bolt and Flame (awakened wolves)

  • Magically awakened companions to Rowan Fairweather
  • Intelligent and loyal; can be communicated with
  • Sometimes scout independently for the guild
  • Living examples of the strange occurrences affecting Northreach

Pack members (various)

  • Occasional animal companions brought by Warden members
  • Horses, dogs, and other trained creatures
  • Not formally part of the roster but recognized presences

FIELD MEMBERS

 

 

Guild Operations

The Contract System

How It Works:

  1. Posting: Clients post contracts on the Waystone Board, describing the problem and offering payment
  2. Review: Marshal Thorne reviews contracts for legitimacy and assigns difficulty ratings
  3. Acceptance: Wardens review available contracts and accept those matching their capabilities
  4. Advance Payment: 25% of the contract value is paid upfront for supplies and preparation
  5. Completion: Wardens complete the contract and provide a report to the Triad
  6. Final Payment: Remaining 75% is paid upon successful completion
  7. Guild Share: 10% of total payment goes to guild operations (already deducted from posted price)
  8. Distribution: Remainder is split among participating Wardens

Contract Example: Wolves of Welton

Posted Contract Value: 800 gp
Guild Operations Fund: 80 gp (10% - already deducted)
Available to Wardens: 720 gp
Advance Payment: 180 gp (25% of 720)
Payment on Completion: 540 gp (75% of 720)

If split 3 ways:
Each Warden receives 240 gp total (60 gp advance, 180 gp on completion)

Payment Variations:

Not all contracts pay in coin. Frontier communities often offer:

  • Trade goods: Preserved food, furs, lumber, or crafted items
  • Services: Lodging, meals, equipment repair, or specialized craftsmanship
  • Future favors: Credit with community leaders or guaranteed support when needed
  • Mixed payment: Combination of coin, goods, and services

Steward Mara evaluates non-coin payments at fair market value and helps Wardens exchange goods they don’t need.

Member Benefits

Free Services at Waystone Inn:

  • Lodging: Bunk in common quarters (private rooms available for small fee)
  • Meals: Hearty frontier cooking, three times daily
  • Stabling: For mounts actively used on guild business
  • Basic Healing: Mundane medical care (Medicine checks and healer’s kit usage)
  • Equipment Storage: Secure storage for personal gear between contracts
  • Library Access: Maps, regional reports, historical records, and Lorewarden Elric’s research notes

Equipment Requisition:

Wardens on active contracts may requisition:

  • Standard adventuring gear (rope, torches, rations, basic tools)
  • Common weapons and armor (shortswords, spears, leather armor, shields)
  • Healing supplies (bandages, healer’s kits)
  • Specialized equipment for specific contracts (cold-weather gear, climbing equipment, etc.)

All requisitioned equipment must be returned or paid for if lost/damaged without good cause. Steward Mara tracks requisitions and expects detailed accounting.

Support Services:

  • Research Assistance: Lorewarden Elric helps identify threats and magical items
  • Tactical Planning: Marshal Thorne provides strategic advice for complex contracts
  • Community Connections: The guild’s reputation opens doors in affiliated settlements
  • Legal Support: The guild vouches for members in local disputes (if justified)
  • Emergency Aid: Guild mobilizes rescue efforts for members in danger

Estimated Value: These benefits represent approximately 20-30 gp per month in saved expenses for active members—significant on the frontier.

How to Join

Requirements:

  1. Demonstrate competence (complete trial contract successfully)
  2. Swear oath to uphold the guild code (Six Tenets)
  3. Sign the charter
  4. Receive your Warden’s badge (worn or carried as proof of membership)

Process:

Step 1: Initial Contact
Speak with Marshal Brenna Thorne at Waystone Inn. Be prepared to:

  • Explain your capabilities honestly
  • Describe relevant experience (combat, magic, wilderness skills, etc.)
  • Answer questions about your background and motivations
  • Accept that the Wardens don’t require full disclosure of your past, but dishonesty discovered later means expulsion

Step 2: Trial Contract
The Marshal assigns a trial contract—typically a minor but genuine threat:

  • Solo or small group assignment
  • Tests both competence and judgment
  • Success means completing the objective; style doesn’t matter
  • Honest failure (with genuine effort) is acceptable; dishonesty or cowardice is not

Step 3: Evaluation
The Triad reviews your performance:

  • Marshal Thorne evaluates tactical competence and courage
  • Steward Mara assesses professionalism and resource management
  • Lorewarden Elric reviews your written report (completeness and honesty)

Step 4: Oath Ceremony
If accepted, you take the oath in Waystone Inn’s common room:

  • Swear to uphold the Six Tenets
  • Sign the charter (your name joins the roster)
  • Receive your Warden’s badge
  • Welcome toast from assembled members

Time Required: The entire process typically takes 1-2 weeks, depending on trial contract availability and complexity.

Reputation and Standing

Building Reputation:

  • Complete contracts successfully and professionally
  • Share important information with the guild
  • Help fellow Wardens when possible
  • Support frontier communities beyond contract requirements
  • Handle difficult situations with judgment and restraint

Losing Standing:

  • Contract failures (forgivable if honest effort was made and reported truthfully)
  • Dishonesty about capabilities or contract outcomes
  • Abandoning companions without overwhelming justification
  • Violating the Guild Code (Six Tenets)
  • Misusing guild resources or reputation for personal gain

Consequences of Standing:

Good Standing:

  • Access to better contracts
  • First choice of assignments
  • Guild support in difficult situations
  • Recommendations to other organizations
  • Potential leadership roles

Poor Standing:

  • Probation period with oversight
  • Assigned only low-priority contracts
  • Reduced trust from leadership and peers
  • Excluded from sensitive assignments

Code Violations:

  • Suspension (temporary removal from active roster)
  • Expulsion (permanent removal; badge revoked)
  • In extreme cases: active opposition from the guild

The Wardens believe in second chances for honest mistakes, but not for betrayal of trust. Marshal Thorne decides standing questions, with input from the full Triad for serious cases.

GUILD OPERATIONS

 

 

The Wider World of Aevoria

Welcome to Aevoria

A World of Ancient Magic and Frontier Adventure

Welcome, adventurer, to the world of Aevoria—a land where civilizations have risen and fallen, where ancient powers sleep beneath ice and stone, and where the frontier still holds secrets waiting to be discovered.

This guide will introduce you to the ten major regions of the known world, from the frozen wastes of the Far North to the volcanic fury of the Emberlands. Whether you seek fortune, knowledge, or simply a place to make your mark, Aevoria offers endless possibilities.

Your story begins in Northreach — a cold, dangerous frontier where survival depends on skill, preparation, and the bonds you forge with your fellow Wardens.

Understanding This World

What Makes Aevoria Unique

A World in Transition
The old certainties are changing. Magic that once seemed predictable now behaves strangely. Ancient ruins stir after millennia of silence. Animals act with uncanny awareness. Across the world, from scholars in southern cities to druids in wild forests, people sense that something fundamental is shifting—though no one yet understands what or why.

Ten Distinct Regions
Aevoria is not one unified empire but a tapestry of cultures, each adapted to their land: dwarves who listen to stone’s resonance beneath mountains, elves who preserve memory in silent forests, humans who build kingdoms on art and politics, and those who thrive in lawless cities or volcanic wastelands. Each region has its own character, dangers, and opportunities.

Magic is Rare but Real
Spellcasters are uncommon, especially on the frontier. A village might have one hedge witch or traveling cleric. Cities boast colleges and temples, but even there, true magic is respected and sometimes feared. Divine magic flows from the gods, while arcane power comes from study, bloodlines, or pacts. Both are tools—dangerous in the wrong hands, invaluable in the right ones.

The Frontier Calls
The civilized heartlands—Solaris, the Stonebound Depths, Vaeltharyn—are places of law, tradition, and relative safety. But the frontier (Northreach, the Emberlands, the Shattered Coast) offers what cities cannot: freedom from ancient hierarchies, unclaimed treasures, and the chance to make your own legend. The frontier doesn’t care about your past; it only cares if you’re strong enough, smart enough, and lucky enough to survive.

WELCOME TO AEVORIA

 

 

The Ten Regions at a Glance

1. Northreach — The Frozen Frontier

Where Your Adventure Begins

  • Character: Cold, isolated, dangerous
  • Who Lives Here: Hardy settlers, Northwatch Wardens, isolated homesteaders
  • What It Offers: Freedom, opportunity, and deadly challenges

Northreach is a sparsely settled frontier where winter lasts most of the year and communities survive through mutual aid and sheer stubbornness. The Northwatch Wardens—your guild—operate from the Waystone Inn, taking contracts to protect settlements from threats both mundane and supernatural.

Recent reports speak of wolves acting with unnatural intelligence, strange lights in the northern sky, and ancient ruins emerging from melting ice. Most people dismiss such tales as frontier superstition. The Wardens know better.

Why Start Here: Northreach represents the classic adventuring frontier—lawless, dangerous, and full of opportunity for those brave (or desperate) enough to seek it.

2. Solaris Dominion — The Cultural Heart

  • Character: Vibrant, politically complex, artistically rich
  • Who Lives Here: Bards, politicians, artists, merchants, courtiers
  • What It Offers: Culture, intrigue, social climbing, bardic colleges

Far to the south, Solaris is everything Northreach is not: warm, wealthy, and civilized. The city thrives on music, storytelling, and political maneuvering. Three major factions compete for the city’s soul, each offering a different vision of power and progress.

News from the frontier travels to Solaris quickly, transformed into songs and stories. What you do in Northreach may become legend in Solaris—though the details will likely be embellished.

Adventure Hooks: Political intrigue, bardic competitions, factional conflicts, investigation of arcane secrets

3. The Nullwood Expanse — The Silent Forest

  • Character: Eerily quiet, memory-focused, deeply mysterious
  • Who Lives Here: Elves of the Silent Court, rangers, hermits
  • What It Offers: Ancient lore, magical silence, preserved histories

The Nullwood is an elven kingdom unlike any other: the forest itself absorbs sound, creating an environment of whispers and gestures. The elves here are guardians of memory, maintaining vast archives of the past and fiercely resisting rapid change.

They view recent “awakenings” in the world with deep unease, though they struggle to explain why these events feel so disturbingly familiar.

Adventure Hooks: Diplomatic missions, memory recovery, ancient secrets, forest guardianship

WELCOME TO AEVORIA

 

 

4. The Stonebound Depths — The Dwarven Kingdom

  • Character: Ancient, traditional, resonant with earth-magic
  • Who Lives Here: Dwarven clans, master craftsmen, geomancers
  • What It Offers: Unmatched craftsmanship, deep-earth lore, geological mysteries

Beneath southern mountains, the dwarves have carved a civilization into living stone. They practice resonance—a form of geomancy that lets them “listen” to the earth. Recently, their sacred Heartstone hummed for the first time in recorded history, a sign the dwarves interpret as the beginning of a new “verse” in the world’s song.

Dwarven goods—weapons, armor, tools—are the finest in the world, but they rarely leave the Depths except through trusted trade partners.

Adventure Hooks: Crafting quests, deep cavern exploration, ancient dwarven ruins, geological mysteries

5. Vharoxis — The City of Masks

  • Character: Lawless, opportunistic, deeply pragmatic
  • Who Lives Here: Criminals, smugglers, exiles, merchants, anyone seeking anonymity
  • What It Offers: Black-market goods, forbidden knowledge, second chances

In Vharoxis, everyone wears a mask—literally. Identity is fluid, law is what you can enforce, and “what you can keep is yours.” The city operates on reputation, contracts, and careful negotiation. Betray your word, and you’ll never do business again. Keep it, and even the most questionable deals are honored.

Strange artifacts from the north fetch high prices in Vharoxis markets. Some Wardens have… complicated histories here.

Adventure Hooks: Smuggling, heists, information trading, moral ambiguity, artifact recovery

6. The Shattered Coast — The Maritime Frontier

  • Character: Treacherous waters, shipwrecks, coastal dangers
  • Who Lives Here: Sailors, pirates, salvage crews, coastal settlers
  • What It Offers: Maritime adventure, sunken treasure, storm magic

The western coast is a graveyard of ships, where jagged reefs and unpredictable storms claim vessels regularly. Despite the danger, it’s the primary trade route between north and south. Pirates, salvagers, and legitimate merchants compete for dominance.

Recently, strange things have been washing ashore: glowing stones, humming metal fragments, creatures that behave wrongly.

Adventure Hooks: Naval combat, shi pwreck salvage, pirate conflicts, storm investigations

WELCOME TO AEVORIA

 

 

7. The Emberlands — The Volcanic South

  • Character: Harsh, resilient, shaped by recent catastrophe
  • Who Lives Here: Survivors, the Red Covenant (disaster relief), desperate refugees
  • What It Offers: Extreme survival challenges, volcanic materials, redemption arcs

Within living memory, a magical cataclysm tore the Emberlands apart. Volcanoes rage, the earth splits open, and fire magic runs wild. Despite this, people endure—they have nowhere else to go. The Red Covenant disaster relief organization provides what help it can, but survival ultimately depends on improvisation and determination.

The Emberlands share something with Northreach: both regions experienced dramatic, unexplainable events. Some scholars are beginning to compare notes.

Adventure Hooks: Disaster relief, volcanic hazards, refugee protection, investigating the cataclysm’s cause

8. The Verdant Marches — The Wild Green

  • Character: Lush, primal, alive with natural magic
  • Who Lives Here: Druids, rangers, farming communities, wild beasts
  • What It Offers: Druidic mysteries, natural magic, agricultural bounty

The Marches are Aevoria’s breadbasket—fertile farmland bounded by ancient forests where druids maintain the balance between civilization and wilderness. Recently, druids report the “Green Stirring”: plants growing unnaturally fast, animals coordinating in impossible ways, the sense that nature itself is waking up.

These reports sound disturbingly similar to stories from Northreach. Information flows between northern Wardens and southern druids through ranger networks.

Adventure Hooks: Druidic rituals, beast investigations, protecting harvests, exploring the Green Stirring

9. The Sunken Dominion — The Underwater Realm

  • Character: Alien, mysterious, barely understood by surface dwellers
  • Who Lives Here: Merfolk, tritons, sea elves, deep-sea creatures
  • What It Offers: Underwater adventure, drowned ruins, coral architecture

Beneath the waves, aquatic peoples maintain their own civilization, largely independent of surface politics. Coastal settlements with mixed populations serve as meeting points, but the deep ocean remains mysterious even to seasoned sailors.

The Dominion is “awakening” in its own way—ancient structures are rising, and sea-dwellers speak of “something old” stirring in the depths.

Adventure Hooks: Underwater exploration, diplomatic missions, maritime mysteries, drowned city investigations

WELCOME TO AEVORIA

 

 

10. The Far North — The Frozen Wastes

  • Character: Deadly cold, ancient mysteries, cosmic dread
  • Who Lives Here: Nomadic herders, desperate scavengers, researchers
  • What It Offers: Extreme survival, ancient ruins, forbidden knowledge

North of Palebank Village lies a frozen wasteland where blizzards rage endlessly and the ice stretches to the horizon. Few travel there by choice. Those who do seek one thing: the ruins of an ancient civilization buried beneath millennia of ice.

Fragments of metal towers, strange formations, sealed entrances—the ruins are scattered across the North, their purpose unknown and their contents deadly. Recent reports speak of ruins “waking up,” ice melting in unnatural patterns, and lights moving beneath frozen surfaces.

The Northwatch Wardens are beginning to suspect that events in the frontier may be connected to something in the Far North. Understanding what lies beneath the ice might be the key to protecting the settlements.

Adventure Hooks: Ruin exploration, survival challenges, artifact recovery, investigating the source of frontier strangeness

How the Regions Connect

While each region has its own character, they’re not isolated. Trade routes, diplomatic relationships, and simple human curiosity connect the world:

Trade and Information
News travels fastest along trade routes. What happens in Northreach reaches Solaris through Shattered Coast shipping lanes, then spreads to Vharoxis (as opportunity) and the Verdant Marches (as concern). Information flows, though it’s often distorted by distance and retelling.

Cultural Exchange
Dwarven crafts, elven archives, Solaran art, and Vharoxis contraband flow between regions. Adventurers, merchants, pilgrims, and refugees carry not just goods but ideas, blending cultures at every crossroads.

Shared Mysteries
Scholars across Aevoria are beginning to notice patterns: unexplained magical phenomena in multiple regions, ancient ruins becoming active, animals and plants behaving strangely. No one has connected all the pieces yet, but the pattern is there for those who look.

Your Role
As a Northwatch Warden, you operate primarily in the frontier. But the contracts you take may lead you elsewhere: escorting a scholar to the Stonebound Depths, tracking smugglers to Vharoxis, or investigating rumors that connect northern events to southern mysteries. The world is vast, but adventurers have a way of finding themselves wherever the action is.

WELCOME TO AEVORIA

Welcome to the Northwatch Wardens

You stand at the edge of the known world, where winter bites deep and dangers lurk in every shadow. The Northwatch Wardens need people like you—capable, resourceful, willing to face the unknown.

The frontier doesn’t care about your past. It only cares whether you’re strong enough to survive and determined enough to protect those who can’t protect themselves.

Your contracts await at the Waystone Inn.

A Note on Discovery

This guide contains common knowledge—things your character might reasonably know or learn through basic inquiry. There are deeper secrets, hidden motivations, and mysteries waiting to be uncovered through gameplay. Trust that the world has more to offer than what’s written here, and approach your adventures with curiosity and caution.

The best stories aren’t the ones you read—they’re the ones you live.

WELCOME TO AEVORIA

 

 

Northreach

The Frontier Region

Theme: Frontier survival

Tone: Gritty, isolated, dangerous Northreach is a cold, sparsely settled frontier region most inhabitants know only local concerns—wolves, bandits, missing hunters. This is the home of the Northwatch Wardens.

Geography

Regional Characteristics

  • Climate: Cold temperate to subarctic
  • Terrain: Rolling hills, dense forests, coastal plains, mountains to the north
  • Water: Rivers, coastal access to the northeast
  • Settlement Pattern: Scattered villages, isolated farmsteads, few towns
  • Infrastructure: Rough roads, limited trade routes, frontier conditions

Northreach’s geography follows a practical travel network centered on Waystone Inn, with all major locations reachable through established routes.

Major Locations

Waystone Inn

Function: Guild headquarters, contract board, safe gathering point

Leadership:

  • Marshal Brenna Thorne — Field commander, tactical decisions
  • Steward Mara Fenwick — Quartermaster, logistics
  • Lorewarden Elric Vael — Arcane scholar, investigation support

Services:

  • Contract postings
  • Room and board
  • Equipment resupply
  • Information gathering
  • Guild training

Atmosphere: Frontier warmth mixed with professional efficiency. A place where strangers become comrades over shared dangers.

Welton (Southwest)

Type: Farming village
Population: ~300 (mostly human, some halfling)
Economy: Wheat and sheep farming

Pinebrook (Southeast)

Type: Trading village
Population: ~250
Economy: Trade hub, crossroads settlement
Notable Feature: Vulnerable to organized crime and frontier threats

Key Themes:

  • Community fragility
  • Crime investigation
  • Frontier justice

Palebank Village (Northeast)

Type: Coastal settlement
Population: ~200
Economy: Fishing, limited trade

Temple of the Dragonknights (Northwest Mountains)

Type: Ancient temple complex

Noke’s Tower (West)

Type: Wizard’s tower
Inhabitant: Finethir Shinebright

Culture and Society

Frontier Mentality

  • Self-reliance: Communities depend on themselves first
  • Mutual aid: Neighbors help neighbors survive
  • Practical pragmatism: Survival trumps ideology
  • Wary of strangers: Trust must be earned
  • Respect for competence: Skill and reliability matter more than background

Social Structure

  • Village councils: Local governance by respected community members
  • Guilds: Trade organizations provide structure (Growers, Fleecers, etc.)
  • Religious leaders: Priests offer guidance but limited authority
  • Adventurers: Wardens and travelers treated with cautious respect

NORTHREACH

 

 

Daily Life

  • Agriculture: Wheat, sheep, limited crops in short growing season
  • Trade: Essential goods flow slowly through rough roads
  • Communication: News travels by travelers; weeks between updates
  • Magic: Rare, mistrusted, but increasingly necessary
  • Threats: Wolves, bandits, weather

Factions and Organizations

The Northwatch Wardens (Player Organization)

A frontier protection guild based at Waystone Inn, taking contracts to protect settlements and investigate threats. (See Chapter 4 for complete charter, roster, and membership details.)

Local Governance

Village Councils:

  • Elected or respected elders
  • Make local policy
  • Manage resources
  • Hire Wardens for problems beyond their capability

Guilds:

  • Growers’ Association (farmers)
  • Fleecers’ Guild (shepherds)
  • Tradespeople (limited specialization)

NORTHREACH

 

 

Solaris Dominion

The Cultural Capital
Theme: Art, politics, bardic tradition, factional tension
Tone: Vibrant, dramatic, culturally rich
Role in the World: The political and cultural powerhouse where rumors of the Echo spread fastest

Overview

The Heart of Song and Story

Solaris is a vibrant metropolis known as the beating heart of music, storytelling, and bardic tradition. The city thrives on creativity, performance, and mythmaking—its plazas echo with tales and its streets feel like they are always mid-song.

But beneath the artistic brilliance lies deep political tension. Three factions compete to define the city’s soul, each offering a different vision of power, magic, and the future. Eclipse Day shattered the old certainties, and now Solaris stands at a crossroads between tradition, tolerance, and transformation.

This is where news travels fastest, where secrets become songs, and where political tensions rise alongside troubling reports from the northern frontier.

Geography

Location

Position: Southern region, significant distance from Northreach
Climate: Temperate Mediterranean; mild winters, warm summers
Terrain: Coastal plains, rolling hills, navigable rivers
Access: Major trade routes, busy harbor, well-maintained roads

The City Itself

Size: Major metropolis; population ~50,000
Layout: Concentric districts radiating from central plaza
Architecture: Grand stone buildings, ornate facades, open-air theaters
Atmosphere: Vibrant, crowded, always performing

Key Districts:

  • The Heart Plaza — Central square; performances, statues, meeting point
  • The Songhall Quarter — Taverns, theaters, bardic colleges
  • The Luminary Heights — Temples, government buildings, wealthy estates
  • The Veilbound Commons — Markets, magical schools, diverse neighborhoods
  • The Twilight Gardens — Newest district; Eclipse Day memorial, Chorus headquarters
  • The Harbor District — Docks, warehouses, international trade

Climate and Culture

The warm climate supports outdoor performance culture:

  • Evening plaza concerts
  • Street theater and buskers
  • Cafe society and public discourse
  • Festivals celebrating arts and history
  • Year-round cultural calendar

Major Locations

The Tail Spinner’s Cord

Type: Legendary tavern, cultural institution
Size: Sprawling, multi-level establishment
Reputation: The birthplace of countless songs and legends

Significance:

  • Center of Solaris’ artistic identity
  • Where bards, musicians, storytellers gather
  • Stories told here “gain a life of their own”
  • Performance stage with magical acoustics
  • Cultural touchstone for entire city

Atmosphere:

  • Warm, welcoming, electric with creativity
  • Walls covered with signed instruments
  • Every table has witnessed history
  • Patrons include everyone from street performers to nobility
  • Neutral ground during factional tensions

Services:

  • Performance stage (open to all, by tradition)
  • Private rooms for delicate meetings
  • Message board for musicians seeking collaborators
  • Rumor network (everything said here spreads)
  • Historical archives (songs recorded in special ledgers)
Current State: Post-Eclipse Day

Since Eclipse Day, the Cord has become the epicenter of cultural response:

  • Competing factions hold events here
  • New songs interpret the Eclipse daily
  • Tensions occasionally flare but tradition holds
  • Neutral ground status tested but maintained

SOLARIS DOMINION

 

 

Eldric’s Monument

Location: Outside the Tail Spinner’s Cord

Form: Life-sized bronze statue

Subject: Eldric the Loreweaver, Solaris’ most revered bard

Depiction: Mid-performance, cloak swirling, lute raised—like the next note might still echo

Inscription: “His songs changed hearts, toppled tyrants, and lit the way through darkness. May we have ears to hear what he foresaw.”

Significance:

  • Symbol of bardic tradition
  • Pilgrimage site for aspiring performers
  • Political symbol (each faction claims his legacy)
  • Prophecy debate (did he foresee Eclipse Day?)

Famous Works of Eldric:

Title Type Reputation
The Ballad of the Guiding Stars Epic travel ballad Said to help travelers find their way in darkness
Whispers of the Everwood Mystical folk tune A haunting melody tied to an enchanted forest
The Promise of Evernight Love ballad Solaris’ most cherished romantic song
The Rogue and the Barmaid’s Revelry Tavern anthem Rowdy, blush-worthy sing-along known worldwide

Eclipse Day Connection: Some scholars claim Eldric’s “Ballad of the Guiding Stars” contains veiled prophecy about cosmic alignment. Lines like “when shadow eats the sun, the old songs wake again” are now debated endlessly.

The Three Factions

Since Eclipse Day, Solaris’ political and cultural landscape has fractured into three competing visions.

1. The Luminary Concord

Philosophy: Order, structure, divine law
Motto: “By light alone do we see clearly”

Beliefs:

  • Magic should serve divine purpose
  • Warlocks represent dangerous corruption
  • Eclipse Day was a warning from the gods
  • Traditional institutions must be preserved
  • Power requires moral foundation

Influence:

  • Control most temples
  • Strong in government and law
  • Wealthy supporters and nobility
  • Orthodox religious authority
  • Legislative power

Stance on Warlocks: Strictly opposed; pacts are dangerous shortcuts inviting corruption. They advocate laws restricting pact magic and mandatory registration of warlocks.

Leadership:

  • High Luminary Cassian Brightvow — Charismatic priest of solar deity
  • Magistrate Elara Goldmark — Legal scholar, policy architect
  • Commander Voss Ironlight — City guard captain, military arm

Supporters:

  • Orthodox clergy
  • Established merchants
  • Conservative nobles
  • Traditional artisans
  • Those who fear change

Eclipse Day Response: “The gods showed us shadow so we would remember the value of light. We must purify our practices and return to proven truths.”

How They Shape Culture:

  • Commission traditional art and music
  • Fund temples and orthodox schools
  • Patrol for “dangerous magic”
  • Promote historical continuity
  • Resist radical change

SOLARIS DOMINION

 

 

2. The Veilbound Circle

Philosophy: Magic is personal journey; diversity is strength
Motto: “All paths to power deserve respect”

Beliefs:

  • Pact magic is misunderstood, not inherently evil
  • Persecution creates criminals, not justice
  • Eclipse Day revealed magic’s true complexity
  • Freedom and tolerance make strong society
  • Understanding beats suppression

Influence:

  • Operate magical schools and sanctuaries
  • Popular with marginalized communities
  • Strong in arts and performance culture
  • International trade connections
  • Grassroots support

Stance on Warlocks: Supportive and protective; pacts are tools, not sins. They provide sanctuary, education, and legal defense for warlocks and other unconventional casters.

Leadership:

  • Archmage Sienna Veilwyn — Founder, evocation specialist, former warlock defender
  • Maestro Kallus Fadeborn — Changeling bard, cultural diplomat
  • Advocate Mira Shadowgrace — Tiefling lawyer, civil rights champion

Supporters:

  • Unconventional casters
  • Artists and performers
  • Merchants dealing in foreign goods
  • Intellectuals and scholars
  • Marginalized communities

Eclipse Day Response: “The cosmos just proved that magic is bigger than our laws. It’s time to embrace that complexity instead of fearing it.”

How They Shape Culture:

  • Sponsor diverse artistic expression
  • Provide magical education to all
  • Legal defense for persecuted casters
  • Promote international exchange
  • Challenge restrictive laws

3. The Chorus of the Eclipse

Philosophy: Balance between light and shadow; transformation is inevitable
Motto: “Hear the new song; the world is changing”

Beliefs:

  • Eclipse Day marked a cosmic shift
  • Old rules no longer apply
  • Balance between forces is key
  • Prophecy and destiny are real
  • New age requires new thinking

Influence:

  • Rapidly growing membership
  • Appeal to those seeking meaning
  • Blend divine, arcane, cosmic philosophies
  • Cultural avant-garde
  • Unpredictable but energetic

Stance on Warlocks: Neutral to welcoming; pacts are one of many paths. They’re more interested in cosmic significance than moral judgment.

Leadership:

  • Seer Dominic Starfall — Human prophet, Eclipse Day visionary
  • Lunar Priestess Thalia Nightbloom — Half-elf cleric, balance philosopher
  • Conductor Vex the Resonant — Warlock bard, performance mysticism

Supporters:

  • Eclipse Day witnesses
  • Younger generation
  • Spiritual seekers
  • Experimental artists

How They Shape Culture:

  • Create new art forms mixing styles
  • Reinterpret traditional works
  • Cosmic-themed performances
  • Meditation and prophecy circles
  • Synthesis of magical traditions

SOLARIS DOMINION

 

 

Eclipse Day

What Happened

A cosmic event that changed Solaris forever.

The Event Itself:

  • Rare celestial alignment plunged city into sudden darkness
  • Lasted approximately 15 minutes
  • Magic surged unpredictably:
    • Some spells failed completely
    • Others became catastrophically powerful
    • New effects manifested spontaneously
  • Strange visions swept through population
  • Rift briefly opened above city, revealing swirling stars and shadow
  • Perfect silence fell during totality

Immediate Chaos:

  • Panic in streets
  • Magical accidents and injuries
  • Property damage from surging spells
  • Mass simultaneous visions
  • Religious fervor and fear
  • Some claimed divine communication

Aftermath:

  • Emergency response and healing
  • Witness testimony collection
  • Competing interpretations
  • Political mobilization
  • Cultural explosion of songs, plays, art
  • Formation of Chorus of the Eclipse
  • Factional tensions escalate

Competing Interpretations

Luminary Concord: Warning from gods about magical corruption
Veilbound Circle: Proof that magic is bigger than divine law
Chorus of Eclipse: Cosmic message; the world entering new era
Scholars: Natural phenomenon with unusual magical resonance
Common Folk: Omen requiring interpretation

The Visions

Most Solarians experienced brief visions during totality. Common themes:

  • Starfields rotating in impossible patterns
  • Voices speaking unknown languages
  • Shadows with their own will
  • Memories of events never experienced
  • Futures that might or might not come to pass
  • Ancient structures awakening underground

Many visions included recurring symbols:

  • Geometric patterns
  • Crystalline structures
  • Distant cold
  • Something sleeping, now stirring

Lingering Effects

Months later, Eclipse Day continues to shape Solaris:

Cultural:

  • Explosion of new artistic works
  • Competing performances interpreting the event
  • Eclipse Day anniversary becoming major festival
  • Tourism from those seeking to “understand”

Political:

  • Three-way factional struggle intensifies
  • New laws proposed and debated
  • Warlock registration controversy
  • Magical practice regulation battles

Magical:

  • Subtle anomalies persist
  • Some locations show residual effects
  • Spellcasting occasionally unpredictable
  • New magical talents emerging
  • Scholarly research intensifies

Social:

  • Community fracturing along factional lines
  • Families divided by interpretation
  • Interfactional marriages strained
  • Cultural events become political
  • But also: shared experience bonds city

SOLARIS DOMINION

 

 

Culture and Society

Music as Civic Language

In Solaris, disputes are settled with performances as often as with politics:

  • Competing proposals presented as songs
  • Debates staged as dueling performances
  • Treaties sealed with collaborative compositions
  • Insults delivered through cutting lyrics
  • Apologies sung publicly
  • History remembered in ballad form

This means:

  • Every citizen knows basic musical theory
  • Political savvy requires artistic literacy
  • Bards wield genuine political power
  • Performance skill opens doors
  • But also manipulates and obscures

Social Structure

Artistic Meritocracy: At least in theory, talent matters more than birth:

  • Renowned performers gain wealth and influence
  • Bardic colleges offer social mobility
  • Patronage system supports emerging talent
  • But also: networking and connections matter
  • In practice: wealth still advantages

Economic Classes:

  • Elite: Noble patrons, master performers, faction leaders
  • Professional: Guild members, established artists, merchants
  • Working: Apprentices, laborers, street performers
  • Marginalized: Outcasts, refugees, the struggling

Factional Allegiance: Often matters more than class:

  • Luminary supporters include wealthy and poor
  • Veilbound champions cross economic lines
  • Chorus attracts diverse membership
  • But: resources concentrate at top

Daily Life

For Common Citizens:

  • Work balanced with cultural participation
  • Evening performances are social glue
  • Gossip spreads through song
  • Politics discussed in cafes
  • Religious practice varies by district
  • Magic visible but not ubiquitous

For Performers:

  • Intense competition for recognition
  • Patronage system shapes careers
  • The Tail Spinner’s Cord as benchmark
  • Festivals provide major opportunities
  • Success brings wealth and influence
  • Failure can be devastating

For Political Class:

  • Public image carefully managed
  • Performance skill expected
  • Factional loyalty tested constantly
  • Backroom deals in private tavern rooms
  • Everything eventually becomes public

Storytelling as Heritage

Many citizens know at least one Eldric tale by heart:

  • Children learn stories before letters
  • Families pass down favorite songs
  • Regional variations exist
  • Reinterpretation is respected art
  • Canon debates can become fierce
  • New stories constantly created

This creates:

  • Shared cultural foundation
  • Common reference points
  • But also competing interpretations
  • Historical debates as entertainment
  • Living tradition that adapts

Bardic Magic Dominates

The city’s magical culture centers on performance:

Bardic Colleges:

Central to factional conflict:

Luminary Position:

Veilbound Position:

  • Warlocks are misunderstood
  • Pacts are agreements, not corruption
  • Persecution creates criminals

Chorus Position:

  • Pacts are cosmic connections
  • Patrons may be misunderstood forces

Current Compromise:

  • Veilbound sanctuaries legal

Immediate:

  • Research into celestial events

Theories:

  • Natural magical cycle

SOLARIS DOMINION

 

 

The Nullwood Expanse

The Elven Kingdom

Theme: Magical silence, curated memory, ancient fear

Tone: Serene, introspective, unsettling

Summary

The Nullwood Expanse is an ancient elven kingdom hidden within a vast forest where magic feels strangely muted. Travelers describe the region as unnervingly quiet—not lifeless, but calm, as if the land itself is holding its breath.

The elves who dwell here, known as the Nullwood Elves, are a people shaped by caution, memory, and an old fear they no longer fully understand. Their magic is subtle and disciplined, their architecture grown rather than built, and their society structured around emotional balance and the preservation of harmony.

The Nullwood is known for:
  • Forests where sound seems softened
  • Shimmering, pale-barked trees that sway without wind
  • Elven cities grown from living wood
  • Scouts who watch the world but rarely intervene
  • A cultural aversion to ancient ruins and relics

Though peaceful, the Nullwood is not passive. Its people are watchful, and their silence hides a history older than any living elf.

Geography & Climate

The Nullwood spans a massive temperate forest in central Aevoria, bordered by Solaris to the west and the Verdant Marches to the south.

Location

Position: Central Aevoria, northwest of Solaris
Climate: Mild, with cool summers and long, misty winters
Terrain: Dense old-growth forest, rolling hills, hidden valleys
Boundaries: Natural forest barriers; visitors discouraged but not prohibited

Key Features

The Quiet Canopy

Towering trees whose leaves absorb sound, creating an atmosphere of perpetual calm.

The Stillgrove

A region where magic feels dampened, even suppressed. Spells still work, but with muted intensity.

The Silverflow River

A slow, reflective river that winds through the kingdom, its surface like polished glass.

The Veilwood Border

Patrolled by elven scouts who monitor magical disturbances and watch for threats from beyond the forest.

Capital City:

Vaeltharyn, the Quiet Crown

Vaeltharyn is a breathtaking city grown from the living forest itself. Its structures are shaped over decades through careful magic and botanical guidance.

Overview

Population: ~12,000 (overwhelmingly elven)
Architecture: Grown from living wood, not built
Atmosphere: Serene to the point of uncanny

Notable Districts

The Whispering Canopy

Elevated walkways and homes woven through the treetops. Gardens suspended in air, with soft natural light filtering through leaves.

The Stillwater Mirror

A perfectly calm lake at the city’s heart. It never ripples except in great disturbance and reflects the sky with unsettling clarity. Site of memory rituals sacred to elven culture.

The Memory Courts

Plazas where elves perform emotional and mnemonic rituals. Circular stone clearings used for ceremonies that maintain cultural clarity.

The Veilwatch Spires

Towers used to monitor magical disturbances beyond the Nullwood. Scouts stationed here log distant events they don’t fully understand.

The city feels serene, timeless, and faintly melancholic.

THE NULLWOOD EXPANSE

 

 

Culture & Society

Nullwood culture is built on three pillars:

1. Silence

Not literal silence—but intentional quiet. Elves speak softly, move gracefully, and avoid unnecessary noise.

2. Memory

The elves maintain curated histories, pruning memories they believe harmful or destabilizing through communal rituals.

3. Caution

They avoid ancient ruins, relics, and magical anomalies with near-religious seriousness.

Social Structure

The Silent Regents

Elder council maintaining equilibrium, led by Regent Althaea Moonwhisper. Seven members, each 500+ years old, who govern through consensus and preserve tradition.

Memory Keepers

Specialized caste managing rituals, training in mnemonic techniques, and leading communal ceremonies to maintain cultural harmony.

Veilwatchers

Scouts monitoring beyond the forest, tracking magical disturbances, and reporting to the Regents without intervening.

Common Citizens

Artisans, cultivators, artists who live quietly, participate in rituals, and accept cultural norms.

Daily Life

Values:
  • Patience above urgency
  • Calm above passion
  • Subtlety above display
  • Memory curation above raw experience
  • Community harmony above individual expression
Arts:
  • Music (quiet, complex, haunting)
  • Poetry (emphasizing silence between words)
  • Weaving and growing-craft
  • Memory-sculpture (ephemeral art)
  • Dance (slow, ritualistic)
Taboos:
  • Loud voices
  • Emotional outbursts
  • Unregulated magic
  • Approaching ancient sites
  • Questioning core traditions
  • Disturbing the Stillwater Mirror

Magic in the Nullwood

Nullwood magic is subtle and disciplined:

Specialties:
  • Illusions
  • Emotional resonance
  • Memory shaping
  • Plant-growth magic

Flashy or destructive magic is frowned upon. Years of training are expected, with emphasis on restraint and control over raw power.

The Dampening Effect

The Nullwood occupies a region where magical effects are subtly suppressed:

  • Spells still work, but feel muted and controlled
  • Wild surges are impossible here
  • Teleportation is unreliable
  • Divination produces unclear results
  • Summoning is difficult

The elves believe this is natural—a blessed place untouched by “the world’s noise.”

Religion

The Nullwood Elves revere:

The Quiet Triad

Three deities representing memory, balance, and stillness.

The First Refuge

A mythic sanctuary where their ancestors found peace after fleeing ancient chaos.

Their faith emphasizes restraint and introspection over grand displays of devotion.

THE NULLWOOD EXPANSE

 

 

Eclipse Day in the Nullwood

When the Eclipse struck:

  • The Stillwater Mirror rippled for the first time in centuries
  • The forest hummed with a faint, discordant vibration
  • Some elves experienced flashes of memories they did not recognize

The Silent Regents have forbidden discussion of these visions, but whispers persist of ancient fears resurfacing.

Relations with Other Regions

Solaris Dominion
Cautious friendship. Solaris is too loud, too political, too curious for elven comfort.

Stonebound Depths
Respect mixed with unease. Dwarves dig too close to things the elves instinctively avoid.

Vharoxis
Distrust. The city of masks traffics in relics the elves fear.

Northreach
Growing concern. Reports of strange magic in the frontier unsettle the elves, though they struggle to explain why it feels disturbingly familiar.

THE NULLWOOD EXPANSE

 

 

The Stonebound Depths

The Dwarven Kingdom
Theme: Geomancy, resonance, deep-earth magic
Tone: Monumental, echoing, ancient

Summary

Deep beneath the mountains of central Aevoria lies the dwarven kingdom known as the Stonebound Depths—a vast subterranean realm carved around ancient crystalline formations and metallic structures the dwarves call the Deep Roots.

To the Stonebound Dwarves, these formations are simply part of the world’s natural foundation. They believe the earth itself carries a song—a deep, resonant hum that only dwarves have the patience and skill to hear. Their magic, their craft, and their culture all revolve around this belief.

The Stonebound Depths are known for:

  • Monumental caverns lit by glowing crystal veins
  • Resonant forges where metal sings as it’s shaped
  • Rune-singers who weave magic through vibration and sound
  • Deep-readers who interpret tremors as messages from the earth
  • A pragmatic, grounded worldview

The dwarves are not isolationists, but they are deliberate. They move at the pace of stone—slow, steady, and unyielding.

Overview

Deep beneath the mountains lies the realm of the Stonebound Dwarves, a people who believe the world’s oldest truths are written in stone. They have built their entire civilization around massive crystalline formations and strange metallic structures they call “Deep Roots”—treating them as natural geological features rather than what they truly are.

The dwarves are master craftsmen, resonance-mages, and geomancers. Their magic developed from studying the subtle vibrations of the very artifacts they live among. They record tremors, interpret stone-songs, and forge with harmonic precision, never realizing they’re dancing to the rhythm of dormant Aeorian technology.

Eclipse Day sent shockwaves through the Depths. The Heartstone—a massive artifact core they worship as a natural wonder—hummed for the first time in recorded history. The dwarves believe a new “verse” in the world’s song has begun. They have no idea their sacred geological marvel is awakening.

Geography & Climate

Location

Position: Mountain range between Northreach and Solaris
Climate: Subterranean (temperature stable, humid in lower depths)
Terrain: Massive cavern systems, underground rivers, mineral veins
Access: Surface entry points well-guarded; most of kingdom underground

Climate

The climate underground is cool, dry, and stable—perfect for dwarven craftsmanship:

  • Temperature remains constant year-round (50-60°F in most areas)
  • Humidity varies by depth (dry in upper halls, humid near underground rivers)
  • No weather systems (protected from surface conditions)
  • Geothermal vents provide warmth in forges and lower levels
  • Air circulation through natural and engineered shafts
  • Stable conditions allow for precise metalwork and crystal cultivation

Key Features

The Stonebound Depths stretch beneath the Ironspine Mountains, a jagged range dividing Solaris from the Emberlands.

Notable locations within the Depths:

  • The Heartstone Chamber — A colossal cavern housing the largest Deep Root formation
  • The Resonant Forges — Workshops built around harmonic metal veins
  • The Rune-Singers’ Hall — An amphitheater where dwarven mages shape magic through sound
  • The Lower Veins — Mining districts rich with rare metals and crystal
  • The Echoing Roads — Ancient tunnels that carry sound for miles

THE STONEBOUND DEPTHS

 

 

The Mountain Range

Surface Features:

  • Tall, ancient peaks
  • Volcanic origins (mostly dormant)
  • Rich mineral deposits
  • Sparse surface settlements (mining outposts)
  • Dangerous terrain

Underground Expanse:

  • Hundreds of miles of worked caverns
  • Natural cave systems enhanced by mining
  • Underground rivers and lakes
  • Geothermal vents
  • Massive chambers (some natural, some carved)
  • Interconnected levels spanning vertical miles

Levels of the Depths

Upper Reaches (0-1000 feet)

  • Trading posts and surface interface
  • Fresh air circulation
  • Lighter industry
  • Mushroom farms
  • Connection to outside world

Middle Halls (1000-3000 feet)

  • Primary residential areas
  • Craft districts and forges
  • Markets and guildhalls
  • Government buildings
  • Most of population lives here

Lower Veins (3000-5000 feet)

  • Deep mining operations
  • Rare mineral extraction
  • Geothermal forges
  • Dangerous but profitable
  • Elite miners only

The Foundations (5000+ feet)

  • Ancient levels, partially sealed
  • Heartstone Chamber location
  • Rune-Singers’ Hall
  • Deep-Readers’ Archive
  • Restricted areas
  • Where “Deep Roots” are strongest

The Forgotten Deeps (Deepest levels)

  • Sealed and abandoned
  • Dangerous tremors
  • Strange echoes
  • Ancient excavations
  • Sometimes things are found here
  • Sometimes things are lost here

Capital City: Khardûn-Tharum, the Deep Crown

Overview

The capital city, a monumental underground metropolis carved around a massive crystalline structure the dwarves call the Heartstone. Khardûn-Tharum is a breathtaking subterranean metropolis that feels ancient, monumental, and alive with subtle vibration.
Population: ~45,000 (overwhelmingly dwarven)
Age: Over 3,000 years (on this site)
Architecture: Carved stone, precise geometric patterns, resonant design
Atmosphere: Echoing, monumental, ancient

The city feels like walking through a living testament to craft and patience—every stone precisely placed, every hall designed for perfect acoustics, every forge positioned to sing in harmony with the mountain itself.

The Heartstone

The centerpiece of dwarven civilization:
Physical Appearance:

  • Massive crystalline structure
  • 200 feet tall, 80 feet wide at base
  • Translucent pale blue with metallic veins
  • Geometric facets
  • Internal glow (faint, steady… usually)
  • Hums at inaudible frequencies
What Dwarves Believe:
  • Natural geological formation
  • Crystallized essence of the mountain
  • Heart of the stone’s song
  • Sacred but not supernatural
  • Stable, eternal, trustworthy
  • Foundation of their civilization
Current State:
  • Since Eclipse Day, occasionally hums audibly
  • Crystals vibrate
  • Internal light pulses
  • Runes shift
  • Patterns form in its facets
  • Dwarves excited, not alarmed
  • Interpreting as natural evolution

THE STONEBOUND DEPTHS

 

 

Notable Districts

The Heartstone Plaza The city’s center, where the Heartstone’s glow illuminates the cavern:

  • Cathedral-like chamber housing the core
  • Treated as sacred geological site
  • Public viewing areas and promenade
  • Research platforms built around the Heartstone
  • Guard posts (protecting it from damage)
  • Meditation spaces for contemplation
  • Where Deep-Readers interpret vibrations
  • Now the busiest place in the city

The Forge-Spiral A descending ring of forges, each tuned to a different harmonic frequency:

  • Metalworking using sound and vibration
  • Forging produces subtle enchantments
  • Master crafters create resonant weapons
  • Armor that “sings” when struck
  • Tools that improve with use
  • Dwarven metalwork renowned worldwide
  • Each level produces different tones, creating a symphony of industry

The Rune-Singers’ Hall Amphitheater where magic is shaped through sound:

  • Circular chamber with perfect acoustics
  • Runes carved in concentric rings
  • Magic channeled through voice and percussion
  • Resonance creates effects
  • Training ground for rune-singers
  • Public performances and ceremonies

The Deep-Readers’ Archive Geological records carved into stone tablets:

  • Thousands of years of seismic data
  • Tremor patterns and interpretations
  • “Messages from the deep”
  • Prophecies read in stone-song
  • Currently in chaos: new patterns don’t match records
  • Readers working frantically to interpret

The Lower Veins Mining districts for rare crystals and metals:

  • Dangerous work
  • High pay

  • Competition fierce
  • Growth accelerating near Heartstone

The Stonebound Council Hall Seat of dwarven governance:

  • Master artisans
  • Guild leaders
  • Geomancers
  • Deep-Readers
  • Military commanders

The Embergate The main surface entrance, heavily fortified:

  • Massive gates of reinforced metal
  • Guard barracks and defensive positions
  • Trade inspection and customs
  • Surface world interface
  • Fortified against external threats
  • Now on heightened alert
  • Currently in continuous session (Eclipse Day response)

Culture & Society

Stonebound culture is built on three fundamental principles:

1. Resonance
Dwarves believe the world has a “deep song”—a harmonic truth that can be heard in stone, metal, and crystal. This resonance is not metaphorical to them; it is literal. They train for decades to hear and interpret these vibrations, and their entire magical tradition stems from this belief.
2. Craft
Every tool, weapon, and structure is a work of art. Craftsmanship is sacred—not merely practical, but spiritual. To create something well is to honor the materials, the maker’s lineage, and the permanence of stone itself.
3. Memory
Dwarves carve their history into stone, believing that written words fade but stone endures. Their records go back thousands of years, preserved in tablets that line the Deep-Readers’ Archive. To forget is to dishonor; to remember is to honor.

THE STONEBOUND DEPTHS

 

 

The Stone Philosophy

Core Beliefs:
  • Stone is scripture
  • Mountains remember
  • Everything is geology (even magic)
  • Patience and precision are virtues
  • What is built well lasts forever
  • The deep has secrets, but they’re natural secrets
In Practice:
  • Craftsmanship as spiritual practice
  • Long-term thinking (centuries, not years)
  • Respect for natural world (as they understand it)
  • Magic as science (resonance, vibration)
  • Distrust of things that won’t last
  • Everything must be built to endure

Social Structure

The Stonebound Council
Governing body, meritocratic selection:

  • Forgemaster Grimnar Ironvein — Master smith, traditionalist
  • Rune-Singer Thalia Deepchant — Magical authority, open-minded
  • Deep-Reader Borin Stonescript — Chief interpreter, troubled by new data
  • Mining Guildmaster Kara Gemcutter — Resource management, pragmatic

Values:

THE STONEBOUND DEPTHS

 

 

Magic in the Depths

Resonance Magic

The distinctive dwarven tradition:

Theory:
  • Everything vibrates at specific frequencies
  • Stone carries memory in its structure
  • Sound can shape reality
  • Runes focus vibration
  • Harmony creates effects
  • Dissonance destroys
Practice:
  • Voice as primary tool (rune-singing)
  • Hammers and chisels as instruments
  • Rhythmic work as spell-casting
  • Forging incorporates magic naturally
  • Architecture designed for resonance
  • Living in constant subtle magic
Applications:
  • Structural Magic: Buildings that repair themselves
  • Forge-Craft: Enchantments built into items during creation
  • Seismic Sensing: Reading tremors and stone-song
  • Defensive Wards: Vibrations that repel or detect
  • Communication: Stone carries messages (slowly)
  • Historical Reading: Extracting memory from stone
Philosophy:
Dwarven magic is physical and grounded. They do not trust “flashy” magic—it feels unstable and undisciplined. To them, proper magic should be as permanent and reliable as the stone itself. Fireballs and lightning bolts are showy but temporary; a properly enchanted blade lasts generations.

Rune-Singing

The formal magical tradition:

Training:
  • Decades of study
  • Perfect pitch required
  • Knowledge of rune meanings
  • Physical endurance (singing is exhausting)
  • Understanding of geology
  • Apprenticeship under master
Techniques:
  • Harmonic chanting
  • Runic percussion
  • Resonant visualization
  • Group work (multiple singers in harmony)
  • Solo performances for precision
  • Emergency fast-singing (dangerous, imprecise)
Common Spells:
  • Shaping stone (gradual, permanent)
  • Detecting minerals
  • Strengthening structures
  • Creating light (phosphorescent resonance)
  • Defensive barriers
  • Seismic detection

Deep-Reading

Interpretation of geological phenomena:

What They Read:
  • Seismic tremors (location, pattern, intensity)
  • Crystal formation rates
  • Metal vein growth
  • Underground water flow
  • Temperature shifts
  • Heartstone vibrations
How They Interpret:
  • Historical precedent
  • Pattern matching
  • Mathematical analysis
  • Intuition (experienced readers)
  • Debate and consensus
  • Recording everything
What It Means:
  • Prophecy (the mountain predicts)
  • Warning (earthquake risk)
  • Opportunity (new veins forming)
  • Blessing (stable periods)
  • Mystery (unexplained patterns)

Religion

The Stonebound revere three divine figures, each representing a fundamental aspect of their civilization:

The Deep Father

Domain: Stone, memory, and endurance
Symbolism: Ancient mountain, unmoving foundation
Teachings: Patience, permanence, and honoring what came before

The Deep Father is seen as the eternal foundation—the consciousness of stone itself. Dwarves pray to him when laying foundations, recording history, or seeking stability. His temples are carved from single pieces of bedrock, never adorned, only polished smooth by generations of reverent hands.

Clergy: Deep-Priests who maintain historical records and perform ceremonies for births, deaths, and significant constructions.

THE STONEBOUND DEPTHS

 

 

The Forge-Mother

Domain: Craft, fire, and creation
Symbolism: Eternal flame, hammer and anvil
Teachings: Excellence in craft, transformation through effort, creation as worship

The Forge-Mother represents the act of making—the transformation of raw material into purpose. Every masterwork is dedicated to her. Her shrines sit in every forge, and master craftsmen are considered her blessed.

Clergy: Forge-Priests who bless new forges, consecrate masterworks, and teach that perfect craft honors the divine.

The Resonant One

Domain: The world’s deep song, harmony, mystery
Symbolism: Vibrating crystal, perfect tone
Teachings: Listen to the stone’s wisdom, seek harmony, embrace mystery

The Resonant One is the most enigmatic of the three—representing the song they hear in stone, the patterns they read in tremors. This figure is neither fully god nor fully natural phenomenon. Rune-singers particularly revere the Resonant One, seeing their magic as communion with this presence.

Clergy: Resonance-Keepers who interpret vibrations, lead ceremonial chants, and maintain the acoustic sanctuaries.

Religious Practice

Worship Style:

  • Quiet, contemplative ceremonies
  • Harmonic chanting in specially carved chambers
  • Offerings of crafted items (tools, weapons, art)
  • Historical recitation
  • Meditation in resonant spaces

Sacred Sites:

  • The Heartstone Chamber (considered most sacred)
  • Ancient temples carved into bedrock
  • The Rune-Singers’ Hall (doubles as religious site)
  • Deep mines where the earth’s song is strongest
  • Family shrines honoring ancestor craftsmen

Beliefs About Death:

  • The body returns to stone
  • The soul joins the mountain’s memory
  • Great works preserve the essence
  • Ancestors speak through resonance
  • History remembers the worthy

Since Eclipse Day: Religious interpretations clash:

  • Traditionalists see a blessing from the Resonant One
  • Reformers sense warning from the Deep Father
  • Mystics claim the Forge-Mother is calling for adaptation
  • All agree something profound is occurring
  • Theological debates intensifying

Eclipse Day in the Stonebound Depths

The Event

When Eclipse Day struck the surface, the Depths felt it immediately:

Physical Effects:
  • Massive tremor (strongest in 500 years)
  • Heartstone hummed audibly for first time ever
  • Crystals throughout city vibrated
  • Some stone cracked in geometric patterns
  • Metal veins glowed briefly
  • Underground rivers churned
Magical Effects:
  • Rune-singers experienced power surge
  • Some spells doubled in effectiveness
  • Others failed completely
  • New resonances emerged
  • Old wards flickered
  • Something felt different
Social Response:
  • Emergency lockdown initially
  • Damage assessment
  • Deep-Readers mobilized
  • Council convened
  • Public panic (controlled)
  • Then: excitement
The Interpretation:

Deep-Readers declared: “A new verse in the world’s song has begun.”

Meaning:
  • Geological shift (natural)
  • New era (positive)
  • Opportunity (more minerals will form)
  • Prophecy fulfilled (debatable)
  • Requires study but not fear

THE STONEBOUND DEPTHS

 

 

Ongoing Effects

Months later:

The Heartstone:
  • Hums audibly daily now
  • Internal light pulses
  • Patterns form and shift in facets
  • Deep-Readers working constantly to interpret
  • Some patterns match ancient records exactly
  • Others completely new
  • Growing concern but also excitement
Seismic Activity:
  • Increased tremors throughout region
  • New patterns emerging
  • Crystal growth accelerated
  • Metal veins expanding
  • Some mines becoming too dangerous
  • But also: unprecedented finds
Social Impact:
  • Increased mining activity
  • Research into Heartstone intensifying
  • Foreign scholars requesting access
  • Religious interpretations emerging
  • Some dwarves uneasy
  • Most excited about discoveries

The Divided Response:

  • Traditionalists: Trust the records; this has happened before
  • Progressives: New phenomenon; we need outside help
  • Opportunists: Profit from increased mining
  • Worried: Something feels wrong about this

Connections to the World

Trade Relations

Major Exports:

  • Worked metal (weapons, armor, tools)
  • Enchanted items (resonant craft)
  • Rare minerals and gems
  • Architectural services
  • Geomantic knowledge
  • Beer (surprisingly popular)

Major Imports:

  • Food (grain, vegetables, livestock)
  • Wood (precious underground)
  • Cloth and leather
  • Books and knowledge
  • Surface luxuries
  • Non-dwarven magic instruction

Relations with Other Regions

Solaris Dominion
Respectful but wary.

  • Strong trade relationship; dwarven metalwork highly valued
  • Cultural exchange (limited)
  • Mutual respect but different temperaments
  • Solaris is too political, too emotional, too loud for dwarven tastes
  • Some dwarven performers in Solaris
  • Solarian scholars study dwarven runes

Nullwood Expanse
Mutual respect.

  • Minimal contact
  • Philosophical differences
  • Dwarves find elves evasive and overly mystical
  • Elves find dwarves too focused on physical
  • Their philosophies clash but do not conflict
  • Some curiosity about magical silence
  • Little actual interaction but no hostility

Vharoxis
Disdain.

  • The dwarves see the outlaw city as a nest of thieves who mishandle relics
  • Public disdain but private commerce
  • Black market for dwarven weapons
  • Smuggled rare minerals
  • Spies seeking resonance magic secrets
  • Grudging acceptance of economic necessity

Northreach
Interest.

  • Distant but aware
  • Some dwarven prospectors in frontier
  • Recent seismic tremors match patterns described in fragmentary ancient records—a fact that deeply unsettles dwarven elders
  • Waystone Inn has dwarven-made furniture
  • Occasional trade caravans
  • Both experiencing “strange times”
  • Growing correlation recognized
  • Increasing concern and curiosity

Stonebound Outposts:

  • Several in volcanic south (Emberlands)
  • Mining operations
  • Studying volcanic resonance
  • Reports of increased activity correlate with Eclipse Day
  • Concern growing

Knowledge Sharing

What They Share Freely:

  • General crafting techniques
  • Basic geology
  • Historical records (selectively)
  • Surface-level magic theory
  • Trade agreements

What They Guard:

  • Advanced resonance techniques
  • Heartstone data
  • Deep-Reader interpretations
  • Location of richest veins

  • Ancient sealed levels

Foreign Scholars:

  • Welcome if respectful
  • Must prove useful
  • Access limited
  • Secrets well-kept
  • Some accepted as honorary guild members
  • After Eclipse Day, more foreigners seeking access

THE STONEBOUND DEPTHS

 

 

VHAROXIS

The City of Masks
Outlaw Capital of Aevoria

Summary

Vharoxis is the infamous outlaw city where smugglers, assassins, thieves, spies, and exiles gather beneath a thousand shifting banners. Built on a jagged peninsula surrounded by treacherous reefs, the city is nearly impossible to approach without local knowledge — and that’s exactly how its rulers like it.
Vharoxis is known for:

  • The Masked Market, where secrets are traded like coin
  • Shifting faction control, with alliances changing weekly
  • A thriving black market for relics, contraband, and forbidden magic
  • Neutral ground for spies and diplomats who can’t meet openly
  • A culture of anonymity, where masks are worn as often as faces

The city has no king, no council, and no laws beyond those enforced by the syndicates that rule its districts. Outsiders call it dangerous. Locals call it opportunity.
Vharoxis thrives on chaos — and profits from it.

Geography & Atmosphere

Vharoxis sits on the Blackwake Peninsula, a rocky outcrop surrounded by fog-choked waters and razor-sharp reefs. Only one harbor is safe, and it is controlled by the city’s most powerful smugglers.

The Peninsula

The peninsula provides natural defenses:

  • Jagged rocks and reefs destroy unwary ships
  • Fog banks roll in unpredictably
  • Cliffs on three sides
  • Single narrow causeway to mainland
  • Perfect for isolation and control

City Layout

The city itself is a labyrinth of:

  • Narrow alleys that twist without pattern
  • Rooftop bridges connecting buildings
  • Hidden tunnels dug over centuries
  • Shadowed plazas where deals are made
  • Secret docks for discreet arrivals
  • Crumbling stone towers repurposed as faction strongholds

The air smells of salt, smoke, and danger.

Districts of Vharoxis

1. The Masked Market

A sprawling bazaar where secrets, relics, identities, contracts, and lives are bought and sold.

Rules:

  • Masks are mandatory
  • Names are optional
  • Violence is punished swiftly
  • Everything has a price

The market changes location nightly. Only those in the know can find it.

2. Blackwake Harbor

Controlled by the Blackwake Corsairs. The only safe harbor for miles.

Features:

  • Smuggler’s haven
  • Every ship entering or leaving pays a “tide tax”
  • International sailors and foreign spies
  • Taverns, brothels, and black-market warehouses
  • Best place to disappear

3. The Ember Warrens

A maze of tunnels and slums lit by fire pits. Home to arsonists, saboteurs, and the Ember Veil syndicate.

Atmosphere:

  • Constantly smoky
  • Cheap housing
  • Dangerous at all hours
  • Where “accidents” happen

4. Ironbound Row

The mercenary district. Arena pits, training halls, and the Ironbound Syndicate’s headquarters.

Features:

  • Gladiatorial games
  • Mercenary recruitment
  • Weapon shops
  • Entertainment and violence for profit

VHAROXIS

 

 

5. The Whispered Vaults

Underground banking houses run by the Whispered Coin. Vaults carved into bedrock where fortunes are stored—and debts are recorded.

Services:

  • Banking (legitimate and otherwise)
  • Moneylending
  • Debt collection
  • Foreclosures on assets

Debts are enforced ruthlessly.

6. The High Spires

Crumbling towers now used as safehouses, sniper nests, and meeting places for spies.

Uses:

  • Observation posts
  • Secret meetings
  • Assassination perches
  • Refuge for those hiding

The Five Syndicates

Vharoxis is ruled by five major factions. None can dominate the city alone — the others would unite to crush them.

1. The Gilded Knives

Specialty: Assassins, spies, information brokers

Philosophy: Knowledge is power; secrets are wealth

Operations:

  • Control the Masked Market
  • Spy networks across the continent
  • Assassination contracts
  • Blackmail and leverage
  • Information vaults (physical and magical)

Leadership: The Curator (masked leader; identity unknown)

2. The Blackwake Corsairs

Specialty: Smugglers and pirates
