COMMON GOODS AND SERVICES

 

 

Magical Items and Services

Spell Scrolls

Availability: Extremely rare in Northreach. Most must be commissioned from Lorewarden Elric or acquired through adventuring.

Commission Prices (from Elric):

  • Cantrip scroll: 25 gp + 1 day
  • 1st-level scroll: 50 gp + 2 days
  • 2nd-level scroll: 150 gp + 5 days
  • 3rd-level scroll: 300 gp + 1 week
  • Higher levels: Not available in Northreach

Requires: Spell components (provided by client if expensive)

Spellcasting Services

Lorewarden Elric Vael occasionally provides magical services to Wardens:

Utility Spells (For Wardens on Contract):

  • Identify: 25 gp (1st level)
  • Detect Magic: 15 gp (1st level)
  • Comprehend Languages: 25 gp (1st level)
  • Augury: 50 gp (2nd level)
  • Locate Object: 75 gp (2nd level)

Combat/Adventure Spells:

  • Generally not provided
  • Emergency situations only, DM discretion
Elric’s Research Time

Lorewarden Elric is often conducting arcane research. Commission requests may take longer than standard spellcasting service times. Plan ahead and provide advance notice for time-sensitive needs.

Magic Item Purchase

Common Magic Items:

  • Potion of Healing: 75 gp (limited stock)
  • Potion of Climbing: 100 gp (rare)
  • Spell scroll (cantrip): 50 gp (if found)

Uncommon and Higher:

  • Not available for purchase in Northreach
  • Must be found in adventures or commissioned from major cities
  • Transport time from Solaris: 4-8 weeks
  • Deposit required: 50% upfront
  • Markup: 2-3× Dungeon Master’s Guide suggested value

Enchantment Services

Weapon/Armor Enhancement:

  • Not available in Northreach
  • Solaris or dwarven craftmasters required
  • Estimated cost: 500+ gp for +1 enhancement
  • Time: 2-6 months

Item Identification:

  • Lorewarden Elric: 25 gp (Identify spell equivalent)
  • Mundane assessment: 5 gp (arcana check, no guarantees)

Curse Removal:

  • Remove Curse spell: 300 gp
  • Greater Restoration: 1,000 gp
  • Available only from higher-level clerics in Divinity’s Beacon

“You want a flaming sword? Go to Solaris. Bring gold. Lots of gold. Maybe come back in a year. Or find one in some ancient ruin and hope the curse isn’t too bad.”

—Lorewarden Elric Vael on magic item requests

COMMON GOODS AND SERVICES

 

 

Contracts and Warden Income

Typical Contract Rewards

The Northwatch Wardens operate on a fair-pay system. Contract values are posted on the Waystone Board.

Minor Contracts (1-2 sessions):

  • Investigation: 50-100 gp total
  • Escort duty: 75-150 gp total
  • Monster hunt (common): 100-200 gp total
  • Recovery/retrieval: 75-125 gp total

Standard Contracts (3-5 sessions):

  • Major investigation: 200-400 gp total
  • Dangerous escort: 300-500 gp total
  • Monster hunt (deadly): 400-800 gp total
  • Ruin exploration: 300-600 gp total + found treasure

Extraordinary Contracts (6+ sessions):

  • Regional threat: 800-1,500 gp total
  • Major diplomatic mission: 600-1,200 gp total
  • Deep wilderness expedition: 1,000-2,000 gp total + salvage rights

Payment Structure:

  • Upfront: 25% on contract acceptance
  • Completion: 75% on successful resolution
  • Guild cut: 10% goes to Warden operations (already calculated in posted rewards)
  • Split: Divided equally among participants unless otherwise negotiated
Example: Wolves of Welton

Contract W-17 posted reward: 800 gp
Party of 3 Wardens completes it
Each Warden receives: 266 gp (guild’s 10% already deducted)
Payment on completion at Waystone Inn

Additional Income Sources

Treasure and Salvage:

  • Anything found beyond contract objectives belongs to finders
  • Guild takes no cut of found treasure
  • Valuable finds should be reported (information purposes)

Crafting and Trade:

  • Wardens can sell crafted goods
  • Can trade with merchants independently
  • Can establish side businesses during downtime

Services to Community:

  • Local settlements may pay for specific help
  • Prices vary by need and ability to pay
  • Builds reputation and goodwill

Bounties:

  • Posted by local authorities
  • Typically 50-500 gp depending on threat
  • “Dead or alive” (prefer alive for questioning)

Living Expenses

Lifestyle Costs (per Week)

Warden Members (Using Guild Benefits):

  • Minimum: 5 gp (personal items, incidentals)
  • Modest: 10 gp (occasional treats, better gear)
  • Comfortable: 25 gp (quality personal items, savings)

Non-Members (Standard PHB Guidelines):

  • Wretched: 0 gp (homeless, begging)
  • Squalid: 1 sp/day (7 sp/week)
  • Poor: 2 sp/day (1 gp 4 sp/week)
  • Modest: 1 gp/day (7 gp/week)
  • Comfortable: 2 gp/day (14 gp/week)
  • Wealthy: 4 gp/day (28 gp/week)
  • Aristocratic: 10+ gp/day (70+ gp/week)

COMMON GOODS AND SERVICES

 

 

Shopping Quick Reference

Essential Gear for New Wardens

Minimum Equipment (If Not Using Class Starting Gear):

  • Weapon (appropriate to class): 15-75 gp
  • Armor (appropriate to class): 15-75 gp
  • Adventuring pack: 10-15 gp
  • Waterskin: 3 sp
  • Rations (10 days): 5 gp
  • Bedroll: 1 gp 5 sp
  • Rope (50 ft): 1 gp 5 sp
  • Torches (10): 1 sp
  • Tinderbox: 7 sp 5 cp
  • Backpack: 3 gp

Total Minimum: ~75-150 gp (highly variable by class)

Cold Weather Addition (Essential for Autumn/Winter):

  • Cold weather outfit: 15 gp
  • Winter blanket: 1 gp
  • Snowshoes: 2 gp

Recommended Additions:

  • Healer’s kit: 7 gp 5 sp
  • Tent (if no shelter available): 3-15 gp
  • Extra rations: 5 gp/10 days
  • Healing potion (1): 75 gp
  • Lock picks (if rogue): 37 gp 5 sp

Sample Budget: First Month as a Warden

Income:

  • 2 standard contracts completed: ~400-500 gp each
  • Personal share (party of 4): ~200-250 gp total

Expenses:

  • Lodging/food: 0 gp (guild benefit)
  • Equipment repairs: 10-20 gp
  • Healing (if needed): 25-100 gp
  • Resupply (rations, ammunition): 10-15 gp
  • Personal lifestyle: 10-40 gp
  • Savings/emergency fund: 50-100 gp

Net: Most Wardens can save 50-150 gp per month while maintaining modest-to-comfortable lifestyle, assuming regular contracts and moderate danger.

COMMON GOODS AND SERVICES

 

 

Merchant Price Negotiation

Haggling in Northreach

Frontier merchants expect negotiation, but the margin is thin. Success requires both skill and respect.

Persuasion Check Results:

Check Result Price Adjustment
5 or lower Merchant offended; +10% markup
6-10 No change; merchant holds firm
11-15 5% discount on total purchase
16-20 10% discount on total purchase
21-25 15% discount + future favor
26+ 20% discount + merchant becomes contact

Modifiers:

  • Bulk purchase (50+ gp): +2 to check
  • Repeat customer: +2 to check
  • Guild member: +1 to check
  • Poor reputation: -2 to check
  • Attempting to haggle necessities during winter: -5 to check (bad form)

Cultural Notes:

  • Haggling is expected for major purchases (weapons, armor, tools)
  • Haggling for food or basic supplies is considered rude
  • Never haggle with healers during emergencies
  • Always haggle with merchants from Vharoxis (they expect it)

Barter and Trade

When Coin is Scarce

Northreach settlements often operate on trade and favor systems, especially in winter or after poor harvests.

Commonly Accepted Trade Goods:

  • Furs and pelts: 5-50 gp value depending on quality
  • Preserved meat: 1 gp/5 lbs
  • Medicinal herbs: 5-20 gp per bundle
  • Crafted goods: Varies by quality and need
  • Labor: 2-5 sp per day worked

Services for Trade:

  • Monster extermination
  • Building repairs
  • Healing services
  • Protection/guarding
  • Magical assistance

Reputation as Currency:

  • Completing contracts builds trust
  • Communities remember who helped them
  • May receive free lodging, supplies, or information
  • “You helped us during the wolf attacks; least we can do is feed you”

COMMON GOODS AND SERVICES

 

 

Special Considerations

Seasonal Scarcity

Items Always Available:

  • Basic food (bread, preserved rations)
  • Common clothing
  • Simple tools
  • Firewood (expensive in winter)
  • Basic weapons (axes, spears, bows)

Items Seasonally Scarce:

  • Fresh produce (winter)
  • Healing potions (winter, after major incidents)
  • Complex repairs (winter - smiths focus on essential work)
  • Mounts (winter - too dangerous to travel)
  • Luxury goods (always scarce, worse in winter)

Items Nearly Impossible to Find:

  • Plate armor (must commission from south)
  • Magic items (except potions)
  • Exotic spell components
  • Fine wines and delicacies
  • Books and scrolls (except Elric’s library)

Emergency Prices

When supplies are critically low or danger is immediate, prices skyrocket:

Crisis Pricing (Blizzard, Siege, Disaster):

  • Basic rations: 5× normal
  • Healing: 3× normal
  • Firewood: 10× normal
  • Shelter: 5× normal
  • Ammunition: 3× normal

Price Gouging:

  • Considered deeply dishonorable in Northreach
  • Communities remember and shun those who exploit crises
  • Wardens investigate and may intervene
  • Marshal Brenna has been known to “requisition” hoarded supplies during emergencies

“There’s making a profit, and then there’s robbing people when they’re desperate. The first is business. The second gets you run out of town—if you’re lucky.”

—Steward Mara Fenwick on merchant ethics

COMMON GOODS AND SERVICES

 

 

Travel and Distance in Northreach

Journey Planning for the Frontier

The frontier rewards preparation and punishes haste. Understanding travel times, seasonal conditions, and the costs of movement can mean the difference between a successful contract and a frozen corpse on the roadside.

“Three days to Palebank in summer. Five in autumn mud. Seven in winter snow—if you’re lucky and the wolves stay hungry somewhere else.”

—Corel, Senior Trailwarden

Travel Times from Waystone Inn

Major Settlements

The following times assume good weather, daylight travel, and a party on foot with standard equipment. Mounted travel or wagons will vary (see Travel Methods below).

Destination Distance On Foot Mounted Wagon Notable Hazards
Welton ~25 miles 1 day 1 day 2 days Wolves (frequent)
Palebank Village ~70 miles 3 days 2 days 5 days Ice frogs, winter weather
Pinebrook ~45 miles 2 days 1 day 3 days Trolls (rare), bandits
Noke’s Tower ~18 miles 1 day 1 day 1 day Magical anomalies
Divinity’s Beacon ~90 miles 4 days 3 days 6 days Rugged terrain, pilgrims
The Far North ~200+ miles 9+ days 6+ days Impassable Everything
Quick Reference: One Day’s Travel

On Foot: 24 miles (open terrain), 18 miles (forest), 12 miles (mountains)
Mounted: 30 miles (open), 24 miles (forest), 18 miles (rough terrain)
Wagon: 15 miles (roads only), impassable in mountains or deep forest

TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH

 

 

Settlement-to-Settlement Routes

Common routes between Northreach settlements:

Welton to Palebank Village

  • Distance: ~50 miles northeast
  • Time: 2 days on foot, 1.5 days mounted
  • Route: North road through pine forests, coastal approach
  • Hazards: Coastal storms, ice during winter

Welton to Pinebrook

  • Distance: ~35 miles west
  • Time: 1.5 days on foot, 1 day mounted
  • Route: Western forest road
  • Hazards: Dense forest, occasional troll sightings

Palebank to Salsvault (Far North ruins)

  • Distance: ~130 miles north
  • Time: 6 days on foot minimum, 4 days mounted
  • Route: No established roads; wilderness navigation
  • Hazards: Extreme cold, dire wolves, ice elementals, isolation
  • Special: Requires Survival DC 15 checks daily, cold weather gear mandatory
Chartering Transport

Wagon hire: 5 gp/day + driver (2 gp/day)
Horse rental: 3 gp/day (8 gp/day for warhorse)
Guide/Scout: 2 gp/day
Armed escort: 5 gp/day per guard

Steward Mara Fenwick can arrange transport for official Warden contracts.

Travel Methods

On Foot (Standard)

Most Wardens travel on foot—it’s reliable, doesn’t require feed, and allows for investigation along the route.

Speeds by Terrain:

  • Open Terrain (roads, plains): 24 miles/day
  • Light Forest (maintained trails): 18 miles/day
  • Dense Forest (game trails): 12 miles/day
  • Mountains (rugged paths): 12 miles/day
  • Swamp or Deep Snow: 6 miles/day

Carrying Capacity: Standard PHB rules apply. Characters with 15+ Strength can maintain normal speed while carrying heavy loads; those with lower Strength should plan accordingly.

Forced March: Traveling more than 8 hours requires a Constitution saving throw (DC 10 + 1 per hour beyond 8) or gain one level of exhaustion.

Mounted Travel

Horses are expensive to maintain on the frontier but offer significant advantages.

Riding Horse:

  • Speed: 30 miles/day (open), 24 miles/day (light forest)
  • Cost: 75 gp to purchase, 3 gp/day to rent
  • Feed: 5 sp/day (stable), forage possible in summer (Survival DC 12)
  • Cannot navigate mountains or deep forest effectively

Draft Horse (Wagon):

  • Speed: 15 miles/day on roads only
  • Capacity: 540 lbs or 6 people
  • Cost: 50 gp to purchase, 5 gp/day to rent with wagon
  • Feed: 5 sp/day
  • Roads required; impassable in rough terrain

Warhorse:

  • Speed: Same as riding horse
  • Combat-trained (doesn’t panic)
  • Cost: 400 gp to purchase, 8 gp/day to rent
  • Rare in Northreach; usually owned by nobles or wealthy mercenaries

TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH

 

 

Snowshoes and Winter Travel

Winter travel in Northreach requires specialized equipment.

Snowshoes:

  • Cost: 2 gp
  • Effect: Negates difficult terrain from snow (up to 2 feet deep)
  • Speed: Normal walking speed in snow
  • Without snowshoes: Snow counts as difficult terrain (half speed)

Sleds:

  • Cost: 10 gp (small), 25 gp (large)
  • Capacity: 300 lbs (small), 800 lbs (large)
  • Requires 1 person (small) or 2 people + draft animal (large)
  • Speed: 12 miles/day in snow

Seasonal Conditions

Northreach’s harsh seasons dramatically affect travel. Plan accordingly or risk death.

Spring (Thaw Moon to Planting Moon)

Conditions: Muddy roads, swollen rivers, unpredictable weather
Temperature: 35-55°F during day, freezing at night
Travel Impact: Roads become difficult terrain; river crossings dangerous

Effects:

  • Wagon travel reduced by 50% (mud)
  • Athletics checks (DC 12) to cross swollen streams
  • Random spring storms (10% chance/day)

Advantages:

  • Game returns; foraging becomes possible (Survival DC 12)
  • Fewer predators (many still denning)

Summer (Planting Moon to Harvest Moon)

Conditions: Mild, wet, occasionally hot
Temperature: 55-75°F, rare nights below 45°F
Travel Impact: Best season for travel

Effects:

  • Normal travel speeds
  • No cold weather survival checks
  • Foraging easy (Survival DC 10)

Challenges:

  • Insects (mostly annoyance)
  • Thunderstorms (15% chance/day in late summer)
  • Increased bandit activity on roads
Summer Travel Advantage

This is the only season where inexperienced travelers can reasonably survive Northreach roads. Most merchant caravans operate exclusively in summer months.

Autumn (Harvest Moon to First Snow)

Conditions: Cool, increasingly unpredictable, early snow possible
Temperature: 40-60°F early autumn, 25-45°F late autumn
Travel Impact: Deteriorating conditions; race against winter

Effects:

  • Early autumn: Normal travel
  • Late autumn (after first frost): Travel speeds reduced 25%
  • Constitution saves (DC 10) for extended outdoor exposure in late autumn

Challenges:

  • Weather changes rapidly
  • Game migrates; foraging becomes difficult (Survival DC 15)
  • Communities stockpiling; hospitality strained

TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH

 

 

Winter (First Snow to Thaw Moon)

Conditions: Lethal cold, deep snow, blizzards
Temperature: -10°F to 30°F, windchill often -20°F or lower
Travel Impact: Extremely dangerous; avoid unless absolutely necessary

“Winter doesn’t care about your courage, your mission, or your god. It just kills. Respect it or join the frozen.”

—Marshal Brenna Thorne

Survival Requirements:

Cold Weather Outfit (mandatory)

  • Cost: 10 gp
  • Effect: Grants advantage on Constitution saves against cold
  • Without it: Automatic failure on survival checks

Shelter (required nightly)

  • Tent/lean-to: Constitution save DC 10 to avoid exhaustion
  • Building with fire: No save required
  • No shelter: Constitution save DC 15 to avoid exhaustion, disadvantage without cold weather outfit

Daily Survival Checks: Traveling in winter requires a Constitution saving throw at the end of each day:

  • DC 10 with shelter and fire
  • DC 15 with shelter, no fire
  • DC 20 without shelter (automatic failure without cold weather outfit)

Failure: Gain one level of exhaustion

Snowstorm Survival: During blizzards (20% chance per winter day):

  • Visibility reduced to 30 feet
  • All terrain is difficult terrain
  • Constitution save DC 18 to avoid exhaustion
  • Impossible to forage or hunt
  • High risk of getting lost (Survival DC 18 to navigate)

Winter Travel Speeds:

  • Snow depth 1-2 feet: Half speed (snowshoes negate)
  • Snow depth 3+ feet: Quarter speed (snowshoes reduce to half speed)
  • During blizzard: Travel not recommended
Winter Death Toll

Every winter, 10-20 travelers die on Northreach roads. Locals know: if you can delay until spring, do so. If you cannot, travel with experienced guides, bring twice the supplies you think you need, and write your will before you leave.

Winter Equipment Checklist:

  • ✓ Cold weather outfit (10 gp)
  • ✓ Snowshoes (2 gp)
  • ✓ Winter tent or bedroll rated for cold (25 gp)
  • ✓ Tinderbox and extra kindling (2 gp)
  • ✓ Double rations (assume storms delay travel)
  • ✓ Healing potions (frostbite and injury common)

Navigation and Getting Lost

Staying on Course

Travel on established roads rarely requires navigation checks. Wilderness travel is another matter.

Navigation Check (Survival):

  • Well-Marked Trail: No check required
  • Game Trail or Rough Direction: DC 10
  • Trackless Wilderness: DC 15
  • Poor Visibility (fog, storm, night): DC 20

Failure: Party travels in wrong direction for 1d6 hours before realizing error. This can add hours or days to journey time.

Tools:

  • Navigator’s Tools: Grants advantage on navigation checks
  • Compass: +2 to navigation checks
  • Accurate Map: +2 to navigation checks (DM discretion on map quality)

TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH

 

 

Landmarks and Wayfinding

Experienced travelers use natural and artificial landmarks:

Natural Landmarks:

  • North Star (clear nights): Provides automatic directional sense
  • Moss growth: Unreliable (DC 20 Survival to use effectively)
  • Prevailing winds: DC 15 Survival to interpret
  • Animal trails: Often lead to water, but not always to safety

Artificial Landmarks:

  • Cairns (stone markers): Indicate traveled routes
  • Blazed trees: Trail markers cut into bark
  • Road stones: Placed every mile on major roads
  • Distant smoke: Settlements or camps (investigate cautiously)
Lorewarden’s Library Maps

The Waystone Inn maintains maps of known routes and dangers. Wardens can copy these maps before departing (1 hour work, cartographer’s tools). Lorewarden Elric Vael personally updates them based on field reports.

Terrain Types and Hazards

Open Terrain (Plains, Roads)

Travel Speed: 24 miles/day on foot, 30 miles/day mounted
Navigation: Easy (DC 10 or no check on roads)
Cover: Minimal; difficult to hide or ambush
Hazards: Exposure to weather, visible to threats from distance

Recommended For: Rapid travel between settlements, wagon transport

Forest (Light)

Travel Speed: 18 miles/day on foot, 24 miles/day mounted
Navigation: Moderate (DC 12)
Cover: Good for stealth and ambush
Hazards: Wild animals, bandits, limited visibility

Recommended For: Avoiding attention, hunting, foraging

Forest (Dense)

Travel Speed: 12 miles/day on foot, mounted not recommended
Navigation: Difficult (DC 15)
Cover: Excellent but limits movement
Hazards: Disorientation, predators, difficult to get help

Avoid Unless: Investigating specific locations, tracking quarry, hiding from pursuit

Mountains

Travel Speed: 12 miles/day on foot, mounted very difficult
Navigation: Difficult (DC 15-20)
Cover: Varies; exposure on ridges, shelter in valleys
Hazards: Cliffs, rockslides, altitude, extreme weather, limited resources

Special Considerations:

  • Climbing may be required (Athletics checks)
  • Cold weather even in summer at high altitude
  • Thin air above 10,000 feet (Constitution saves DC 12 or exhaustion)
Mountain Travel

Only attempt mountain crossings with experienced guides, proper equipment, and compelling reasons. The Temple of the Dragonknights expeditions lost 30% of participants to mountain hazards before even reaching the temple.

TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH

 

 

Coastal Regions

Travel Speed: 18-24 miles/day depending on terrain
Navigation: Moderate (DC 12), coastline provides orientation
Cover: Minimal on beaches, good in coastal cliffs
Hazards: Tides, storms, rocky shores, sea creatures

Special Rules:

  • Tide tracking: High tide can cut off beach routes (Nature DC 12 to predict)
  • Storms: Coastal storms arrive with little warning (10% chance/day, higher in autumn)
  • Cliff climbing: Often required for coastal exploration (Athletics DC 13-18)

Random Encounters

Travel in Northreach is rarely uneventful. The frequency of encounters depends on terrain and season.

Encounter Frequency by Terrain

Roads near settlements: 10% chance per day
Wilderness trails: 25% chance per day
Trackless wilderness: 40% chance per day
Winter travel: 50% chance per day (weather and creatures)

Encounter Distance:

  • Open terrain: Spotted at 200-500 feet
  • Forest: Spotted at 50-100 feet
  • Mountains: Highly variable (50-300 feet)
  • Night or poor visibility: 30 feet
DM’s Note

Your DM determines actual encounter frequency and content. These percentages provide guidelines for wilderness travel pacing. Not all encounters are hostile—some may be other travelers, merchant caravans, or wandering NPCs with information.

Common Encounter Types

Wildlife (40% of encounters):

  • Wolves (most common)
  • Bears (autumn, near dens)
  • Owlbears (rare but deadly)
  • Elk or deer (usually flee)

Humanoids (30% of encounters):

  • Other Wardens or travelers
  • Hunters and trappers
  • Bandits (summer months)
  • Refugees or displaced persons

Environmental (20% of encounters):

  • Severe weather
  • Difficult terrain (river crossings, cliffs)
  • Natural hazards (avalanche, rockslide)
  • Foraging opportunities

Magical/Unusual (10% of encounters):

  • Awakened creatures (post-Echo)
  • Strange phenomena
  • Ancient ruins or landmarks
  • Arcane disturbances

Resting During Travel

Short Rest (1 hour)

Can be taken during normal travel day without extending journey time. Most parties rest at midday.

Suitable Locations:

  • Roadside clearings
  • Established campsites
  • Forest groves
  • Sheltered valleys

Activities During Short Rest:

  • Eating and drinking
  • Tending wounds (Medicine checks)
  • Repairing equipment
  • Consulting maps

TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH

 

 

Long Rest (8 hours)

Requires safe location and time. Extends travel day significantly.

Camp Setup:

  • Time Required: 30 minutes to establish camp, 30 minutes to break camp
  • Watch Rotation: 2-hour shifts for parties of 4 (each gets 6 hours sleep + 2 hours watch)
  • Fire: Provides warmth, light, and cooking but may attract attention

Suitable Camp Locations:

Good Camps (Long Rest succeeds automatically):

  • Wayfarer shelters (stone huts along major roads)
  • Abandoned buildings (if safe)
  • Deep forest groves (concealed)
  • Mountain caves (checked for occupants)

Poor Camps (Constitution DC 10 or gain exhaustion):

  • Exposed roadside
  • Wet or marshy ground
  • Windy hilltops
  • Areas with recent predator signs

Dangerous Camps (Constitution DC 15 or gain exhaustion):

  • No shelter during storm
  • Extremely cold without fire
  • Haunted or corrupted locations
  • Active monster territory
Wayfarer Shelters

Stone shelters exist along major Northreach roads, spaced roughly one day’s travel apart. These simple structures provide protection from weather and are maintained by local communities. Always check for occupants (human or otherwise) before settling in.

Watch Duty

Someone must watch for danger during long rests in the wilderness.

Watch Rotation (4-person party):

  • 1st Watch (dusk): 2 hours
  • 2nd Watch (early night): 2 hours
  • 3rd Watch (midnight): 2 hours
  • 4th Watch (pre-dawn): 2 hours

Watch Duties:

  • Perception checks to detect threats (DC varies)
  • Maintain fire if present
  • Wake party if danger approaches
  • Note unusual sounds or sights

Sleeping in Armor:

  • Light armor: No penalty
  • Medium armor: No Long Rest benefit (counts as Light Activity)
  • Heavy armor: Cannot gain Long Rest benefits

“First watch is when you’re fresh and alert. Second watch is when you’re fighting sleep. Third watch is when you think you hear everything. Fourth watch—that’s when things actually happen. Stay sharp on fourth.”

—Bordel Barleywind, veteran Trailwarden

Foraging and Hunting

Feeding a party on the road reduces supply costs but takes time and skill.

Foraging for Food

Time Required: 1 hour (conducted during travel, slows party by 1 hour)
Skill Check: Survival
DC by Season:

  • Spring: DC 14 (scarce, new growth)
  • Summer: DC 10 (abundant)
  • Autumn: DC 12 (harvest but dwindling)
  • Winter: DC 20 (nearly impossible)

TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH

 

 

Success: Find 1d6 pounds of edible plants, berries, roots, or mushrooms (1 pound = 1 day’s food for one person)

Terrain Modifiers:

  • Forest: +0
  • Plains/Open: +2 to DC
  • Mountains: +5 to DC
  • Coastal: -2 to DC (shellfish, seaweed)
Herbalism Kit

Characters with herbalism kit proficiency can attempt to find medicinal plants while foraging. Separate Survival check (DC 15) yields 1d4 herbs suitable for crafting healing supplies.

Hunting

Time Required: 4 hours minimum (half-day activity)
Skill Check: Survival (tracking) then attack rolls (combat)
DC by Season:

  • Spring/Summer: DC 12 (game abundant)
  • Autumn: DC 10 (game fattening for winter)
  • Winter: DC 18 (scarce, desperate)

Success: Encounter game appropriate to terrain

  • Rabbits/Small Game: 1d4 pounds meat
  • Deer/Medium Game: 3d6 pounds meat
  • Elk/Large Game: 6d6 pounds meat

Processing Game:

  • Requires 1 hour + Survival check DC 10
  • Failure wastes 50% of meat
  • Success preserves all meat
  • Preserved meat lasts 1 week in cool weather, 3 days in warm weather

Hunting Risks:

  • Attracts predators (scent of blood)
  • Loud (gunshots or combat alert nearby creatures)
  • Time-consuming (party must stop for hours)

Special Travel Situations

Stealth Travel

When avoiding detection is critical:

Group Stealth Check:

  • Entire party rolls Stealth
  • Use slowest result
  • Move at half normal speed
  • Disadvantage in open terrain
  • Advantage in dense forest

Light Discipline:

  • No fires or lanterns
  • Darkvision characters lead
  • Humans/others navigate by starlight (Survival DC 15)

Forced March

Traveling more than 8 hours per day:

Each hour beyond 8:

  • Constitution save DC 10 + 1 per extra hour
  • Failure: Gain one level of exhaustion
  • Must Long Rest to attempt again

Example: 10-hour day = Con save DC 12
12-hour day = Con save DC 14

Traveling at Night

Risks:

  • Cannot navigate without light (Survival DC 20)
  • Encounter chance doubles
  • Moving at night risks injury (Dexterity save DC 12 on rough terrain or take 1d6 damage from falls)

Benefits:

  • Avoid daytime patrols or detection
  • Cooler temperatures in summer
  • Surprise sleeping creatures

Appendix

Glossary of Aevoria

A quick reference guide to terms, places, organizations, and people of the world

This glossary provides pronunciation guides and brief definitions for important names, places, and concepts in Aevoria. For more detailed information, see the referenced chapters.

Pronunciation Key:

  • Capitals indicate stressed syllables
  • Phonetic spellings use common English sounds
  • Regional variations noted where significant

A

Aeor (AY-or) Ancient civilization of powerful mages that fell in a cataclysm. Ruins of Aeor lie buried in the Far North, and Aeorian artifacts occasionally surface. Known for ambitious arcane experiments and magical hubris. See: The Far North, Salsvault

Aeorian Echo Phenomenon of rising magical energy emanating from buried Aeorian ruins, particularly Salsvault. Causes unpredictable magical effects, awakening intelligence in creatures, and destabilizing arcane workings. Central mystery of the Northwatch Wardens campaign. See: Frozen Sick adventure

Aevoria (ay-VOR-ee-uh) The continent and world in which the Northwatch Wardens campaign takes place. Divided into ten major regions with diverse cultures, climates, and peoples.

Archivists of Aeor Scholarly organization dedicated to studying Aeorian ruins and recovering lost knowledge safely and responsibly. Based primarily in northern research stations. Viewed with a mix of respect and caution—their work is valuable but dangerous. See: Organizations chapter

Argyle (AR-gyle) Common pronunciation mistake: “ar-GYE-luh” Settlement in the Far North. Minor frontier post dealing with harsh arctic conditions.

Aurixean Valignaak (or-IK-see-an VAL-ig-nahk) Dragon name. Common mistake: “OR-ex-ee-an” Silver dragon scholar and Northwatch Warden. Curious, methodical, and somewhat awkward in social situations. Specializes in investigation and historical research. Based at Waystone Inn. See: People of Northreach chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

B

Baleth Cindermoon Half-elf Warden from the Emberlands. Quiet, pragmatic survivor with deep knowledge of disaster relief and improvised solutions. Carries scars from the Emberlands’ destruction. Based at Waystone Inn. See: People of Northreach chapter

Bordel Barleywind Halfling chef and keeper of Waystone Inn. Jovial, welcoming, and observant. Provides comfort food, local gossip, and practical wisdom. The Inn’s emotional heart. See: People of Northreach chapter

Brenna Thorne Marshal of the Northwatch Wardens. Human fighter from Northreach. Direct, practical leader with military background. Commands field operations and makes tactical decisions. “Work smarter, not just harder.” See: People of Northreach chapter, Northwatch Wardens chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

C

Cloakwood Forest region in Northreach. Dense woodland home to rangers, druids, and occasional dangerous creatures. Trade route passes through its edge.

Corel Wood elf ranger-druid hybrid working with the Northwatch Wardens. Speaks little, prefers action. Expert tracker and wilderness guide. Based at Waystone Inn. See: People of Northreach chapter

Covenant of the Silent Vigil Religious order dedicated to protecting society from unaccountable magical power. Opposes reckless arcane experimentation, demonic pacts, and dangerous artifacts. Not anti-magic, but pro-responsibility. Views vary by region—respected enforcers or zealous opposition. See: Organizations chapter, Gods and Religion chapter

Croaker Cave Bandit hideout north of Palebank Village. Named for the croaking sounds echoing from within (frogs, not bandits). Site of conflict during Frozen Sick adventure. See: The Frozen Sick adventure

Currency Aevoria uses standard D&D coinage: copper pieces (cp), silver pieces (sp), gold pieces (gp), and platinum pieces (pp). Regional currencies exist but are easily exchanged. See: Currency and Trade chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

D

Divinity’s Beacon (div-IN-ih-tees BEE-kun) Holy city in the heartlands of the Solaris Dominion. Multi-faith center of pilgrimage and theological study. Neutral ground for all faiths. Home to grand temples, libraries, and religious scholars. Known for hospitality to pilgrims and fierce opposition to unaccountable magic. See: Places of Legend chapter

Dragonknights, The Cult of dragon-worshippers who sought to gain draconic power through rituals and pacts. Led by Brother Alastair. Believed dragons were superior beings deserving worship and service. Defeated in the Temple of the Dragonknights adventure. See: Temple of the Dragonknights adventure

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

E

Eclipse Day Historical event in Solaris. Natural solar eclipse that occurred during a major cultural moment. Commemorated with silence and reflection. Specific details vary by telling. See: Solaris Dominion chapter

Elric Vael (EL-rik VAYL) Lorewarden of the Northwatch Wardens. Half-elf scholar and divination wizard. Provides research support, arcane expertise, and historical context. Curious, methodical, slightly absent-minded. “The answer is in the archives.” See: People of Northreach chapter, Northwatch Wardens chapter

Elro Aldataur (EL-roh al-DAH-tor) Common mistake: “el-ROH al-duh-TAR” Elf scholar in Palebank Village. Researches Aeorian history and the source of the mysterious illness. Knowledgeable but somewhat reckless in pursuit of discovery. See: People of Northreach chapter, Frozen Sick adventure

Emberlands Region of Aevoria devastated by magical cataclysm within living memory. Landscape torn by lingering fire and earth magic. Home to resilient survivors, the Red Covenant disaster relief organization, and desperate communities. Known for improvisation and fierce determination. See: Regions chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

F

Far North, The Arctic region at the top of the world. Home to buried Aeorian ruins, extreme weather, and isolated settlements. Inhabited by hardy folk, nomadic tribes, and researchers studying Aeor. Source of the Aeorian Echo phenomenon. See: Regions chapter

Father Johan Merriksonn (YOH-han MEH-rik-sun) “Father Johan” is fine; full name rarely used Dwarf cleric of the Stonefather in Northreach. Provides healing, spiritual guidance, and community support. Practical faith focused on endurance and honest work. Based in a modest shrine near Waystone Inn. See: People of Northreach chapter

Finethir Shinebright (FIN-uh-theer SHINE-bright) Sheep polymorphed into human form Polymorphed sheep seeking help to stop his polymorphing wizard brother Noke. Panicked, confused, and desperate. Central character in The Wild Sheep Chase adventure. See: Wild Sheep Chase adventure

First Settlers, The Historical group that established Northreach settlements generations ago. Arrived from various southern regions seeking opportunity and freedom. Their stories and traditions form the foundation of Northreach culture. See: Northreach chapter, Songs of Northreach

Freelance Brotherhood Loose network of independent adventurers, mercenaries, and problem-solvers. Not a formal organization—more of a mutual aid society. Helps members find work, share information, and avoid dangerous contracts. Viewed as pragmatic professionals or unreliable freelancers depending on perspective. See: Organizations chapter

Frozen Sick Mysterious illness affecting Palebank Village. Victims develop icy blue veins, fever despite cold skin, and eventual crystallization. Caused by exposure to Aeorian spores from Salsvault. Curable with frigid woe antidote. See: Frozen Sick adventure

Flynt Wymblen Gnome tinkerer and inventor working with the Northwatch Wardens. Enthusiastic gadgeteer with variable success rate. Provides experimental equipment and creative solutions (with occasional explosions). Based at Waystone Inn. See: People of Northreach chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

G

Galvena Aballon (gal-VEE-nah ah-BAL-on) Common mistake: “gal-VEN-uh” Human ex-soldier recruited to the Northwatch Wardens. Disciplined, loyal, struggles with nightmares from past battles. Competent warrior seeking new purpose. Based at Waystone Inn. See: People of Northreach chapter

Gleaners, The Rural mutual aid network in farming regions. Help neighbors with harvests, barn-raisings, and recovery from disasters. Informal but reliable. Represent community values of shared labor. See: Organizations chapter

Guz Half-orc laborer and Northwatch Warden. Quiet, immensely strong, kind-hearted. Does heavy lifting and manual work. Often underestimated due to his silence. Excellent judge of character. Based at Waystone Inn. See: People of Northreach chapter, Songs of Northreach

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

H

Horizon Wayfinders Organization of scouts, cartographers, and guides specializing in frontier exploration. Reliable sources for maps, route information, and frontier intelligence. Neutral and professional. See: Organizations chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

I

No major entries

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

J

Joel Andersmith Human blacksmith in Northreach settlements. Practical craftsman providing weapon repair, horseshoes, and general metalwork. Reliable, straightforward, charges fair prices. See: People of Northreach chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

K

Khardûn-Tharum (kar-DOON THAR-um) Dwarven name. Stress first and third syllables. Capital city of the Stonebound Depths. Great underground metropolis carved into living stone. Center of dwarven craft, culture, and geomancy. Known for resonance halls and ancestral vaults. See: Stonebound Depths chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

L

Leanor Slatebeard (LEE-nor SLAYT-beerd) Dwarf tracker in Welton. Gruff, pragmatic, expert at reading wilderness signs. Helps investigate wolf attacks on Westly’s farm. Takes contracts but cares about community safety. See: People of Northreach chapter, Wolves of Welton adventure

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

M

Mara Fenwick Steward of the Northwatch Wardens. Human quartermaster from merchant family background. Manages supplies, logistics, and finances with cheerful efficiency. “We’ll make it work.” See: People of Northreach chapter, Northwatch Wardens chapter

Mila Teno (MY-luh TEH-noh) Common mistake: “mee-LAH” Human cartographer and clerk for the Northwatch Wardens. Organized, detail-focused, maintains mission records and maps. Provides intelligence and documentation support. Based at Waystone Inn. See: People of Northreach chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

N

Noke (NOHK) Rhymes with “spoke” Polymorphing wizard conducting dangerous experiments. Finethir’s brother. Accidentally transformed himself into a sheep and is pursued in the Wild Sheep Chase adventure. Ambitious researcher with poor judgment. See: Wild Sheep Chase adventure

Noke’s Tower Wizard’s tower west of Waystone Inn. Site of Noke’s polymorphing experiments. Contains spell components, research notes, magical traps, and aggressive sheep. See: Wild Sheep Chase adventure

Northreach Frontier region of Aevoria. The player characters’ starting location. Characterized by harsh winters, practical communities, and frontier independence. Home to the Waystone Inn (Northwatch Wardens headquarters). Known for resilience, hospitality to newcomers, and deep suspicion of authority. See: Northreach chapter

Northwatch Wardens Adventuring guild based at Waystone Inn in Northreach. Operates on contract system—members take jobs and get paid. Leadership triad: Marshal Brenna Thorne (tactics), Steward Mara Fenwick (logistics), Lorewarden Elric Vael (research). Motto: “We watch. We act. We endure.” See: Northwatch Wardens chapter

Nullwood Expanse (NULL-wood ex-PANS) Elven-dominated forest region characterized by silence wards and memory preservation culture. Home to the Silent Court. Trees absorb sound; inhabitants speak in whispers and gestures. Values memory, records, and cautious change. See: Regions chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

O

No major entries

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

P

Palebank Village Coastal settlement in northeast Northreach. Fishing and trade community near frozen wilderness. Site of the Frozen Sick adventure where mysterious illness strikes. Gateway to northern exploration. See: Northreach chapter, Frozen Sick adventure

Pelc (PELK) Rhymes with “elk” Human merchant in Palebank Village. Trades in furs, fish, and expedition supplies. Practical, profit-minded but fair. Source of local information and goods. See: People of Northreach chapter

Pinebrook Trading village in southeast Northreach. Agricultural and commerce focus. Site of “Peril in Pinebrook” adventure involving mysterious disappearances. See: Northreach chapter, Peril in Pinebrook adventure

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

Q

No major entries

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

R

Red Covenant, The Disaster relief organization operating in the Emberlands and beyond. Provides aid, rebuilding assistance, and refugee support. Funded by donations and wealthy patrons. Viewed with deep respect—they work where others won’t. See: Organizations chapter

Resonance Dwarven cultural practice of listening to stone. Geomantic technique for understanding structural integrity, finding ore, and detecting danger. Both practical skill and spiritual connection to the Stonefather. See: Stonebound Depths chapter

Rowan Fairweather Human bard and Northwatch Warden. Charismatic storyteller, morale booster, and negotiator. Performs at Waystone Inn, gathers rumors, handles diplomatic situations. “There’s always a story here.” Based at Waystone Inn. See: People of Northreach chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

S

Salsvault (SALZ-volt) Stress first syllable Buried Aeorian ruin far north of Palebank Village. Source of frigid woe spores and the Aeorian Echo phenomenon. Dangerous research site containing ancient magical experiments. See: Frozen Sick adventure, The Far North chapter

Sera Gelanadel (SAIR-uh gel-AN-uh-del) Elven name. Common mistake: “suh-RAH” High elf sorcerer and Northwatch Warden. Noble background, arcane expertise, diplomatic skills. Handles magical investigations and social situations. Polished but genuine. Based at Waystone Inn. See: People of Northreach chapter

Shepherd’s Crook Inn Community gathering place in Welton. Local tavern and social hub run by welcoming proprietors. Source of village news and gossip. See: Welton, Wolves of Welton adventure

Silent Court, The Governing body of the Nullwood Expanse. Elven council that preserves memory and protects the forest. Deliberate, cautious, values tradition. Communicates in elaborate sign language and whispers. Distrusts rapid change and outsiders. See: Organizations chapter, Nullwood Expanse chapter

Solace Nexus (SOH-luss NEX-us) Ley-line port city in the Verdant Marches. Hub for regulated magical transportation and spellwork. Known for arcane bureaucracy, spell licensing, and magical trade. Efficient but paperwork-heavy. See: Places of Legend chapter

Solaris (soh-LAIR-iss) Region and city share the name Cultural capital of Aevoria and the Solaris Dominion. Center of arts, politics, bardic colleges, and courtly intrigue. Known for Eclipse Day commemoration, sophisticated culture, and complex social politics. See: Regions chapter

Solaris Dominion Southern region of Aevoria centered on the city of Solaris. Characterized by cultural sophistication, strong Radiant Queen worship, and political complexity. Heartland of civilization and traditional power structures. See: Regions chapter

Solace Trade Consortium Powerful merchant guild controlling most long-distance trade routes. Provides banking, contract enforcement, and trade negotiations. Essential for commerce but expensive. Viewed as reliable professionals or greedy monopolists depending on perspective. See: Organizations chapter

Stonebound Assembly Governing council of the Stonebound Depths. Dwarven leadership based on clan representation and demonstrated craft mastery. Values tradition, quality work, and community stability. See: Organizations chapter, Stonebound Depths chapter

Stonebound Depths Dwarven homeland beneath southern mountains. Underground realm of mines, forges, and great halls. Known for masterwork crafting, ancestral traditions, resonance geomancy, and stone expertise. Values endurance, quality, and honoring ancestors. See: Regions chapter

Stonefather, The Dwarven deity of craft, endurance, and stone. Patron of artisans, miners, and those who build things to last. Emphasis on honest work and practical faith. See: Gods and Religion chapter

Sunken Dominion Underwater realm of aquatic peoples (merfolk, tritons, sea elves). Explored through diving, water-breathing magic, or coastal settlements with mixed population. Known for beautiful coral architecture and mysterious deep-sea cultures. See: Regions chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

T

Takk Oaksplitter (TAK OAK-split-er) “Takk” rhymes with “back” Half-orc carpenter and Northwatch Warden. Skilled woodworker providing construction, repairs, and carpentry. Calm, methodical, takes pride in quality work. Based at Waystone Inn. See: People of Northreach chapter

Temple of the Dragonknights Cult stronghold in the northwest mountains of Northreach. Site of dragon-worshipping rituals and draconic power experiments. Location of capstone adventure for Season One. See: Temple of the Dragonknights adventure

Tide Callers’ Guild Maritime organization of sailors, navigators, and weather-watchers. Provide shipping services, coastal rescue, and navigation expertise. Essential for Shattered Coast and maritime trade. See: Organizations chapter

Tillus Merrion (TIL-us MAIR-ee-on) Human council member in Welton. Practical village leader handling administrative matters and community decisions. Concerned about wolf attacks threatening his community. See: People of Northreach chapter, Wolves of Welton adventure

Tulgi Lutan (TOOL-gee LOO-tan) Goliath name. Stress first syllable of each name. Goliath healer in Palebank Village. Herbalist and practical medicine provider. Treats mundane injuries and illnesses with natural remedies. Caring but gruff. See: People of Northreach chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

U

Unmasked Parliament Governing council of Vharoxis. Operates without masks (unusual for Vharoxis culture), signaling transparency in official capacity. Manages city infrastructure and mediates disputes. Limited power—much of Vharoxis operates outside official channels. See: Organizations chapter, Vharoxis chapter

Urgon Wenth (UR-gon WENTH) Dwarf name. Both parts rhyme with “fur-gone” and “tenth” Dwarf blacksmith in Palebank Village. Provides weapon repair, metal goods, and smithing services. Traditional craftsman maintaining dwarven quality standards. Reliable and fair. See: People of Northreach chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

V

Vaeltharyn (VALE-thar-in) Elven name. Stress first syllable. Capital city of the Nullwood Expanse. Great elven metropolis grown into living trees. Center of memory preservation and silent culture. Known for vast libraries, whisper chambers, and living architecture. See: Nullwood Expanse chapter

Verdant Marches, The (VER-dent MAR-chez) Fertile farmland region of central Aevoria. Breadbasket of the continent. Known for agriculture, seasonal festivals, and nature-aligned worship. Home to Solace Nexus ley-line port. See: Regions chapter

Verdant Mother, The Nature deity of growth, seasons, and balance. Patron of farmers, druids, and those living in harmony with natural cycles. Worship involves seasonal festivals and offerings. See: Gods and Religion chapter

Vharoxis (vah-ROX-iss) Stress middle syllable: “vah-ROX-iss” Outlaw city on the southern coast. Known for mask culture, black market trade, and absence of traditional law. “What you can keep is yours.” Operates on reputation, contracts, and personal power. Dangerous but full of opportunities unavailable elsewhere. See: Regions chapter

GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA

 

 

W

Waystone Inn Headquarters of the Northwatch Wardens. Fortified inn serving as guild base, lodging, tavern, and community hub. Run by halfling chef Bordel Barleywind. Located centrally in Northreach territory. See: Northwatch Wardens chapter

Welton Farming village southwest of Waystone Inn. Agricultural community experiencing mysterious wolf attacks in the Wolves of Welton adventure. Home to the Shepherd’s Crook Inn. See: Northreach chapter, Wolves of Welton adventure

Westly Shepherd in Welton whose farm is attacked by awakened wolves. Frightened but trying to protect his livelihood. Hires Northwatch Wardens to investigate. See: Wolves of Welton adventure

Westly’s Farm Sheep farm west of Welton. Site of initial wolf attacks that trigger the Wolves of Welton adventure. Remote location with vulnerable livestock. See: Wolves of Welton adventure

Wild Sheep Chase, The Comic relief adventure involving polymorphing wizard Noke, his sheep-brother Finethir, and aggressive awakened sheep. Lighthearted tone but connects to campaign themes of destabilizing magic. See: Wild Sheep Chase adventure

Willen Featherock Aarakocra scout and Northwatch Warden. Airborne reconnaissance specialist providing aerial perspective and scouting. Enthusiastic, helpful, sometimes fails to understand ground-based limitations. Based at Waystone Inn. See: People of Northreach chapter

Wolves of Welton Adventure involving awakened wolves with developing intelligence attacking farms near Welton. First major indication of the Aeorian Echo phenomenon affecting wildlife. Moral complexity—wolves aren’t evil, just hungry and confused. See: Wolves of Welton adventure

SONGS OF THE NORTHREACH

 

 

THE FRONTIER BREATHES

LANTERNS AT THE WAYSTONE

Verse 1

There’s a lantern at the Waystone Inn That never seems to fade. Through winter storms and drifting snows, Its golden light is laid. Travelers say the hearth burns warm No matter how winds roar— And the road feels shorter somehow When you’re walking toward its door.

Chorus

Lanterns at the Waystone, Shining through the night. Guiding weary footsteps By their gentle, steady light. Lanterns at the Waystone, Soft against the cold— A quiet place on a long, long road, Where stories rest untold.

Verse 2

Some swear the air grows calmer there, As if the world exhales. Others say the shadows fall In strangely peaceful trails. But no one speaks of omens, And no one asks for signs— They simply take their comfort In the warmth the inn provides.

Chorus

Lanterns at the Waystone, Shining through the night. Guiding weary footsteps By their gentle, steady light. Lanterns at the Waystone, Soft against the cold— A quiet place on a long, long road, Where stories rest untold.

Bridge

Maybe it’s the timber, Maybe it’s the stone— Maybe it’s the feeling Of never being quite alone.

Final Chorus

Lanterns at the Waystone, Shining through the night. Guiding weary footsteps By their gentle, steady light. Lanterns at the Waystone, Soft against the cold— A quiet place on a long, long road, Where stories rest untold.

THE HUNTER WHO RETURNED ALONE

Verse 1

They say the snows were higher then, The winds a sharper blade. The hunters marched at winter’s call Through shadowed, frozen glade. But only one came walking back, Her bowstring stiff with frost— And no one asked what met them there, Or what the others lost.

Chorus

Oh the winter keeps its secrets, And the pines, they never tell. Some roads lead home in silence, Some wanderings end in hell. But the Hunter who returned alone Still walks the northern stone— And the wind that follows at her heels Is colder than the bone.

Verse 2

She never speaks of what she saw, Nor names the ones she led. But when the moon is thin and pale, Her eyes turn toward the dead. The Wardens know her steady hand, Her voice that does not shake— But none can read the quiet grief That winter will not break.

Chorus

Oh the winter keeps its secrets, And the pines, they never tell. Some roads lead home in silence, Some wanderings end in hell. But the Hunter who returned alone Still walks the northern stone— And the wind that follows at her heels Is colder than the bone.

Bridge

Some say the storm remembers, Some say the night does too— But she just keeps on walking, As all true hunters do.

Final Chorus

Oh the winter keeps its secrets, And the pines, they never tell. Some roads lead home in silence, Some wanderings end in hell. But the Hunter who returned alone Still walks the northern stone— And the wind that follows at her heels Is colder than the bone.

THE FRONTIER BREATHES

 

 

THE WOMAN WITH TWO SHADOWS

Verse 1

There’s a tale they tell in market towns Of a woman quick and bright— Who walks as if she listens To footsteps out of sight. They say she keeps her ledger clean, Her smile warm and wide— But some swear when the lanterns dim, A second shadow walks beside.

Chorus

Oh the woman with two shadows, She moves like shifting sand. One rooted in the daylight, One reaching for her hand. No one knows her story, No one speaks her name— But the woman with two shadows Walks faster than her shame.

Verse 2

She bargains fair with merchants, She laughs with honest folk— But travelers whisper softly Of debts that never spoke. And though she keeps her head down low, Her eyes still scan the door— As if she fears a knocking From a life she knew before.

Chorus

Oh the woman with two shadows, She moves like shifting sand. One rooted in the daylight, One reaching for her hand. No one knows her story, No one speaks her name— But the woman with two shadows Walks faster than her shame.

Bridge

Some say she fled the winter, Some say she fled the knife— But all agree her shadows Have followed all her life.

Final Chorus

Oh the woman with two shadows, She moves like shifting sand. One rooted in the daylight, One reaching for her hand. No one knows her story, No one speaks her name— But the woman with two shadows Walks faster than her shame.

THE SLEEPLESS SCHOLAR

Verse 1

There’s a candle in the tower That burns through every night. A scholar keeps his vigil there By thin and silver light. He writes of winds that wander wrong, Of stars that shift their place— And though he speaks in gentle tones, There’s worry in his face.

Chorus

Oh the sleepless scholar watches While the northern shadows grow. He listens to the quiet For things he cannot show. And though his words are measured, And though his smile is mild— The sleepless scholar knows too much To ever sleep like a child.

Verse 2

Some say he dreams with open eyes, Of frost beneath the stone— Of something stirring far away In places long unknown. He never speaks of visions, He never names the signs— But he keeps his quill at ready When the winter moon declines.

Chorus

Oh the sleepless scholar watches While the northern shadows grow. He listens to the quiet For things he cannot show. And though his words are measured, And though his smile is mild— The sleepless scholar knows too much To ever sleep like a child.

Bridge

The Wardens trust his wisdom, Though they do not know its cost— For every night he studies Is another morning lost.

Final Chorus

Oh the sleepless scholar watches While the northern shadows grow. He listens to the quiet For things he cannot show. And though his words are measured, And though his smile is mild— The sleepless scholar knows too much To ever sleep like a child.

THE FRONTIER BREATHES

 

 

THE SHEPHERD WHO HEARD THE HILLS SPEAK

Verse 1

They say he walks the Welton fields Before the break of day, Listening to the quiet earth In his own peculiar way. He knows the paths the rivers take, The turns the foxes choose— And he can read the winter wind Like others read the news.

Chorus

Oh the hills speak softly To the ones who walk alone. Their whispers ride the morning frost, Their secrets carved in stone. And though he never tells them, And though he never seeks— The shepherd of the Welton fields Once heard the hillside speak.

Verse 2

Some claim he knows the wolves by name, And they know him in kind. He walks the borders unafraid With steady heart and mind. But when the moon is hanging low And shadows stretch and creep— He pauses, as if listening To something in the deep.

Chorus

Oh the hills speak softly To the ones who walk alone. Their whispers ride the morning frost, Their secrets carved in stone. And though he never tells them, And though he never seeks— The shepherd of the Welton fields Once heard the hillside speak.

Bridge

A dream can be a warning, A dream can be a guide— But some dreams stay unspoken, Kept quietly inside.

Final Chorus

Oh the hills speak softly To the ones who walk alone. Their whispers ride the morning frost, Their secrets carved in stone. And though he never tells them, And though he never seeks— The shepherd of the Welton fields Once heard the hillside speak.

TRACKS IN THE SNOW THAT NEVER FADE

Verse 1

There’s a tale the rangers whisper When the winter nights grow long— Of a man who walks the northern trails With silence in his song. They say he knows the forest well, Each ridge and frozen glade— But he avoids a certain hollow Where old tracks never fade.

Chorus

Oh the snow remembers footsteps, And the wind recalls the cries. Some paths are marked by shadows, Some truths by silent eyes. And though he walks with steady stride, His heart is heavy‑laid— For he has seen the kind of tracks That never truly fade.

Verse 2

He keeps his stories close at hand, His memories even closer. He speaks of wolves with reverence, Of winter growing colder. But when the fire burns low at night, And talk begins to stray— He stares into the embers As if they pull him far away.

Chorus

Oh the snow remembers footsteps, And the wind recalls the cries. Some paths are marked by shadows, Some truths by silent eyes. And though he walks with steady stride, His heart is heavy‑laid— For he has seen the kind of tracks That never truly fade.

Bridge

Some say he guards a secret, Some say he guards a friend— But all agree the northern trails Will follow him to end.

Final Chorus

Oh the snow remembers footsteps, And the wind recalls the cries. Some paths are marked by shadows, Some truths by silent eyes. And though he walks with steady stride, His heart is heavy‑laid— For he has seen the kind of tracks That never truly fade.

THE FRONTIER BREATHES

 

 

THE GIRL WHO FEARED THE MOONLIT PINES

Verse 1

She walks with steady footsteps And her armor gleams like dawn— But when the night wind stirs the pines, Her courage feels withdrawn. For somewhere in the shadows, Where the silver moonlight spills, She hears a distant memory That time has never stilled.

Chorus

Oh the moonlit pines remember, And the winter winds recall— The cries that fade in darkness, The names we never call. And though she stands unshaken When danger draws its lines— Her heartbeat quickens softly Near the moonlit, whispering pines.

Verse 2

She trains with blade and discipline, Her stance both sharp and true— But when the wolves begin to howl, Her breath comes cold and few. She hides it from her comrades, She hides it from herself— But fear can linger quietly Like a book upon a shelf.

Chorus

Oh the moonlit pines remember, And the winter winds recall— The cries that fade in darkness, The names we never call. And though she stands unshaken When danger draws its lines— Her heartbeat quickens softly Near the moonlit, whispering pines.

Bridge

Some wounds are carved in silence, Some griefs are never named— But still she walks the northern trails, Determined, unashamed.

Final Chorus

Oh the moonlit pines remember, And the winter winds recall— The cries that fade in darkness, The names we never call. And though she stands unshaken When danger draws its lines— Her heartbeat quickens softly Near the moonlit, whispering pines.

THE SHEPHERD WHO HEARD TOO MUCH

Verse 1

He walks the fields at sunrise With a tremble in his stride— A shepherd born to quiet work, To hills both deep and wide. But something in the shadows Has left him pale and worn— A whisper carried on the wind From one cold winter morn.

Chorus

Oh the shepherd who heard too much, Oh the voice that chilled his bone— Some truths are meant for moonlight, Some best left unknown. And though he tries to steady The shaking in his touch— The hills remember clearly What the shepherd heard too much.

Verse 2

He flinches at the nighttime, At the rustle in the grass— At distant howls that echo Through the Welton mountain pass. He never tells the full tale, He never speaks the sound— But fear has left its footprints Where his courage once was found.

Chorus

Oh the shepherd who heard too much, Oh the voice that chilled his bone— Some truths are meant for moonlight, Some best left unknown. And though he tries to steady The shaking in his touch— The hills remember clearly What the shepherd heard too much.

Bridge

Some nights he wakes in silence, Some nights he wakes in cries— But always with the memory Of something wise… and wild.

Final Chorus

Oh the shepherd who heard too much, Oh the voice that chilled his bone— Some truths are meant for moonlight, Some best left unknown. And though he tries to steady The shaking in his touch— The hills remember clearly What the shepherd heard too much.

THE WOLF WHO WALKED LIKE A MAN

Verse 1

They whisper of a silver wolf Who walks the forest floor— Not prowling like his kinfolk, But thinking something more. His eyes are sharp with knowing, His steps both sure and slow— As if he bears a question That no creature ought to know.

Chorus

Oh the wolf who walked like a man, With a mind both wild and wise— A shadow born of winter, A spark behind his eyes. And though he leads in silence, And though he hides his fear— The wolf who walked like a man Knows something waking near.

Verse 2

He watches from the treeline When the moon is thin and pale— A sentinel of secrets In the frost along the trail. Some say he speaks in glances, Some say he dreams in fire— But all agree his quiet gaze Is older than desire.

Chorus

Oh the wolf who walked like a man, With a mind both wild and wise— A shadow born of winter, A spark behind his eyes. And though he leads in silence, And though he hides his fear— The wolf who walked like a man Knows something waking near.

Bridge

Some gifts are born unwanted, Some gifts are born of dread— But still he guards the forest Where the ancient paths are led.

Final Chorus

Oh the wolf who walked like a man, With a mind both wild and wise— A shadow born of winter, A spark behind his eyes. And though he leads in silence, And though he hides his fear— The wolf who walked like a man Knows something waking near.

THE FIRE IN THE WINTER PACK

Verse 1

They tell of one with burning eyes Who stalks the frozen glen— A wolf whose growl is thunder, Whose pride outmatches men. He walks with fire beneath his fur, A storm behind his stride— And every step he takes declares A challenge to the wild.

Chorus

Oh the fire in the winter pack, Oh the fury in his breath— A blaze that cuts through silence Like a promise unto death. And though the night grows colder, And though the shadows track— The fire in the winter pack Will never turn his back.

Verse 2

Some say he dreams of kingdoms, Of forests bowed in awe— Of wolves who rise like sovereigns Above the ancient law. He stands upon the ridgeline When the moon is sharp and bright— A silhouette of hunger Against the northern night.

Chorus

Oh the fire in the winter pack, Oh the fury in his breath— A blaze that cuts through silence Like a promise unto death. And though the night grows colder, And though the shadows track— The fire in the winter pack Will never turn his back.

Bridge

Some flames are born of anger, Some flames are born of pride— But his was born of something That stirs the world outside.

Final Chorus

Oh the fire in the winter pack, Oh the fury in his breath— A blaze that cuts through silence Like a promise unto death. And though the night grows colder, And though the shadows track— The fire in the winter pack Will never turn his back.

THE WIND THAT WOULDN’T SLEEP

Verse 1

There’s a whisper in the treeline When the dusk begins to fall— A restless kind of murmuring That stirs the hearts of all. But she alone can hear it clear, A voice beneath the deep— A wind that wanders day and night Because it cannot sleep.

Chorus

Oh the wind that wouldn’t slumber, Oh the wind that wouldn’t rest— It circles through the forest Like a warning unexpressed. And though she walks in quiet grace, With calm in every breath— She feels the stirring underfoot Of something not at rest.

Verse 2

She listens to the trembling leaves, The shifting of the loam. She knows the forest’s every sigh, Its heartbeat and its home. But lately there’s a tension there, A pulse beneath the stone— As if the roots remember Something ancient and unknown.

Chorus

Oh the wind that wouldn’t slumber, Oh the wind that wouldn’t rest— It circles through the forest Like a warning unexpressed. And though she walks in quiet grace, With calm in every breath— She feels the stirring underfoot Of something not at rest.

Bridge

Some say she dreams in colors, Some say she dreams in sound— But she just keeps on listening To the murmurs underground.

Final Chorus

Oh the wind that wouldn’t slumber, Oh the wind that wouldn’t rest— It circles through the forest Like a warning unexpressed. And though she walks in quiet grace, With calm in every breath— She feels the stirring underfoot Of something not at rest.

TOMORROW’S TUNE

Verse 1

He strums a lively melody In taverns warm and bright— A gnome with jokes and jests to spare, A spark in every night. But sometimes in his singing, A strange refrain appears— A line that feels like memory From days not yet near.

Chorus

Oh tomorrow’s tune is playing In the corner of his mind— A song that runs ahead of him, A step beyond the time. And though he laughs and shrugs it off, And though he plays it soon— There’s something oddly familiar In the notes of tomorrow’s tune.

Verse 2

He claims it’s just coincidence, A trick of bardic flair— But some who hear his verses Feel a shiver in the air. For every now and then he hums A chorus soft and low— That hints at things unspoken, At paths he shouldn’t know.

Chorus

Oh tomorrow’s tune is playing In the corner of his mind— A song that runs ahead of him, A step beyond the time. And though he laughs and shrugs it off, And though he plays it soon— There’s something oddly familiar In the notes of tomorrow’s tune.

Bridge

Some songs are born of stories, Some songs are born of fate— But his seem born of moments That haven’t happened yet.

Final Chorus

Oh tomorrow’s tune is playing In the corner of his mind— A song that runs ahead of him, A step beyond the time. And though he laughs and shrugs it off, And though he plays it soon— There’s something oddly familiar In the notes of tomorrow’s tune.

THE APPRENTICE AND THE BROKEN STAR

Verse 1

She studies by the lantern’s glow, Her quill a restless spark— A mind too bright for quiet nights, Too curious for the dark. She speaks of falling starlight, Of patterns in the sky— And though her hands may tremble, There’s fire in her eye.

Chorus

Oh the apprentice and the broken star, Oh the questions without end— She chases truths that flicker Just beyond the river’s bend. And though the world grows stranger, And though the signs are far— She keeps her gaze unshaken On the path of the broken star.

Verse 2

She laughs at her own missteps, She blushes at her fears— But still she reads the shifting winds That others never hear. Some say she’s just a dreamer, Some say she’s in too deep— But she alone sees constellations Where others only sleep.

Chorus

Oh the apprentice and the broken star, Oh the questions without end— She chases truths that flicker Just beyond the river’s bend. And though the world grows stranger, And though the signs are far— She keeps her gaze unshaken On the path of the broken star.

Bridge

Some lights fall for a reason, Some lights fall without aim— But she will follow every spark Until she learns its name.

Final Chorus

Oh the apprentice and the broken star, Oh the questions without end— She chases truths that flicker Just beyond the river’s bend. And though the world grows stranger, And though the signs are far— She keeps her gaze unshaken On the path of the broken star.

THE CANDLE THAT WON’T GO OUT

Verse 1

He keeps a single candle Burning through the night— A beacon for the weary, A soft and steady light. He tends it with devotion, He guards it with a prayer— And though his smile is gentle, There’s sorrow settled there.

Chorus

Oh the candle that won’t go out, Though winter howls and cries— A flame that stands against the dark, A hope that never dies. And though his heart is heavy, And though he walks in doubt— He keeps his vigil faithfully With the candle that won’t go out.

Verse 2

He listens to confession, He comforts those in pain— But when the chapel empties, His tears fall like the rain. For some wounds have no healing, Some losses have no name— Yet still he lights the lantern And tends the fragile flame.

Chorus

Oh the candle that won’t go out, Though winter howls and cries— A flame that stands against the dark, A hope that never dies. And though his heart is heavy, And though he walks in doubt— He keeps his vigil faithfully With the candle that won’t go out.

Bridge

Some prayers are made in silence, Some griefs are held alone— But still he lights the candle For the ones who won’t come home.

Final Chorus

Oh the candle that won’t go out, Though winter howls and cries— A flame that stands against the dark, A hope that never dies. And though his heart is heavy, And though he walks in doubt— He keeps his vigil faithfully With the candle that won’t go out.

THE MASTER WHO WALKED INTO WINTER

Verse 1

They say he trained in silence, Where the frost meets morning’s breath— A student of the stillness, Of the space between each step. But when they speak of winter, A shadow fills his eyes— For one who walked before him Never made the return rise.

Chorus

Oh the master lost to winter, Oh the path that fades to white— Some journeys end in daylight, Some vanish into night. And though he walks with balance, And though his heart is clear— The master lost to winter Still whispers in his ear.

Verse 2

He listens to the snowfall As if it holds a clue— A secret in the quiet Only patient hearts pursue. He never speaks the full tale, He never names the cost— But every time the cold wind stirs, He mourns what he has lost.

Chorus

Oh the master lost to winter, Oh the path that fades to white— Some journeys end in daylight, Some vanish into night. And though he walks with balance, And though his heart is clear— The master lost to winter Still whispers in his ear.

Bridge

Final Chorus

Oh the master lost to winter, Oh the path that fades to white— Some journeys end in daylight, Some vanish into night. And though he walks with balance, And though his heart is clear— The master lost to winter Still whispers in his ear.

THE QUIET ROAD OF GUZ

Verse 1

He walks with heavy footsteps, But his heart is gentle‑made— A man who’s learned the weight of wrongs, And how the past won’t fade. He keeps his words in careful hands, His temper held in check— But sometimes in the silent hours, Old whispers brush his neck.

Chorus

Oh the quiet road he follows, Oh the burdens that he bears— A path of slow redemption Through winters no one shares. And though he stands with courage, And though he strives to choose— The quiet road grows longer For a man once known as Guz.

Verse 2

He flinches at the flicker Of magic in the air— Not fear of spell or sorcery, But memories laid bare. He tries to drown the echoes, He tries to walk them down— But shadows cling to those who’ve worn A darker, older crown.

Chorus

Oh the quiet road he follows, Oh the burdens that he bears— A path of slow redemption Through winters no one shares. And though he stands with courage, And though he strives to choose— The quiet road grows longer For a man once known as Guz.

Bridge

Some voices fade with distance, Some linger in the bone— But he keeps walking forward, Determined and alone.

Final Chorus

Oh the quiet road he follows, Oh the burdens that he bears— A path of slow redemption Through winters no one shares. And though he stands with courage, And though he strives to choose— The quiet road grows longer For a man once known as Guz.

ASH ON THE SHRINE

Verse 1

They found her in the ruins Where the sacred candles lay— Their wax still warm with memory, Their light long swept away. She knelt among the ashes, Her armor scorched and torn— And though she spoke no vow aloud, A fiercer oath was born.

Chorus

Oh the ash upon the shrine Still clings to her like fate. A promise forged in silence, A fire that will not wait. And though her voice is gentle, And though her steps align— There burns a quiet fury In the ash upon the shrine.

Verse 2

She walks with holy purpose, Her gaze both calm and clear— But something in her shadow Still trembles with the fear. Not fear of death or darkness, Not fear of tooth or scale— But fear of failing those she served, Of letting justice fail.

Chorus

Oh the ash upon the shrine Still clings to her like fate. A promise forged in silence, A fire that will not wait. And though her voice is gentle, And though her steps align— There burns a quiet fury In the ash upon the shrine.

Bridge

Some wounds are made of fire, Some vows are made of stone— But hers was made of both at once, And she bears it all alone.

Final Chorus

Oh the ash upon the shrine Still clings to her like fate. A promise forged in silence, A fire that will not wait. And though her voice is gentle, And though her steps align— There burns a quiet fury In the ash upon the shrine.

THE FIRE THAT TREMBLES

Verse 1

They say his flame burns steady, A torch against the cold— A dragonborn of noble line, With fire in his soul. But sometimes when the night grows still, And winter grips the air— His breath comes sharp and ragged, As if something stirs elsewhere.

Chorus

Oh the fire that trembles, Oh the flame that knows its kin— A spark that flares in warning Of the storm that waits within. And though he stands unshaken, And though his pride is true— The fire that trembles in his chest Knows more than he can view.

Verse 2

He speaks of ancient stories, Of wings that split the sky— Of battles carved in memory Long before his time. But when the distant thunder rolls, Or shadows coil and climb— He stiffens, as if hearing A call from some old rhyme.

Chorus

Oh the fire that trembles, Oh the flame that knows its kin— A spark that flares in warning Of the storm that waits within. And though he stands unshaken, And though his pride is true— The fire that trembles in his chest Knows more than he can view.

Bridge

Some blood remembers battles, Some blood remembers flame— And his remembers something That will not speak its name.

Final Chorus

Oh the fire that trembles, Oh the flame that knows its kin— A spark that flares in warning Of the storm that waits within. And though he stands unshaken, And though his pride is true— The fire that trembles in his chest Knows more than he can view.

THE PATRON’S WHISPER

Verse 1

He walks with silver laughter, A shadow at his heel— A tiefling with a wandering smile And secrets kept concealed. He charms the crowded taverns, He dazzles every hall— But sometimes when the candles dim, He listens for a call.

Chorus

Oh the patron’s whisper, Soft as falling snow— A voice that curls around him From places none can know. And though he plays the jester, And though his grin is wide— The patron’s whisper lingers Like a shadow at his side.

Verse 2

He speaks in clever riddles, He dances through the night— But when the moon grows heavy, His eyes lose all their light. For something in the quiet Reminds him who he serves— A presence cold and patient, A pull he can’t unnerve.

Oh the patron’s whisper, Soft as falling snow— A voice that curls around him From places none can know. And though he plays the jester, And though his grin is wide— The patron’s whisper lingers Like a shadow at his side.

Some bargains leave a mark, Some promises a chain— But he still walks in elegance Through snowfall and through rain.

Final Chorus
